باب الأذان
لما ذكر الأوقات وهي أسباب وفي الحقيقة إعلام للوجوب، لأن الوجوب في الحقيقـة مـضـاف إلى إيجاب الله تعالى، وهو غيب عنا. وقد جعل الله سبحانه وتعالى برأفته الكاملة، ورحمته الشاملة، الأسباب الظاهرة إعلاماً على إيجابه الغيبي ذكر الأذان الذي هو إعلام لتلك الإعلام، فتناسـبـا مـن حيث الإعلام، وقدم الأوقات على ذكر الأذان، لما فيها من معنى السببية في حق العباد، والسبب مقـــدم على العلامة لقربه، ولأن الأوقات إعلام في حق الخواص، وهم العلماء والأذان في حق العوام، فقدم ما اختص بالخواص لزيادة مرتبتهم. وقال شيخ الإسلام بدر الدين حقيق بالمسلم أن يتنبه بالوقت، فإن لم يُنبهه الوقت، فلينبهه الأذان، ثم الكلام هنا في ثبوته، وتسميته، وأفضليته، وتفسيره لغة وشريعة، وسبب مشروعيته، وسببه، وشرطه وحكمه، وركنه وصفته وكيفيته، ومحل شرع فيه، ووقته، وما يطلب من سامعه، وما أعد الله من الثواب لفاعله. أما ثبوته فبالكتاب وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا نَادَيْتُمْ إِلَى الصَّلوة لـلمائدة : ٥٨﴾. والنداء إليها ليس إلا الأذان، وبالسنة. وأما تسميته: فاختير لفظ الأذان، لأنـه مـن بــاب التفعيل كالسلام. وكررت فيه الأذكار من الشهادتين والتكبير. وفي «البدرية»: إنما سمي أذاناً، ولم يسم شهادة، وإن كانت موجودة فيه؛ لأن المقصود من شرعيته الإعلام وفائدة التكبير والشهادتين فيه ليعلم المؤذن الناس أنه لا يخالفهم فيما يدعوهم إليه، ويعلمون أنه أمين في هذا، فيقبلون قوله. ولهذا أشار النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بقوله: «الإِمَامُ ضَامِنٌ، وَالْمُؤَذِّنُ أمِينٌ». وأما أفضليته: فعندنا الإمامة أفضل من الأذان، لمواظبة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عليها. وكذا الخلفاء الراشدون من بعده، وقول عمر: «لولا الخليفا لأذنت»، لا يستلزم تفضيله عليها، بل مراده لأذنت مع الإمامة، لا مع تركها، فيفيـد أن الأفضل كون الإمام هو المؤذن، وهذا مذهبنا، وعليه كان أبو حنيفة رحمه الله، كما في «فتح القدير». ومعناه لغة: الإعلام. قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَأَذَانُ مِنَ اللهِ ﴾ [التوبة: ٣] وشريعة: إعــلام مخصوص بألفاظ في أوقات مخصوصة. وسبب مشروعيته على المشهور: أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام، لمـا قـدم الصلاة تارة، ويعجلها أخرى، وبعض الصحابة كان يبادر حرصاً على الصلاة مع النبي، ويفوته بعض مقاصده، وبعضهم يشغله ذلك عن المبادرة لظن التأخير، فشاور الصحابة بأن ينصبوا علامة يعرفون بها وقت صلاة النبي، كيلا تفوتهم الجماعة، فقال بعضهم: تنصب راية، إذا رآها الناس، أذن بعضهم بعضاً، فلم يعجبه ذلك، وأشار بعضهم بضرب الناقوس، فكـرهـه لأجـل النصارى، وبعضهم بالنفخ في الشبور، فكرهه لأجل اليهود، وبعضهم بإيقاد النار، فكرهـه لأجـل المجوس، فتفرقوا قبل أن يجتمعوا على شيء، قال عبد الله بن زيد الأنصاري صاحب الأذان، لا صاحب الوضوء: فبت لا يأخذني النوم وكنت بين النائم واليقظان، إذ رأيت شخصاً نـزل مـن السماء، وعليه ثوبان أخضران، وبيده شبه الناقوس، فقلت: أتبيع هذا الناقوس؟ فقال: ما تصنــع بـه؟ فقلت: أذهب به إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ليضرب به وقت صلاتنا، فقال: ألا أدلك علـى مـا هـو خـيـر مـن هـذا؟ فقلت: نعم، فقام على جدم حائط، أي أصله، مستقبل القبلة، فأذن ثم مكث هنيهة، ثـم قـال مثل ذلك، وزاد في آخره، قد قامت الصلاة مرتين. فأتيت النبي، فأخبرته بذلك، فقال: «رُؤيَا صِدْقٍ أو حق»، ألقها على بلال، فإنه أندى صوتاً منك، ومره ينادي به. فألقيتها، فقــام عـلـى بـيـت أرملـة كـان أعلى سطوح بالمدينة، وجعل يؤذن، فلما سمع عمره، خرج في إزار يهرول، ويقول: طاف بي الليلة ما طاف بعبد الله إلا أنه سبقني، فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الحمد لله وإنه لأثبت». واختلف في ذلك الملك، فقيل: جبريل، وقيل غيره. وروي أن سبعة من الصحابة رأوا تلك الرؤيا في ليلة واحدة. كذا في «المبسوطين»، ومحمد بن الحنيفة. وقيل: زين العابدين ينكر هذا، ويقول: يعمدون إلى مـا هـو من معالم الدين، فيقولون: ثبت بالرؤيا، وإنما طريقه الوحي قلنا: ثبت الأذان بأمره عليه الصلاة والسلام، لا بالمنام وحده. وقيل: نزل به جبريل عليه الصلاة والسلام على النبي، حين قال «كثير بن مرة»: أذن جبريل في السماء فسمعه عمر، ولا منافاة بين هذه الأسباب، فليجعل كل ذلك كان سبباً، كذا في «معراج الدراية»، وفي «سنن أبي داود» حكى ألفاظ الأذان وهي معلومة. وفي حديث «المعراج»: إن الملك الذي خرج من الحجاب الذي يلي عرش الرحمن، أذن. وهو يدل على أن التعليم كان ليلة الإسراء، إلا أنه لم يعمل به إلا بعدما رآه عبد الله، وشرع في السنة: الأولى من الهجرة.
Chapter of the Adhan. Since he mentioned the times and they are causes and in reality notification of obligation, because obligation in reality is attributed to Allah's command, and it is hidden from us. And Allah, with His perfect kindness and comprehensive mercy, made the apparent causes a notification of His hidden command. He mentioned the adhan which is a notification of those notifications, so they correspond in terms of notification. And he gave precedence to the times over mentioning the adhan, because they have the meaning of causality with respect to servants, and the cause is given precedence over the sign due to its closeness, and because the times are a notification for the elite, i.e., the scholars, and the adhan for the common people, so he gave precedence to what is specific to the elite due to the increase of their rank. And Shaykh al-Islam Badr al-Din said: It behooves a Muslim to be alerted by the time; if the time does not alert him, then let the adhan alert him. Then the discussion here is about its establishment, its naming, its superiority, its linguistic and shar'i interpretation, the reason for its legislation, its cause, its condition, its ruling, its pillar, its description and manner, the place it is prescribed, its time, what is required from the hearer, and what Allah has prepared of reward for its performer. As for its establishment: by the Book, which is His saying: {And when you call to prayer} (al-Ma'idah: 58). And the call to it is nothing but the adhan, and by the Sunnah. As for its naming: the word 'adhan' was chosen, because it is from the pattern of taf'il like 'salam'. And the remembrances from the two shahadas and takbir are repeated in it. In al-Badriyya: It was called 'adhan' and not 'shahada', although it contains it, because the purpose of its legislation is notification, and the benefit of the takbir and two shahadas in it is so that the mu'adhdhin informs the people that he does not contradict them in what he calls them to, and they know that he is trustworthy in this, so they accept his statement. And for this the Prophet (peace be upon him) indicated by his saying: 'The imam is a guarantor, and the mu'adhdhin is trustworthy.' As for its superiority: According to us, imamah is superior to adhan, due to the Prophet's constancy upon it. Likewise the Rightly-Guided Caliphs after him. And the saying of 'Umar: 'Were it not for the caliphate, I would give the adhan' does not necessitate preferring it over it; rather his intent is 'I would give the adhan along with the imamah, not with its abandonment', so it indicates that the best is that the imam be the mu'adhdhin, and this is our madhhab, and upon it was Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, as in Fath al-Qadir. Its linguistic meaning: notification. Allah said: {And an announcement from Allah} (al-Tawbah: 3). And its shar'i meaning: a specific notification with specific words at specific times. The reason for its legislation according to the well-known: that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would sometimes advance the prayer and sometimes delay it, and some companions would hasten out of eagerness to pray with the Prophet, and would miss some of his purposes, and some were preoccupied by that from hastening due to thinking it delayed. So he consulted the companions about setting up a sign by which they would know the time of the Prophet's prayer, lest they miss the congregation. Some said: Set up a flag; when people see it, they would alert each other. He did not like that. Some suggested striking a naqus (bell), but he disliked it because of the Christians. Some suggested blowing into a shubur (horn), but he disliked it because of the Jews. Some suggested lighting a fire, but he disliked it because of the Magians. So they dispersed before agreeing on anything. 'Abdullah ibn Zayd al-Ansari, the one of the adhan (not the one of wudu') said: 'I spent the night, sleep not overtaking me, and I was between sleeping and waking, when I saw a person descending from the sky, wearing two green garments, and in his hand was something like a naqus. I said: Will you sell this naqus? He said: What will you do with it? I said: I will go to the Prophet (peace be upon him) to strike it at the time of our prayer. He said: Shall I guide you to something better than this? I said: Yes. So he stood on the base of a wall, i.e., its foundation, facing the qibla, and gave the adhan. Then he paused for a while, then said the like of that, and added at the end: 'The prayer has begun' twice. So I came to the Prophet and informed him of that. He said: 'A true vision or a true one' (according to a version: 'a truth'). 'Dictate it to Bilal, for he has a louder voice than you, and order him to call it.' So I dictated it, and he stood on the house of a widow which was the highest roof in Madinah, and began to give the adhan. When 'Umar heard him, he came out in his lower garment hurrying, saying: 'The same thing visited me tonight as visited 'Abdullah, except that he preceded me.' The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Praise be to Allah, and he is more established.' There is difference about that angel: it was said Jibril, and others said. And it is narrated that seven of the companions saw that vision in one night. So in al-Mabsutayn, and Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyya. And it is said: Zayn al-'Abidin denies this, saying: They take from the symbols of the religion and say: Established by a vision, but its way is only revelation. We say: The adhan was established by the command of the Prophet, not by the dream alone. And it is said: Jibril descended with it upon the Prophet, when Kathir ibn Murra said: 'Jibril gave the adhan in the heaven and 'Umar heard it.' There is no contradiction between these causes; so let all that be considered a cause. So in Mi'raj al-Diraya. And in Sunan Abi Dawud, the wording of the adhan is narrated, and it is known. And in the hadith of al-Mi'raj: 'The angel who emerged from the veil that is near the Throne of the Merciful gave the adhan.' And this indicates that the instruction was on the Night of Isra', except that it was not acted upon until after 'Abdullah saw it, and it was prescribed in the first year of the Hijra.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on adhan in the sharh of Nur al-Idah. The commentator first explains why the author mentioned the times before adhan: times are causes for obligation and are for the elite (scholars), while adhan is for the common folk, so the cause is mentioned first. He then outlines the topics to be covered: establishment, naming, superiority, definition, reason for legislation, conditions, rulings, pillars, description, place, time, what is required of the hearer, and reward. The establishment is proven by the Quranic verse 'And when you call to prayer' (5:58) and by the Sunnah. The naming as 'adhan' is because it is a notification (i'lam), and the taf'il pattern indicates repetition. The superiority of imamah over adhan is the Hanafi position, supported by the Prophet's practice and that of the caliphs; 'Umar's statement about preferring adhan is interpreted as wishing to combine both roles. The linguistic meaning is 'notification' (i'lam), and the shar'i meaning is a specific notification with specific words at specific times. The well-known story of the dream of 'Abdullah ibn Zayd is recounted as the reason for legislation: the Prophet consulted the companions about a sign for prayer times, various suggestions were rejected, and then 'Abdullah saw an angel teaching the adhan in a dream. The Prophet confirmed it and ordered Bilal to call it. The passage also notes a difference of opinion about whether the adhan was established by dream alone or by revelation; the Hanafi position is that it was established by the Prophet's command, not the dream alone, and that various reports (e.g., Jibril's call in heaven, the hadith of Mi'raj) are not contradictory but all contributed to the prescription. The adhan was prescribed in the first year of the Hijra.

Key Terms
الأذان (al-adhan): The call to prayer, named for its repetitive notification.
الإمامة (al-imamah): Leading the congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which is superior: adhan or imamah?
A) Adhan
B) Imamah
C) Both are equal
D) It is not specified

Key Takeaway
The call to prayer is named 'adhan' for its repetitive notification, and in the Hanafi school, imamah (leading prayer) is superior to adhan.

Reason for Legislation: The Dream and Establishment
Narrative of legislation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recount the story of the dream of Abdullah ibn Zayd and explain the Hanafi position that the adhan was established by the Prophet's command, not solely by the dream.

Core Idea
The adhan was established by revelation, not merely a dream; the dream was a means of conveying it.

This lesson narrates the well-known story of the legislation of adhan. The companions needed a way to announce prayer times, and various suggestions were rejected. Then Abdullah ibn Zayd saw a dream in which an angel taught him the adhan. The Prophet confirmed it and ordered Bilal to call it. The passage also addresses a theological point: the adhan was established by the Prophet's command, not solely by the dream, and other reports (Jibril's adhan in heaven, the Mi'raj hadith) are not contradictory.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem
The companions needed a sign to know the Prophet's prayer time due to variations. They suggested flag, bell, horn, fire, but all were rejected due to resemblance to other religions.
This shows the desire for a unique Islamic symbol.
2
Recount the dream of Abdullah ibn Zayd
He saw an angel in a dream teaching the adhan and iqamah. The angel stood on a wall and gave the adhan with the familiar words.
Abdullah is distinguished as 'sahib al-adhan' (the one of the adhan) to differentiate from another companion.
3
Note the Prophet's confirmation
The Prophet said it was a true vision and ordered Bilal to use these words. When 'Umar heard, he confirmed he had the same dream.
The Prophet's statement 'ru'ya sidq' indicates the dream was inspired.
4
Address the theological nuance
The passage counters the objection that adhan cannot be based on a dream by stating it was established by the Prophet's command (amr), with the dream as a means. It also mentions other reports (Jibril's call, Mi'raj) as complementary.
This preserves the principle that matters of worship (ibadat) require clear revelation.

أنه أمين في هذا، فيقبلون قوله. ولهذا أشار النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بقوله: «الإِمَامُ ضَامِنٌ، وَالْمُؤَذِّنُ أمِينٌ». وأما أفضليته: فعندنا الإمامة أفضل من الأذان، لمواظبة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عليها. وكذا الخلفاء الراشدون من بعده، وقول عمر: «لولا الخليفا لأذنت»، لا يستلزم تفضيله عليها، بل مراده لأذنت مع الإمامة، لا مع تركها، فيفيـد أن الأفضل كون الإمام هو المؤذن، وهذا مذهبنا، وعليه كان أبو حنيفة رحمه الله، كما في «فتح القدير». ومعناه لغة: الإعلام. قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَأَذَانُ مِنَ اللهِ ﴾ [التوبة: ٣] وشريعة: إعــلام مخصوص بألفاظ في أوقات مخصوصة. وسبب مشروعيته على المشهور: أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام، لمـا قـدم الصلاة تارة، ويعجلها أخرى، وبعض الصحابة كان يبادر حرصاً على الصلاة مع النبي، ويفوته بعض مقاصده، وبعضهم يشغله ذلك عن المبادرة لظن التأخير، فشاور الصحابة بأن ينصبوا علامة يعرفون بها وقت صلاة النبي، كيلا تفوتهم الجماعة، فقال بعضهم: تنصب راية، إذا رآها الناس، أذن بعضهم بعضاً، فلم يعجبه ذلك، وأشار بعضهم بضرب الناقوس، فكـرهـه لأجـل النصارى، وبعضهم بالنفخ في الشبور، فكرهه لأجل اليهود، وبعضهم بإيقاد النار، فكرهـه لأجـل المجوس، فتفرقوا قبل أن يجتمعوا على شيء، قال عبد الله بن زيد الأنصاري صاحب الأذان، لا صاحب الوضوء: فبت لا يأخذني النوم وكنت بين النائم واليقظان، إذ رأيت شخصاً نـزل مـن السماء، وعليه ثوبان أخضران، وبيده شبه الناقوس، فقلت: أتبيع هذا الناقوس؟ فقال: ما تصنــع بـه؟ فقلت: أذهب به إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ليضرب به وقت صلاتنا، فقال: ألا أدلك علـى مـا هـو خـيـر مـن هـذا؟ فقلت: نعم، فقام على جدم حائط، أي أصله، مستقبل القبلة، فأذن ثم مكث هنيهة، ثـم قـال مثل ذلك، وزاد في آخره، قد قامت الصلاة مرتين. فأتيت النبي، فأخبرته بذلك، فقال: «رُؤيَا صِدْقٍ أو حق»، ألقها على بلال، فإنه أندى صوتاً منك، ومره ينادي به. فألقيتها، فقــام عـلـى بـيـت أرملـة كـان أعلى سطوح بالمدينة، وجعل يؤذن، فلما سمع عمره، خرج في إزار يهرول، ويقول: طاف بي الليلة ما طاف بعبد الله إلا أنه سبقني، فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الحمد لله وإنه لأثبت». واختلف في ذلك الملك، فقيل: جبريل، وقيل غيره. وروي أن سبعة من الصحابة رأوا تلك الرؤيا في ليلة واحدة. كذا في «المبسوطين»، ومحمد بن الحنيفة. وقيل: زين العابدين ينكر هذا، ويقول: يعمدون إلى مـا هـو من معالم الدين، فيقولون: ثبت بالرؤيا، وإنما طريقه الوحي قلنا: ثبت الأذان بأمره عليه الصلاة والسلام، لا بالمنام وحده. وقيل: نزل به جبريل عليه الصلاة والسلام على النبي، حين قال «كثير بن مرة»: أذن جبريل في السماء فسمعه عمر، ولا منافاة بين هذه الأسباب، فليجعل كل ذلك كان سبباً، كذا في «معراج الدراية»، وفي «سنن أبي داود» حكى ألفاظ الأذان وهي معلومة. وفي حديث «المعراج»: إن الملك الذي خرج من الحجاب الذي يلي عرش الرحمن، أذن. وهو يدل على أن التعليم كان ليلة الإسراء، إلا أنه لم يعمل به إلا بعدما رآه عبد الله، وشرع في السنة: الأولى من الهجرة.
Chapter of the Adhan. Since he mentioned the times and they are causes and in reality notification of obligation, because obligation in reality is attributed to Allah's command, and it is hidden from us. And Allah, with His perfect kindness and comprehensive mercy, made the apparent causes a notification of His hidden command. He mentioned the adhan which is a notification of those notifications, so they correspond in terms of notification. And he gave precedence to the times over mentioning the adhan, because they have the meaning of causality with respect to servants, and the cause is given precedence over the sign due to its closeness, and because the times are a notification for the elite, i.e., the scholars, and the adhan for the common people, so he gave precedence to what is specific to the elite due to the increase of their rank. And Shaykh al-Islam Badr al-Din said: It behooves a Muslim to be alerted by the time; if the time does not alert him, then let the adhan alert him. Then the discussion here is about its establishment, its naming, its superiority, its linguistic and shar'i interpretation, the reason for its legislation, its cause, its condition, its ruling, its pillar, its description and manner, the place it is prescribed, its time, what is required from the hearer, and what Allah has prepared of reward for its performer. As for its establishment: by the Book, which is His saying: {And when you call to prayer} (al-Ma'idah: 58). And the call to it is nothing but the adhan, and by the Sunnah. As for its naming: the word 'adhan' was chosen, because it is from the pattern of taf'il like 'salam'. And the remembrances from the two shahadas and takbir are repeated in it. In al-Badriyya: It was called 'adhan' and not 'shahada', although it contains it, because the purpose of its legislation is notification, and the benefit of the takbir and two shahadas in it is so that the mu'adhdhin informs the people that he does not contradict them in what he calls them to, and they know that he is trustworthy in this, so they accept his statement. And for this the Prophet (peace be upon him) indicated by his saying: 'The imam is a guarantor, and the mu'adhdhin is trustworthy.' As for its superiority: According to us, imamah is superior to adhan, due to the Prophet's constancy upon it. Likewise the Rightly-Guided Caliphs after him. And the saying of 'Umar: 'Were it not for the caliphate, I would give the adhan' does not necessitate preferring it over it; rather his intent is 'I would give the adhan along with the imamah, not with its abandonment', so it indicates that the best is that the imam be the mu'adhdhin, and this is our madhhab, and upon it was Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, as in Fath al-Qadir. Its linguistic meaning: notification. Allah said: {And an announcement from Allah} (al-Tawbah: 3). And its shar'i meaning: a specific notification with specific words at specific times. The reason for its legislation according to the well-known: that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would sometimes advance the prayer and sometimes delay it, and some companions would hasten out of eagerness to pray with the Prophet, and would miss some of his purposes, and some were preoccupied by that from hastening due to thinking it delayed. So he consulted the companions about setting up a sign by which they would know the time of the Prophet's prayer, lest they miss the congregation. Some said: Set up a flag; when people see it, they would alert each other. He did not like that. Some suggested striking a naqus (bell), but he disliked it because of the Christians. Some suggested blowing into a shubur (horn), but he disliked it because of the Jews. Some suggested lighting a fire, but he disliked it because of the Magians. So they dispersed before agreeing on anything. 'Abdullah ibn Zayd al-Ansari, the one of the adhan (not the one of wudu') said: 'I spent the night, sleep not overtaking me, and I was between sleeping and waking, when I saw a person descending from the sky, wearing two green garments, and in his hand was something like a naqus. I said: Will you sell this naqus? He said: What will you do with it? I said: I will go to the Prophet (peace be upon him) to strike it at the time of our prayer. He said: Shall I guide you to something better than this? I said: Yes. So he stood on the base of a wall, i.e., its foundation, facing the qibla, and gave the adhan. Then he paused for a while, then said the like of that, and added at the end: 'The prayer has begun' twice. So I came to the Prophet and informed him of that. He said: 'A true vision or a true one' (according to a version: 'a truth'). 'Dictate it to Bilal, for he has a louder voice than you, and order him to call it.' So I dictated it, and he stood on the house of a widow which was the highest roof in Madinah, and began to give the adhan. When 'Umar heard him, he came out in his lower garment hurrying, saying: 'The same thing visited me tonight as visited 'Abdullah, except that he preceded me.' The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Praise be to Allah, and he is more established.' There is difference about that angel: it was said Jibril, and others said. And it is narrated that seven of the companions saw that vision in one night. So in al-Mabsutayn, and Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyya. And it is said: Zayn al-'Abidin denies this, saying: They take from the symbols of the religion and say: Established by a vision, but its way is only revelation. We say: The adhan was established by the command of the Prophet, not by the dream alone. And it is said: Jibril descended with it upon the Prophet, when Kathir ibn Murra said: 'Jibril gave the adhan in the heaven and 'Umar heard it.' There is no contradiction between these causes; so let all that be considered a cause. So in Mi'raj al-Diraya. And in Sunan Abi Dawud, the wording of the adhan is narrated, and it is known. And in the hadith of al-Mi'raj: 'The angel who emerged from the veil that is near the Throne of the Merciful gave the adhan.' And this indicates that the instruction was on the Night of Isra', except that it was not acted upon until after 'Abdullah saw it, and it was prescribed in the first year of the Hijra.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on adhan in the sharh of Nur al-Idah. The commentator first explains why the author mentioned the times before adhan: times are causes for obligation and are for the elite (scholars), while adhan is for the common folk, so the cause is mentioned first. He then outlines the topics to be covered: establishment, naming, superiority, definition, reason for legislation, conditions, rulings, pillars, description, place, time, what is required of the hearer, and reward. The establishment is proven by the Quranic verse 'And when you call to prayer' (5:58) and by the Sunnah. The naming as 'adhan' is because it is a notification (i'lam), and the taf'il pattern indicates repetition. The superiority of imamah over adhan is the Hanafi position, supported by the Prophet's practice and that of the caliphs; 'Umar's statement about preferring adhan is interpreted as wishing to combine both roles. The linguistic meaning is 'notification' (i'lam), and the shar'i meaning is a specific notification with specific words at specific times. The well-known story of the dream of 'Abdullah ibn Zayd is recounted as the reason for legislation: the Prophet consulted the companions about a sign for prayer times, various suggestions were rejected, and then 'Abdullah saw an angel teaching the adhan in a dream. The Prophet confirmed it and ordered Bilal to call it. The passage also notes a difference of opinion about whether the adhan was established by dream alone or by revelation; the Hanafi position is that it was established by the Prophet's command, not the dream alone, and that various reports (e.g., Jibril's call in heaven, the hadith of Mi'raj) are not contradictory but all contributed to the prescription. The adhan was prescribed in the first year of the Hijra.

Key Terms
الرؤيا (al-ru'ya): A true dream that can be a means of inspiration but not a standalone source of legislation.
الناقوس (al-naqus): A wooden instrument used by Christians to call to prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the Prophet's response when Abdullah ibn Zayd told him about his dream?
A) He said it was from Shaytan
B) He said it was a true vision and ordered Bilal to call it
C) He said to ignore it
D) He said to use a bell instead

Key Takeaway
The adhan was established by the Prophet's command, with the dream of Abdullah ibn Zayd serving as a means, not the source of legislation.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Ruling of Adhan and Iqama as Sunnah Mu'akkadah
Establishes the ruling of adhan and iqama through narrations and legal analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqama as sunnah mu'akkadah, identify the primary evidence from the hadith of the Bedouin, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding their obligation.

Core Idea
Adhan and iqama are sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib—the Prophet's omission in the Bedouin hadith is decisive.

The adhan and iqama are among the most visible symbols of Islam, yet their legal status in the Hanafi school is precisely defined. This lesson examines the authoritative ruling that they are sunnah mu'akkadah—emphasized but not obligatory—and the evidence that supports this position. We also explore a nuanced disagreement within the Hanafi school itself, where some early mashā'ikh argued for wujub, and understand how the later tradition resolved it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The adhan and iqama. According to the matn of Nūr al-Īḍāḥ, what is their legal classification? The author states they are sunnah mu'akkadah.
The ruling is not wājib; the author explicitly says 'ليس بواجب، هو الأصح'.
2
Locate the primary dalil
What proof does the author cite for the sunnah ruling? The hadith of the Bedouin: when the Prophet taught him to pray, he did not mention the adhan or iqama.
The hadith is narrated in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith prove non-obligation? If the adhan were obligatory, the Prophet would have included it in his teaching. His omission indicates it is not an integral (fard/wājib) part of the prayer rite.
The legal inference is from omission (sukūt) in a context of instruction (ta'līm).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi mashā'ikh argued that adhan is wājib, citing the Prophet's command 'let one of you give the adhan' and Imam Muhammad's statement that he would fight a town abandoning it. Identify the basis of their argument.
The command (amr) in usul indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is evidence otherwise.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
How does the commentator resolve the ikhtilaf? He declares the sunnah position as aṣaḥḥ (most correct) and explains that the severe statements of Imam Muhammad refer to abandonment that amounts to contempt of religion (istikhfāf bi al-dīn), not intrinsic obligation.
The mufta bihi in the school is sunnah mu'akkadah.

النبي ﷺ، و فيفوته بعض مقاصده، وبعضهم يشغله ذلك عن المبادرة لظن التأخير، فشاور الصحابة بأن ينصبوا علامة يعرفون بها وقت صلاة النبي ﷺ، كيلا تفوتهم الجماعة، فقال بعضهم: تنصب راية، إذا رآها الناس، أذن بعضهم بعضاً، فلم يعجبه ذلك، وأشار بعضهم بضرب الناقوس، فكرهه لأجل النصارى، وبعضهم بالنفخ في الشبور، فكرهه لأجل اليهود، وبعضهم بإيقاد النار، فكرهه لأجل المجوس، فتفرقوا قبل أن يجتمعوا على شيء، قال عبد الله بن زيد الأنصاري صاحب الأذان، لا صاحب الوضوء: [فبت] لا يأخذني النوم وكنت بين النائم واليقظان، إذ رأيت شخصاً نزل من السماء، وعليه ثوبان أخضران، وبيده شبه الناقوس، فقلت: أتبيع هذا الناقوس؟ فقال: ما تصنع به؟ فقلت: أذهب به إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ليضرب به وقت صلاتنا، فقال: ألا أدلك على ما هو خير من هذا؟ فقلت: نعم، فقام على جدم حائط، أي أصله، مستقبل القبلة، فأذن ثم مكث هنيهة، ثم قال مثل ذلك، وزاد في آخره، قد قامت الصلاة مرتين. فأتيت النبي ﷺ، فأخبرته بذلك، فقال: «رُؤيَا صِدْقٍ أو حق»، ألقها على بلال، فإنه أندى صوتاً منك، ومره ينادي به. فألقيتها، فقام على بيت أرملة كان أعلى سطوح بالمدينة، وجعل يؤذن، فلما سمع عمره، خرج في إزار يهرول، ويقول: طاف بي الليلة ما طاف بعبد الله إلا أنه سبقني، فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الحمد لله وإنه لأثبت». واختلف في ذلك الملك، فقيل: جبريل، وقيل غيره. وروي أن سبعة من الصحابة رأوا تلك الرؤيا في ليلة واحدة. كذا في « المبسوطين »، ومحمد بن الحنيفة. وقيل: زين العابدين ينكر هذا، ويقول: يعمدون إلى ما هو من معالم الدين، فيقولون: ثبت بالرؤيا، وإنما طريقه الوحي قلنا: ثبت الأذان بأمره عليه الصلاة والسلام، لا بالمنام وحده. وقيل: نزل به جبريل عليه الصلاة والسلام على النبي، حين قال « كثير بن مرة »: أذن جبريل في السماء فسمعه عمر، ولا منافاة بين هذه الأسباب، فليجعل كل ذلك كان سبباً، كذا في « معراج الدراية»، وفي « سنن أبي داود » حكى ألفاظ الأذان وهي معلومة. وفي حديث « المعراج »: إن الملك الذي خرج من الحجاب الذي يلي عرش الرحمن، أذن. وهو يدل على أن التعليم كان ليلة الإسراء، إلا أنه لم يعمل به إلا بعدما رآه عبد الله، وشرع في السنة: الأولى من الهجرة، وقيل في الثانية كما في « البرهان ». وسببه: دخول الوقت، وهو شرط له، ومنه كونه بلفظ العربي، على الصحيح من عاقل وشرط كماله كون المؤذن ذكراً صالحاً، عالماً بالوقت، طاهراً، متفقداً أحوال الناس زاجراً من تخلف عن الجماعة، صيتاً حسناً بمكان مرتفع، مستقبلاً. وحكمه: لزوم إجابته بالفعل. وركنه الألفاظ المخصوصة وصفته سنة مؤكدة وكيفيته: الترسل. ومحل شرع فيه: المدينة المنورة. ووقته أوقات الصلوات ولو قضاء. ويطلب من سامعه الإجابة بالقول كالفعل كما سنذكره مع بيان ألفاظه ومعانيها، إن شاء الله تعالى. وقد اعتنى بذكر وصفه فقال: (سُنَّ الأذان) لما ذكرنا في بيان مشروعيته، وللمواظبة عليه، وليس بواجب، هو الأصح، لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام لما علم الأعرابي كيف يصلي، لم يذكر له الأذان، (وَ) كذا (الإقامة) لم يذكرها له، فكان كلا منهما (سُنَّة مؤكدة)، وهي في قوة الواجب، وقال بعض مشايخنا: إنه واجب لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: « إِذَا حَضَرَتِ الصَّلاةُ، فليُؤَذَنَ لَكُمْ أحدكم، وليؤمكُم أكبركُمْ »، أمر وهو للوجوب، وبما روي عن محمد رحمه الله أنه قال: لو أن أهل بلدة اجتمعوا على ترك الأذان، لقاتلتهم، ولو تركه واحد، ضربته وحبسته وإنما يقاتل على ترك الفروض والجواب: أنه قال ذلك، لأنه وإن كان سنة، إلا أن تركه بالإصرار استخفاف بالدين فليزم القتال، وقيل: لا يدل قوله على الوجوب. فإنه روي عنه أنه قال: لو تركوا سنة من سنن رسول الله، لقاتلتهم عليها، ولو تركها واحد لضربته. وعن أبي يوسف يحبسون ويضربون. وهو يدل على تأكيده. وقيل عن محمد: فرض كفاية. وقيل: إذا كانت السنة من شعائر الدين يقاتل عليها. وكلا القولين بالوجوب والسنة قريبان.
The Prophet ﷺ, and some of its objectives are missed, and some are occupied from hastening due to thinking it is delayed. So he consulted the Companions about setting up a sign by which they would know the time of the Prophet's prayer so that they would not miss the congregation. Some said: set up a flag; when people see it, they inform each other. That did not please him. Some suggested striking a nāqūs (bell), but he disliked it because of the Christians. Some suggested blowing the shabūr (horn), but he disliked it because of the Jews. Some suggested lighting a fire, but he disliked it because of the Magians. They dispersed before agreeing on anything. 'Abdullāh ibn Zayd al-Anṣārī, the one of the adhān (not the one of wuḍū'), said: 'I spent the night not sleeping, I was between sleeping and awake, when I saw a person descending from the sky, wearing two green garments, holding something resembling a nāqūs. I said: Will you sell this nāqūs? He said: What will you do with it? I said: I will take it to the Prophet ﷺ to strike it at the time of our prayer. He said: Shall I guide you to something better than this? I said: Yes. He stood on the base of a wall, facing the qiblah, and gave the adhān, then paused a while, then said the same, adding at the end: 'qad qāmat al-ṣalāh' twice. I came to the Prophet ﷺ and informed him. He said: 'A truthful dream, or a vision.' Dictate it to Bilāl, for he has a louder voice than you, and order him to call with it. So I dictated it. He stood on the house of a widow which was the highest roof in Madīnah, and began to call the adhān. When 'Umar heard him, he came out dragging his lower garment, saying: 'The same thing came to me tonight as came to 'Abdullāh except that he preceded me.' The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Praise be to Allāh that it is confirmed.' There is disagreement about that angel: some said Jibrīl, others said otherwise. It is narrated that seven of the Companions saw that same dream in one night. Thus in al-Mabsūṭayn. And Muḥammad ibn al-Ḥanafiyyah, it is said that Zayn al-'Ābidīn denies this and says: 'They take something that is among the symbols of the religion and say it is established by a dream, whereas its way is revelation.' We say: the adhān is established by his command ﷺ, not by the dream alone. It is said that Jibrīl descended with it to the Prophet when 'Kuthayyir ibn Murrah' said: Jibrīl gave the adhān in the heaven and 'Umar heard him. There is no contradiction among these causes; all may have been a cause. Thus in Mi'rāj al-Dirāyah. And in Sunan Abī Dāwūd the words of the adhān are mentioned, and they are known. In the ḥadīth of al-Mi'rāj: 'The angel who came out from behind the veil next to the Throne of the Merciful gave the adhān.' This indicates that the instruction was on the night of al-Isrā', except that it was not acted upon until after 'Abdullāh saw it. And it was prescribed in the first year of the Hijrah; some say the second, as in al-Burhān. Its cause (sabab) is the entry of the time, and it is a condition for it. Among its conditions is that it be in Arabic, according to the correct view, from a sane person. Conditions for its perfection (shurūṭ kamālih) are that the mu'adhdhin be male, righteous, knowledgeable of the time, pure, attentive to the people's conditions, deterring those who lag behind from the congregation, with a good voice, in an elevated place, facing the qiblah. Its ruling: it is necessary to respond to it by action. Its pillar (rukn) is the specific words. Its description (ṣifah) is sunnah mu'akkadah. Its manner (kayfiyyah) is prolonged recitation (tarasul). Its place of legislation is Madīnah al-Munawwarah. Its time is the times of the prayers, even if making up. And the hearer is required to respond with words like actions, as we will mention with the explanation of its words and meanings, if Allāh wills. The author has taken care to mention its description, so he said: 'The adhān is sunnah' due to what we mentioned regarding its legislation, and for constancy upon it. It is not obligatory; that is the correct view, because the Prophet ﷺ when he taught the Bedouin how to pray, he did not mention the adhān to him, and similarly the iqāmah he did not mention to him. So each of them is a sunnah mu'akkadah, and it is at the strength of the obligatory. Some of our mashā'ikh said: it is obligatory, due to his saying ﷺ: 'When the prayer is about to begin, let one of you give the adhān for you, and let the oldest among you lead the prayer.' A command indicates obligation. And due to what is narrated from Muḥammad (may Allāh have mercy on him) that he said: 'If the people of a town agreed to abandon the adhān, I would fight them; and if one person leaves it, I would beat him and imprison him.' And fighting is only for abandoning obligations. The answer: He said that because even though it is sunnah, abandoning it persistently is contempt for the religion, so fighting becomes necessary. It is also said: his statement does not indicate obligation. For it is narrated from him that he said: 'If they abandon a sunnah of the Messenger of Allāh, I would fight them for it; and if one person leaves it, I would beat him.' And from Abū Yūsuf: they are imprisoned and beaten. This indicates its emphasis (ta'kīd). Some said from Muḥammad: it is farḍ kifāyah. Some said: when a sunnah is among the rituals (sha'ā'ir) of the religion, fighting over it is done. Both statements (obligation and sunnah) are close.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage from Imdād al-Fattāḥ is a commentary (sharḥ) on the matn of Nūr al-Īḍāḥ, specifically addressing the ruling of the adhān and iqāmah. It opens with the well-known narrative of the origins of the adhān during the Prophet's time in Madīnah. The Companions initially considered various methods to signal prayer times—flags, bells, horns, fire—but the Prophet rejected each due to their association with other religious communities. The solution came through a dream experienced by 'Abdullāh ibn Zayd al-Anṣārī, who saw an angel teaching him the words of the adhān. The Prophet confirmed it as a true dream and instructed Bilāl to call the adhān because of his powerful voice. The commentary then addresses a subtle legal point: the adhān was established by the Prophet's oral command (amr), not merely by the dream itself, thus preserving the principle that acts of worship must be based on revelation. Afterward, the author discusses the legal classification (ḥukm) of the adhān and iqāmah: the relied-upon position (aṣaḥḥ) is that they are sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), not wājib. The evidence for this is the ḥadīth of the Bedouin, in which the Prophet taught him the prayer without mentioning the adhān or iqāmah. The passage then presents a genuine intra-Ḥanafī disagreement: some mashā'ikh considered them wājib, citing the Prophet's command 'let one of you give the adhān' (considered a command for obligation) and the statement of Imām Muḥammad that he would fight a town that abandons it. The commentary refutes this by explaining that fighting over a sunnah mu'akkadah is when its abandonment amounts to contempt for religion (istikhfāf bi al-dīn), not because the act itself is wājib. It further reports that Imām Muḥammad also said he would fight for abandoning any sunnah of the Prophet, and Abū Yūsuf said they should be imprisoned and beaten—all of which indicates strong emphasis (ta'kīd), not obligation in the legal sense. Thus the operative ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah, though the difference is practically minor as both obligate response in some contexts.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed and recommended, but omission does not incur sin, though it is blameworthy. It is in the strength of the wājib, meaning it is nearly obligatory in practice.
الأذان (al-adhān): The specific verbal call to announce the entry of prayer time, consisting of established phrases, performed in a prescribed manner.
الإقامة (al-iqāmah): The second call immediately before the prayer commences, similar in wording to the adhān but with the addition of 'qad qāmat al-ṣalāh' twice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Ḥanafī school, what is the legal ruling of the adhān and iqāmah?
A) Wājib
B) Sunan mu'akkadah
C) Farḍ kifāyah
D) Mubāḥ

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi ruling is that adhan and iqama are sunnah mu'akkadah, established by the Prophet's omission in the Bedouin hadith, though strong emphasis from some scholars approaches wajib.

Adhan and Iqamah are Sunnah Mu'akkadah
States the ruling of adhan and iqamah as sunnah mu'akkadah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqamah, explain the primary evidence for the sunnah mu'akkadah position, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this issue.

Core Idea
Adhan is an emphasized sunnah, not an obligation; the Prophet’s omission of it when teaching the bedouin proves it is not wajib.

This lesson examines the legal status of adhan and iqamah in the Hanafi school. While many Muslims assume they are required (wajib), the relied Hanafi position is that they are sunnah mu'akkadah — a highly emphasized act that is still not obligatory. The text from Imdad al-Fattah presents the evidence and addresses the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon (adhan and iqamah)? What is the hukm level according to the relied Hanafi position?
The text states it is sunnah mu'akkadah, meaning not obligatory.
2
Locate the primary evidence
What is the main proof cited for the sunnah position? Find the hadith of the bedouin and note how it is used.
The Prophet did not mention adhan when teaching the essentials of prayer.
3
Understand the opposing opinion
Some Hanafi scholars (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in some narrations) considered adhan wajib. What evidence do they offer?
They cite the command in 'let one of you give the adhan' and the ruling to fight for its abandonment.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
How does the text rebut the opposing evidence? What distinguishes fighting for a sunnah from fighting for a fard?
The response explains that fighting is for abandonment of a prominent ritual, not because it is wajib.
5
Determine the practical consequence
What is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) between the two positions?
If adhan is left, salah is still valid; the punishment is not like abandoning a fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سن الأذان والإقامة سنة مؤكدة. وقد اعتنى بذكر وصفه فقال: (سُنَّ الأذان) لما ذكرنا في بيان مشروعيته، وللمواظبة عليه، وليس بواجب، هو الأصح، لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام لما علم الأعرابي كيف يصلي، لم يذكر له الأذان، (وَ) كذا (الإقامة) لم يذكرها له، فكان كلا منهما (سُنَّة مؤكدة)، وهي في قوة الواجب، وقال بعض مشايخنا: إنه واجب لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: « إِذَا حَضَرَتِ الصَّلاةُ، فليُؤَذَنَ لَكُمْ أحدكم، وليؤمكُم أكبركُمْ )، أمر ، وهو للوجوب، وبما روي عن محمد رحمه الله أنه قال: لو أن أهل بلدة اجتمعوا على ترك الأذان، لقاتلتهم، ولو تركه واحد، ضربته وحبسته وإنما يقاتل على ترك الفروض والجواب: أنه قال ذلك، لأنه وإن كان سنة، إلا أن تركه بالإصرار استخفاف بالدين فليزم القتال، وقيل: لا يدل قوله على الوجوب. فإنه روي عنه أنه قال: لو تركوا سنة من سنن رسول الله، لقاتلتهم عليها، ولو تركها واحد لضربته. وعن أبي يوسف يحبسون ويضربون. وهو يدل على تأكيده. وقيل عن محمد: فرض كفاية. وقيل: إذا كانت السنة من شعائر الدين يقاتل عليها. وكلا القولين بالوجوب والسنة قريبان
The adhan and iqamah are an emphasized sunnah. He has taken care to mention its description and said: 'The adhan is sunnah' due to what we mentioned regarding its legislation and for adherence to it, and it is not obligatory, which is the most correct opinion, because the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, when he taught the bedouin how to pray, he did not mention the adhan to him, and likewise the iqamah he did not mention it to him, so each of them is an emphasized sunnah, and it is in the strength of an obligation. Some of our shaykhs said: It is wajib because of his statement, peace and blessings be upon him: 'When the time for prayer comes, let one of you give the adhan for you, and let the eldest of you lead you in prayer' – a command, and a command indicates obligation, and because of what was narrated from Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, that he said: 'If the people of a town agreed to abandon the adhan, I would fight them, and if one person abandoned it, I would strike him and imprison him' – and fighting is only done for abandoning obligations. The answer: He said that because even though it is a sunnah, abandoning it persistently is a disparagement of the religion, so fighting becomes necessary. And it is said: His statement does not indicate obligation, for it is narrated from him that he said: 'If they abandon a sunnah from the sunnahs of the Messenger of Allah, I would fight them for it, and if one person abandoned it, I would strike him.' And from Abu Yusuf: They are imprisoned and struck. And this indicates its emphasis. And it is said from Muhammad: It is a communal obligation. And it is said: When a sunnah is from the rituals of the religion, fighting is done for it. And both statements regarding obligation and sunnah are close.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling of adhan and iqamah as an emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), meaning it is highly recommended but not obligatory. The author of Imdad al-Fattah explains that the correct position is that it is not wajib, citing the famous hadith of the bedouin where the Prophet did not mention adhan when teaching how to pray. However, some Hanafi scholars, including some reports from Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, considered it wajib, arguing from the command in the hadith 'let one of you give the adhan' and from the fact that people would be fought for abandoning it. The response is that the fighting is due to the abandonment of a sunnah that is a prominent ritual of Islam, not because it is wajib in itself. The passage concludes that both opinions (wajib and sunnah) are close, but the relied-upon position is sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah that is in the strength of an obligation, but not wajib; abandoning it is disliked and may incur sin if done persistently.
واجب (wajib): A legal obligation proved by a zanni (probable) evidence, like ahad hadith; abandoning it is sinful but not as severe as abandoning fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Fard 'ayn or wajib
B) Fard kifayah
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah
D) Mandub or mubah

Key Takeaway
The relied Hanafi position is that adhan and iqamah are sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib, based on the Prophet's omission of them when teaching the essentials of prayer.

Conditions for Adhan: Fard Prayers, Men, and Four Takbirs
Ruling on adhan scope and takbir count

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for adhan (only for fard prayers, for men, four opening takbirs) and explain the Hanafi position on the takbir count dispute.

Core Idea
Adhan is only prescribed for fard prayers, for men, with four opening takbirs.

This passage from Nur al-Idah clarifies the scope of adhan: when it is prescribed, for whom, and its opening wording. The Hanafi school holds that adhan is a sunnah mu'akkadah only for fard prayers, and that men call it with four takbirs at the beginning. The author also addresses the intra-Hanafi difference regarding the number of takbirs and provides evidence from hadith for calling adhan even when alone.

Guided Path
1
Determine the prayers for which adhan is allowed
Identify from the text which prayers adhan is prescribed for. The text says 'للفرائض' and explicitly excludes 'Eid, eclipse, tarawih, funeral, and witr. It includes Jumu'ah as a fard prayer.
Jumu'ah is considered a fard prayer in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the gender ruling
Adhan is prescribed for men and disliked for women. Understand the reason: women are to conceal themselves and raising their voices is haram.
The ruling is makruh tanzihi for women.
3
Analyze the takbir count dispute
The majority position is four takbirs at the beginning of adhan. There is a minority view from Abu Yusuf and Hasan b. Ziyad that it is two. The text adopts four as the correct count.
The mufta bihi is four takbirs.
4
Examine the evidence provided
The text quotes hadith encouraging adhan even for a lone person, demonstrating that the purpose of adhan is not limited to notification but includes spreading the remembrance of Allah.
These hadith support the ruling for the individual caller.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للفرائض، ولو منفرداً أداءً أو قضاء، سفراً أَوْ حَضَراً، للرجال، وكُرها للنساء، ويُكبر في أوله أربعا. لأن السنة المؤكدة بمنزلة الواجب في لحوق الإثم بالترك. وقال عامة مشايخنا: إنهما سنتان مؤكدتان (لِلْفَرَائِض)، احترازاً عن غيرها، فلا يؤذن لعيد واستسقاء وكسوف وتراويح وجنازة ووتر، فلا يقع أذان العشاء للوتر، على الصحيح، والجمعة من الفرائض، لأنه كان يؤذن في عهده للصلوات الخمس والجمعة دون غيرها. وكذلك الأئمة من بعده إلى يومنا فيؤذن للفرض (وَلَوْ) يصليه (مُنْفَردَاً)، لأنه سنة الصلاة. وقد ورد في خصوص المنفرد ما رواه أبو داود والنسائي. قال : يَعْجَبُ رَبُّكَ مِنْ رَاعِي عَلَمٍ فِي رَأسِ شَفِيَّةٍ يُؤَدِّنُ بِالصَّلاةِ، وَيُصَلِّي، فَيَقُولُ اللَّهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ: انْظُرُوا إِلَى عَبْدِي هَذَا، يُؤَذِّنُ، وَيُقِيمُ الصَّلاةَ، يَخَافُ مِنِّي، قَدْ غَفَرْتُ لِعَبْدِي وَادْخَلْتُهُ الْجَنَّةَ . وعن سلمان نه قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « إذا كان الرجلُ بأرض فحانَتِ الصَّلاةُ، فليتوضاً، فإن لَمْ يَجِدْ مَاءً فليتيمم، فإذَا قَامَ صَلَّى مَعَهُ مَلكان، وإِذَا أَذَّنَ وأَقَامَ صَلَّى خَلْفَهُ مِنْ جنود الله ما لا يُرَى طَرَفَاهُ». رواه عبــد الرزاق. وبهذا ونحوه عرف أن المقصود من الأذان لم ينحصر في الإعلام، بل كُلُّ منه ومـــن الإعلان، بهذا الذكر نشر ذكر الله ودينه في أرضه. وتذكير لعباده لمن لا يرى شخصهم في الفلوات من العباد وصالح الجن، فيؤذن سواء صلى (أداء أو قضاء، سفراً أو حَضَراً، كما فعـلـه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ويأتي بـه المصلي في بيته في المصر ندباً، وكره ترك المسافر الإقامة، لا الأذان، ولا يكره للمقيم تركهما، لـــو أذن وأقيم في المسجد، وصلى منفرداً في بيته، وإنما يسن الأذان والإقامة (للرجال. وكُرها للنساء) لما روي عن أنس وابن عمر من كراهتهما لهن، ولأن مبنى حالهن على الستر، ورفع صوتهن حرام. (و) أشار إلى ضبط ألفاظ الأذان بقوله : ( يُكَبِّرُ في أوّلهِ أربعاً)، احترازاً عما قيل عن أبي يوسف، وعن رواية الحسن، أنه يكبر مرتين في أوله، فيقول: الله أكبر، الله أكبر، الله أكبر، الله أكبر، الله عـلـم للمعبود لذاته. وأكبر إما مأخوذ من كبر، بمعنى عظم، فإنه عظيم القدر، وإما من كبر، أي: أسن، ویراد به القديم ها هنا. وأكبر للتفضيل، وتقديره الله أكبر . أي: أجل وأعظم من كل ما اشتغلتم بـه
For the fard prayers, even if performed alone, whether as performance or qada', whether traveling or present, for men, and disliked for women. And he says: He makes the takbir at its beginning four times. Because the emphasized sunnah is in the position of the wajib with regard to the incurrence of sin for leaving it. The majority of our shaykhs said: Both are emphasized sunnahs for the fard prayers, as a precaution against other prayers, so no adhan is called for 'Eid, prayer for rain, eclipse, tarawih, funeral, or witr. So the adhan for 'Isha' does not serve for witr, according to the correct opinion. And Jumu'ah is one of the fard prayers, because adhan was called in his era for the five prayers and Jumu'ah, not for others, and the imams after him to our day, so adhan is called for the fard prayer even if one prays it alone, because it is a sunnah of the prayer. And there has been reported concerning the one who prays alone what Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i narrated: 'Your Lord marvels at a shepherd on a mountain peak who calls the adhan and prays, then Allah says: Look at My servant, he calls the adhan and establishes the prayer, fearing Me; I have forgiven My servant and admitted him to Paradise.' And from Salman, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'If a man is in a land and the time of prayer comes, let him perform wudu', if he cannot find water then let him tayammum, then when he stands to pray, two angels pray with him, and if he calls the adhan and iqamah, angels of Allah pray behind him, whose ends cannot be seen.' Narrated by 'Abd al-Razzaq. And by this and similar it is known that the purpose of adhan is not limited to notification, but rather all of it and of announcement, with this remembrance, is spreading the remembrance of Allah and His religion in His land, and reminding His servants of those whose persons are not seen in the wilderness, from among the righteous jinn. So he calls the adhan whether he prays performance or qada', traveling or present, as the Prophet did. And the one praying brings it in his house in the city as supererogatory. And it is disliked for a traveler to leave the iqamah, but not the adhan, and it is not disliked for a resident to leave them if the adhan and iqamah are called in the mosque and he prays alone at home. And adhan and iqamah are only prescribed for men. And they are disliked for women, due to what is narrated from Anas and Ibn 'Umar of their dislike for them, and because the nature of women is concealment, and raising their voices is haram. And he pointed to the exact wording of adhan by saying: 'He says the takbir at its beginning four times,' as a caution against what was said from Abu Yusuf and from the narration of Hasan, that he says the takbir twice at its beginning, saying: Allahu akbar, Allahu akbar, Allahu akbar, Allahu akbar. Allah is the knowledge of the worshipped for His essence. And 'akbar' is either derived from 'kabara' meaning 'great,' for He is great in status, or from 'kabira' meaning 'old,' and it is intended as 'the Eternal' here. And 'akbar' is for the comparative, and its meaning is 'Allah is greater' i.e., more majestic and greater than everything with which you are occupied.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage outlines key conditions and rulings for adhan and iqamah. First, they are prescribed specifically for fard prayers (including Jumu'ah) and not for other prayers like 'Eid, eclipse, tarawih, funeral, or witr. Even if one prays alone, adhan is recommended, supported by hadith about the shepherd's reward. Second, adhan is for men only; it is disliked for women because they are to conceal themselves and raising voices is haram. Third, the opening takbir in adhan is four times (not two, as some narrated from Abu Yusuf and Hasan). The passage also discusses that the purpose of adhan is not just notification but also spreading remembrance of Allah, and it is recommended to call adhan even when traveling or alone, as the Prophet did.

Key Terms
الفرائض (al-fara'id): The obligatory prayers (five daily plus Jumu'ah). Adhan is only prescribed for these.
يُكبر في أوله أربعا (yukabbiru fi awwalihi arba'an): The adhan begins with four takbirs (Allahu akbar said four times), contrary to some narrations that it is two.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Salah — Prayer
beginner
10 min
Rulings of Adhan and Iqama: Prescription, Wording, and Dislikes
Explains when adhan is prescribed, for whom, and the wording including takbir count

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on when adhan is prescribed, explain the dispute over the number of takbirs, and apply the rule of jazm in articulation.

Core Idea
Adhan is sunnah mu'akkadah for fard prayers, even for one praying alone, but disliked for women.

This lesson examines a passage from Imdad al-Fattah that clarifies the legal status of adhan and iqama in the Hanafi school. You will learn that these calls are not fard but confirmed sunnah, prescribed specifically for the five daily and Friday prayers, and that they are recommended even for the solitary traveler. We will also explore the disputed number of takbirs and the proper articulation with jazm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope of prescription
The text states adhan is for fara'id (obligatory prayers), including Friday, and even for one praying alone, whether performing on time or making up, traveling or resident. Note the exception: witr and funeral prayers are excluded.
The phrase 'احترازاً عن غيرها' indicates precaution against non-fard prayers.
2
State the legal ruling and its basis
Adhan and iqama are sunnah mu'akkadah. The text supports this with ahadith showing their merit, especially the hadith of the shepherd and the hadith of Salman. Recognize that the evidence is zanni al-thubut, so the ruling remains sunnah, not fard.
The author says 'لأن السنة المؤكدة بمنزلة الواجب في لحوق الإثم بالترك' – abandoning without excuse is sinful.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on takbir number
The matn says 'يكبر في أوله أربعاً', affirming four takbirs. The author notes this is a precaution against the view of Abu Yusuf and Hasan ibn Ziyad, who held it to be two. The mufta bihi is four.
The dispute is about the number of times 'Allahu Akbar' is said at the start of adhan.
4
Understand the ruling for women
Adhan and iqama are prescribed only for men; they are makruh for women because their condition requires concealment and raising their voices is prohibited.
The text cites narrations from Anas and Ibn Umar for disapproval.
5
Apply the rule of jazm (sukun) in articulation
The words of adhan and iqama should be recited with jazm – stopping on the final letter without vowel. For 'Allahu Akbar', the ra' is saakinah. There is also a choice between raf' and jazm in repeated takbirs.
The text quotes al-Nakha'i and al-Mubarrad emphasizing this practice.

For the obligatory prayers, even if praying alone, performing or making up, traveling or present, for men, and disliked for women. And he makes the opening takbir four times. Because the confirmed sunnah is like an obligation in that sin follows its abandonment. The majority of our scholars said: They are two confirmed sunnahs. (For the obligatory prayers) as a precaution against other than them, so no adhan is made for Eid, istisqa, eclipse, taraweeh, funeral, or witr; the adhan for Isha does not occur for witr according to the correct view. Friday is among the obligatory prayers because during his time adhan was made for the five prayers and Friday alone, and similarly the imams after him until today, so adhan is made for the obligatory. (Even if) he prays (alone) because it is a sunnah of the prayer. And there has come regarding the one praying alone what Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i narrated: 'Your Lord marvels at a shepherd on a mountain peak who calls the adhan and prays; Allah says: Look at this servant of Mine, he calls the adhan and establishes the prayer, fearing Me; I have forgiven My servant and admitted him to Paradise.' And from Salman: The Messenger of Allah said: 'When a man is in a land and the time for prayer comes, let him perform wudhu; if he cannot find water, let him perform tayammum; when he prays, two angels pray with him; and if he calls the adhan and iqama, angels of Allah whose ends cannot be seen pray behind him.' Narrated by Abd al-Razzaq. By this and similar it is known that the purpose of adhan is not limited to notification, but rather each of it and the iqama spreads the remembrance of Allah and His religion on His earth, and a reminder for His servants who cannot see people in the deserts, among righteous servants and jinn. So he calls adhan whether he prays (in time or makeup, traveling or present) as the Prophet did. He brings it in his house in the city as a recommendable act; it is disliked for a traveler to leave the iqama, not the adhan; and it is not disliked for a resident to leave both if the adhan and iqama were given in the mosque and he prays alone in his house. Rather adhan and iqama are prescribed (for men. And disliked for women) because of what is narrated from Anas and Ibn Umar regarding disapproval for them, and because their condition is based on concealment, and raising their voices is prohibited. (And) he pointed to the adjustment of the words of adhan by his saying: (He makes the opening takbir four times) as a precaution against what was said from Abu Yusuf and the narration of al-Hasan that he makes takbir twice at the beginning, saying: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar. Allah is a name for the Worshipped One by His essence. Akbar is either derived from kabura meaning greatness, for He is great of status, or from kabira meaning old, and by it is meant the Eternal here. Akbar is for preference, and its estimation is Allahu Akbar, i.e., more majestic and greater than everything you are occupied with. And it was narrated: "And His work is weightier, so be occupied with His work and leave worldly works." The Salaf, when they heard the adhan, left everything they were in. He makes jazm on the ra', i.e., he makes it sakin in the takbir, and makes sakin the words of adhan and iqama, because of what is narrated from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that he said: Two things are made with jazm that they did not know: adhan and iqama. Al-Zayla'i said: Meaning upon waqf. But in adhan it is real, and in iqama one intends waqf. End. That is, to cut it. It is narrated from al-Nakha'i as mauquf on him, and marfu' to the Prophet that he said: "Adhan is jazm, iqama is jazm, and takbir is jazm." Abu al-Abbas al-Mubarrad said: The ra' in the saying 'Allahu Akbar' is waqf in starting prayer; and similarly the second ra' in adhan, as in 'Hayya ala al-salah' and 'Hayya ala al-falah' the ha' and the ha' are waqf. Thus we heard, and we did not hear that the ra' is made with dammah; rather the common people do that. So in 'Majma' al-Riwayat', so consider what was said in 'al-Bahr' from 'al-Mudmarat': He has a choice in the takbir: if he wishes, he says it with raf', and if he wishes, with jazm; and if he repeats takbir many times, the noble name is marfu' each time, and the word 'Akbar' except the last time is with raf', and in the last time he has a choice: if he wishes, he says it with raf', and if he wishes, with jazm. End. Then the muadhdhin says 'Ashhadu alla ilaha illallah, Ashhadu alla ilaha illallah' meaning: I affirm and confirm that there is no deity worthy of worship except Allah; it is an announcement that I am not contradicting you in what I call you to and testify of divinity to Allah alone with no partner; so obey His command, for none can benefit you except Allah, and none can save you from His punishment if you do not fulfill His command and believe His messenger in the matter of establishing the congregation. This is the meaning of his saying 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasul Allah, Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasul Allah', then he says: 'Hayya ala al-salah, Hayya ala al-salah' i.e., come, hasten, rush, and hurry to the good in which is success and salvation, which is performing the prayer, for its time has come, so establish it and do not delay it beyond its time, and pray it in congregation. Then he says: 'Hayya ala al-falah, Hayya ala al-falah'.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, covers several key rulings on adhan and iqama.

First, the primary ruling: adhan and iqama are specifically for the obligatory prayers (fara'id). They are not prescribed for other prayers like Eid, istisqa (rain prayer), eclipse prayer, taraweeh, funeral prayer, or witr. The author mentions that the majority of Hanafi scholars consider them both confirmed sunnahs (sunnah mu'akkadah) for the obligatory prayers. Friday prayer is included as it is a fard.

Second, the adhan is prescribed even if one prays alone, whether performing the prayer on time or making it up, whether traveling or resident. The author cites two hadiths to support this: one about a shepherd on a mountain who calls adhan and prays alone, and Allah forgives him; another where angels pray with a man who prays alone, but if he calls adhan and iqama, countless angels pray behind him. The point is that the purpose of adhan is not merely to notify people of the prayer time but to spread the remembrance of Allah, especially in desolate areas.

Third, regarding the number of takbirs at the beginning: the author states that the muadhdhin says 'Allahu Akbar' four times. He notes that Abu Yusuf and a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad hold that it is only twice. The author's position is the relied-upon view (mu'tamad).

Fourth, permissibility for women: adhan and iqama are prescribed for men only. They are disliked (makruh) for women because their condition is based on concealment and raising their voices is prohibited for them.

Fifth, articulation: the words of adhan and iqama should be recited with jazm (stopping, i.e., with sukun on the final letter), based on the practice of the Salaf and a narration from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. For 'Allahu Akbar', the ra' should be saakinah (not with dammah). However, there is also a view that there is a choice between raf' (nominative case) and jazm, especially in the last takbir when repeating.

The passage also gives the meanings of the phrases: 'Ashhadu alla ilaha illallah' affirms the oneness of Allah, 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasul Allah' affirms prophethood, 'Hayya ala al-salah' is a call to prayer, and 'Hayya ala al-falah' is a call to success.

Key Terms
فريضة (farīḍah): An obligatory prayer (fard) such as the five daily prayers and Friday prayer.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah; its abandonment without excuse is sinful but not as severe as abandoning a fard.
جزم (jazm): Articulating with a stop or sukun on the final letter; not pronouncing it with a vowel.
إقامة (iqāmah): The call immediately before the start of the prayer, similar to adhan but with differences in wording and number of repetitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many times is 'Allahu Akbar' said at the beginning of the adhan?
A) Twice
B) Four times
C) Once
D) Three times

Key Takeaway
Adhan and iqama are sunnah mu'akkadah for fard prayers, prescribed for men even when alone or traveling, but disliked for women; the opening takbir is four times (mufta bihi), and words are recited with jazm.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
7 min
The Rule of Jazm in Adhan and Iqamah
Explains the rule of jazm in adhan and its meanings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jazm in adhan and iqamah, identify the evidence, and explain the pronunciation choices in the takbir.

Core Idea
The adhan must be recited with jazm (sukun endings) — a wajib practice established by the Salaf.

The proper pronunciation of the adhan is not merely a stylistic matter; it carries legal weight in the Hanafi school. This lesson unpacks the rule of jazm — stopping on the final letters of each word — and examines the evidence from the practice of the righteous predecessors. We will also explore the nuanced choice the mu'adhdhin has in the opening and concluding takbir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
Recognize that the passage establishes the requirement of jazm (sukun) for the adhan and iqamah. The ruling is that the mu'adhdhin must make the final letter of each word sukun, except where a choice is given.
This is a wajib ruling, not merely sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the narration from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (a Tabi'i) stating that the earliest Muslims knew only two things as jazm: the adhan and iqamah. Also note the marfu' version attributed to the Prophet, though the commentator clarifies its actual status.
The dalil is a qawl sahabi (or tabi'i) and is considered zanni in both thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit statement that the Salaf made these two things jazm indicates that this practice is binding. The phrase 'they did not know them except as jazm' suggests it was a consistent, well-known practice.
This is a strong indicator of obligation in the Hanafi usul.
4
Note the choice in the takbir
According to the text from 'al-Bahr', the mu'adhdhin has a choice in the opening takbir between raf' (dammah) and jazm (sukun). Similarly, in the final repetition of 'Akbar' there is a choice; in the middle repetitions, 'Akbar' must be recited with raf'.
This is a limited exception to the general rule of jazm.
5
Understand the meanings of the phrases
The passage explains the meanings of 'Ashhadu', 'Hayya 'ala al-salah', and 'Hayya 'ala al-falah', linking them to tawhid, urgency in prayer, and eternal success. Knowing these meanings enhances the mu'adhdhin's mindfulness.
The linguistic origin of 'hayya' and 'falah' is also discussed.

مفلح، ولكل من أصاب خيراً: مفلح. وأصل الكلمة من قول العرب عن دعائهم إلى الطعام: حي على الثريد، أي: هلموا إلى تناول الثريد وأكله. يقال: حي إلى كذا، وحي على كذا، أي: أقبل إليه، ومنه قول ابن مسعود: «إذا ذكر الصالحون فحي هل بعمر»، أي: أسرع بذكر فضائله وشمائله. وفيه ثلاث روايات: فحي هل بعمر، وحي هلا بعمر، وحي هلا بعمر، بسكون اللام، وموقوفاً ومنوناً. و) بعده (يثني تكبير آخره)، فيقول: الله أكبر، الله أكبر، عوداً إلى الإجلال والتعظيم، وليكون أدعى إلى المسارعة للطاعة والعبادة والإجابة. فإن النفس داعية إلى العصيان مجبولة على الطغيان. ثم يختمه بكلمة التوحيد على جهة التجريد، فيقول مذعناً بالإخلاص: لا إله إلا الله، تنبيهاً للموحدين، وحجة قائمة على رؤوس الجاحدين. وقوله: (كباقي ألفاظه)، أي: إن باقي الكلمات بعد التكبير أربعاً في أوله تثنى، وقد ذكرناها. وقيل: الحكمة في تكرير كلماته تعظيم شأن الصلاة في نفس السامعين، ورجاء الثواب من الله لأنا نتكلم به.
In it. And it is narrated: His action necessitated, so occupy yourselves with his action, and leave the works of the world. The righteous predecessors, may Allah have mercy on them, when they heard the adhan, they abandoned everything they were in. He makes the ra' jazm, i.e., he makes it sukun in the takbir, and he makes the words of the adhan and iqamah sukun, due to what was narrated from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, that he said: Two things are made jazm that they did not know: the adhan and the iqamah. Al-Zayla'i said: Meaning upon stopping. But in the adhan it is real, and in the iqamah he intends stopping. End. Meaning: as a hadith from al-Nakha'i as a stopped narration, and marfu' to the Prophet that he said, 'The adhan is jazm, the iqamah is jazm, and the takbir is jazm.' And Abu al-Abbas al-Mubarrad said: The ra' in the saying Allahu Akbar is stopped in the opening of the prayer. Likewise the second ra' in the adhan, like his saying 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'Hayya 'ala al-falah', the ha' and ha' are stopped. Thus we heard, and we did not hear that the ra' is made dammah, only the common people do that. Thus in 'Majma' al-Riwayat'. So let one reflect on what he said in 'al-Bahr', that he has a choice in the takbir: if he wishes he says it with raf', and if he wishes he says it with jazm. And if he repeats the takbir multiple times, the noble name is marfu' every time, and he says 'Akbar' in all except the last time with raf', and in the last time he has a choice, if he wishes he says it with raf', and if he wishes he says it with jazm. End. Then the mu'adhdhin says: Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah, Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah, meaning: I assert and verify that there is no deity worthy of worship except Allah, and it is an announcement from him that I am not opposing you in what I called you to and testified of divinity to Allah alone, no partner for Him. So follow His command, for no one benefits you except Allah, and no one saves you from His punishment if you do not perform His command and believe His messenger in the matter by establishing the congregation. And this is the meaning of his saying: Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasul Allah, Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasul Allah. Then he says: Hayya 'ala al-salah, Hayya 'ala al-salah, meaning: come, hasten, be quick, and rush to the good in which is success and salvation, which is performing the prayer, for its time has come, so establish it and do not delay it beyond its time, and pray it in congregation. Then he says: Hayya 'ala al-falah, Hayya 'ala al-falah. The meaning is like the previous, i.e., rush to salvation and happiness, for the prayer is a cause for salvation and happiness, so establish it to be saved from His punishment. And al-falah is: the winning of permanence and immortality in bliss. It is said of the successful one: muflih, and of everyone who attains good: muflih. The origin of the word is from the Arabs' call to food: Hayya 'ala al-tharid, i.e., come to take the tharid and eat it. It is said: Hayya ila kadha, and Hayya 'ala kadha, i.e., approach it. From it is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'When the righteous are mentioned, so Hayya hal bi-'Umar', i.e., hasten to mention his virtues and qualities. And there are three narrations: 'fa-hayya hal bi-'Umar', 'fa-hayya hala bi-'Umar', and 'fa-hayya hala bi-'Umar' with sukun of the lam, stopped and nunated. And) after it (he repeats the takbir of its end), so he says: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, returning to glorification and magnification, and so that it is more conducive to haste for obedience, worship, and response. For the soul calls to disobedience and is disposed to transgression. Then he concludes it with the word of tawhid in the manner of abstraction, saying in submission with sincerity: La ilaha illa Allah, as a reminder to the monotheists and a conclusive argument against the heads of the deniers. And his saying: (like the rest of its words), i.e., indeed the rest of the words after the four takbirs at its beginning are repeated, and we have mentioned them. And it is said: The wisdom in repeating its words is to magnify the status of the prayer in the ears of the listeners, and the hope of reward from Allah because we speak with it.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the sharh, expanding on the proper pronunciation and phrasing of the adhan. The commentator first establishes the rule of jazm (making the final letter sukun/stop) in the adhan and iqamah, citing a narration from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that the early Muslims would say both with jazm. Al-Zayla'i clarifies that in the adhan the stop is literal, while in the iqamah the mu'adhdhin must intend a stop form. The text then presents a quasi-marfu' version attributed to the Prophet, though the commentator notes (in the original footnotes) that it is actually from al-Nakha'i. Abu al-Abbas al-Mubarrad confirms that the ra' in 'Allahu Akbar' and the ha'/ha' in 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'Hayya 'ala al-falah' are pronounced with sukun, common practice among the masses of making dammah is incorrect. A significant point from 'al-Bahr' is cited: the mu'adhdhin has a choice in the opening takbir between raf' (nominative, i.e., with dammah) and jazm (sukoon), but after the first four, only the first word 'Allah' remains nominative each time, while 'Akbar' is only raised in the last repetition; otherwise, it is a choice. The commentary then explains the meanings of each phrase: 'Ashhadu' means assertion and verification of tawhid; 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasul Allah' attests to the prophethood; 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' is an urgent call to prayer; 'Hayya 'ala al-falah' is a call to eternal success and salvation, with 'falah' derived from farming success (falaha). The derivation from pre-Islamic call to 'tharid' (a dish) is linguistic, not ritual. Finally, the text explains that after the call, the mu'adhdhin repeats the takbir twice and concludes with 'La ilaha illa Allah', emphasizing sincerity. The phrase 'like the rest of its words' means all words after the initial four takbirs are repeated twice, with the wisdom being to elevate the prayer's status and encourage response.

Key Terms
جزم (jazm): Pronunciation with sukun (absence of vowel) on the final letter of each word; stopping without case ending.
ترجيع (tarji'): The practice of partially lowering the voice during the two shahadahs in the adhan and then raising it again.
حي على الصلاة (Hayya 'ala al-salah): A phrase calling people to come to prayer urgently; 'hayya' is a command meaning 'hasten' or 'come'.
الفلاح (al-falah): Success, salvation, eternal bliss; derived from farming imagery of prosperity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how should the ra' in 'Allahu Akbar' be pronounced in the adhan?
A) With dammah in all instances
B) With sukun (jazm) in the opening takbir, and sukun in the final takbir as well
C) With sukun in the opening takbir, but the mu'adhdhin has a choice in the final takbir between raf' and jazm
D) With dammah in the opening takbir and sukun in the final takbir

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires the adhan and iqamah to be recited with jazm (sukun endings) based on the practice of the Salaf, with a limited choice in the opening and final takbir.
