No Tarji' in the Shahadatayn During Adhan
Proves that tarji' is not part of the adhan, addressing a Shafi'i view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rejects tarji' in the shahadahs and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the madhhab dispute framework.

Core Idea
Tarji' in the shahadah is not part of the adhan — it was a personal exception for Abu Mahdhurah, not a general sunnah.

The adhan is an established worship, but small details like whether to modulate the voice in the shahadahs are disputed. This passage defends the Hanafi position that tarji' is not part of the adhan, and explains why the case of Abu Mahdhurah is not generalizable. By understanding the proofs, you will see how the Hanafi school relies on the practice of Bilal and the purpose of the adhan.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: tarji' in the shahadahs is not part of the adhan; it is at most mubah (permissible), not sunnah.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
The Shafi'i school holds tarji' as sunnah, citing the Prophet's instruction to Abu Mahdhurah.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Explain why Abu Mahdhurah's case was specific (khasa'is): pedagogical or emotional reasons, not general legislation.
The text also mentions inauthentic reports of Bilal doing tarji'.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafis do not perform tarji'; Shafi'is do. Hanafis consider it mubah, so not sinful if done.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mu'tamad (relied upon), supported by the practice of Bilal and the majority of Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تَرْجِيعَ في الشَّهادتين لأن الروايات متفقة على أن بلالاً رضي الله عنه لم يكن يرجع، ولأن المقصود من الأذان قوله حي على الصلاة حي على الفلاح ولا ترجيع فيهما، ففيما سواهما أولى. كذا في «معراج الدراية» ولأنه ليس في أذان الملك النازل، وعليه أذان بلال. وما قيل أنه رجع لم يصح. وعدم الترجيع في أذان غير أبي محذورة دليل على عدم كونه من أجزائه. وترجيع أبي محذورة من خصائصه، الأمر قام به، فأمره النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بالترجيع حالة التعلم ليحسن تعليمه، وهو كان عادة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في التعليم، فظن أنه أمره بالترجيع، أو لكونه كان في جاهليته يبغض النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أشد بغض، ففعله لزيادة محبته بعد إسلامه وزيادة إخلاصه في إيمانه، وقيل غير ذلك. وقال صاحب «البحر»: الظاهر من عباراتهم، أي مشايخنا أن الترجيع عندنا مباح فيه، ليس بسنة ولا مكروه. وكان للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ثلاثة مؤذنين: بلال وأبو محذورة واسمه سمرة، وابن أم مكتوم واسمه عمرو. فإذا غاب بلال أذن أبو محذورة، وإذا غاب أبو محذورة أذن عمرو.
And there is no tarji' in the two shahadahs, because the narrations agree that Bilal, may Allah be pleased with him, did not do tarji'. And because the purpose of the adhan is the saying 'Hayya 'ala al-salah, Hayya 'ala al-falah', and there is no tarji' in them, so in other than them it is more appropriate. Thus in 'Mi'raj al-Dirayah'. And because it is not in the adhan of the descending angel, and upon it is the adhan of Bilal. And what is said that he did tarji' is not authentic. And the absence of tarji' in the adhan of other than Abu Mahdhurah is evidence that it is not part of its components. And the tarji' of Abu Mahdhurah is from his specific characteristics; the matter was particular to him. So the Prophet ordered him to do tarji' at the time of learning to improve his teaching, and it was the Prophet's custom in teaching, so he thought that he ordered him to do tarji'. Or because he, in his pre-Islamic ignorance, severely hated the Prophet, so he did it to increase his love after his Islam and increase his sincerity in his faith. And other reasons were said. And the author of 'al-Bahr' said: The apparent from their expressions, i.e., our scholars, is that tarji' with us is permissible (mubah), not sunnah and not makruh. And the Prophet had three mu'adhdhins: Bilal, Abu Mahdhurah (his name is Samura), and Ibn Umm Maktum (his name is Amr). So when Bilal was absent, Abu Mahdhurah gave the adhan, and when Abu Mahdhurah was absent, Amr gave the adhan.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the inclusion of tarji' (partial lowering and raising of voice) in the two shahadahs of the adhan. The Hanafi position, derived from the practice of Bilal (رضي الله عنه), is that there is no tarji'. The text provides multiple proofs: (1) The consensus of narrations that Bilal did not do tarji'. (2) The main purpose of the adhan is the call 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'Hayya 'ala al-falah', which themselves have no tarji'; so the shahadahs, being less central, are even less deserving. (3) The adhan of the 'descending angel' (a reference to the mi'raj) had no tarji', and Bilal conformed to that. (4) Reports that Bilal did tarji' are not authentic. (5) The fact that no other mu'adhdhin besides Abu Mahdhurah practiced it proves it is not part of the adhan's essential structure. Abu Mahdhurah's tarji' is treated as a personal peculiarity: the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) ordered it while teaching him to improve his learning style, or it was a means to increase his love after his conversion from intense hatred. Thus, it is not a sunnah for the general community. The author of 'al-Bahr' goes further, stating that according to Hanafi scholars, tarji' is simply permissible (mubah) — neither recommended nor disliked. This shows that while the Hanafi school does not institute tarji' as a sunnah, it does not forbid it entirely if someone does it inadvertently or out of habit, provided it does not misrepresent the adhan. The final note lists the Prophet's three mu'adhdhins, underscoring that Bilal's method is the standard, while Abu Mahdhurah's was exceptional.

Key Terms
ترجيع (tarji'): In the context of adhan, it means to lower the voice when saying the two shahadahs and then raise it again; a form of modulation.
أبو محذورة (Abu Mahdhurah): A companion of the Prophet whose adhan included tarji' as a special exception.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school not consider tarji' in the shahadahs as part of the adhan?
A) Because the Prophet never ordered it for any mu'adhdhin
B) Because the narrations agree that Bilal did not do tarji', and the purpose of adhan lies in 'Hayya 'ala' which have no tarji'
C) Because tarji' is disliked (makruh) in all cases
D) Because tarji' was only allowed for Ibn Umm Maktum

Key Takeaway
Tarji' in the shahadahs is not part of the adhan; it is at most mubah, and the exception of Abu Mahdhurah does not establish a general sunnah.

Ruling on Tathniya and Tarji' in Adhan
Explains repetition of final takbir and rejection of tarji' in shahadatayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tarji' in the shahadatayn and explain the evidence from the practice of Bilal.

Core Idea
Tarji' in the shahadatayn is not from the sunnah; it is merely mubah, as the consistent practice of Bilal shows.

This passage from Nur al-Idah with its commentary clarifies two aspects of the adhan: the repetition of the final takbir like the other phrases, and the absence of tarji' in the shahadatayn. While the Shafi'i school considers tarji' sunnah, the Hanafi school holds that tarji' is neither sunnah nor makruh—it is simply permissible. The evidence from the practice of Bilal and the purpose of the adhan is presented to support this view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage gives two rulings: tathniya (repetition) of the final takbir, and the absence of tarji' in the shahadatayn. First, note that the final takbir is repeated twice like other phrases. Second, understand that tarji' (lowering then raising the voice) is not part of the sunnah adhan.
Tathniya is agreed upon; the focus is on tarji'.
2
Examine the evidence for no tarji'
The text cites that all narrations agree Bilal did not practice tarji'. Furthermore, the essential purpose of the adhan is the call 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah', which themselves have no tarji', so the other phrases are even less likely to have it.
The dalil is the consensus of narration about Bilal.
3
Understand the special case of Abu Mahdhura
Abu Mahdhura practiced tarji' but this is considered a specific concession. It may have been for teaching purposes or due to his recent conversion, not a general sunnah. The text explains that this was unique to him.
The Prophet had three mu'adhdhins: Bilal, Abu Mahdhura, and Ibn Umm Maktum.
4
Determine the Hanafi ruling on tarji'
According to Sahib al-Bahr, the apparent view of Hanafi scholars is that tarji' is mubah (permissible), not sunnah nor makruh. This is based on the absence of evidence for prohibition and the permissibility of variations in delivery.
The ruling is from later Hanafi authorities.
5
Appreciate the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school considers tarji' sunnah based on the hadith of Abu Mahdhura. Hanafis respond by distinguishing Abu Mahdhura's case as a special concession. The practical difference is that in a Hanafi setting, the mu'adhdhin may choose not to do tarji', while a Shafi'i mu'adhdhin would see it as recommended.
This ikhtilaf is a legitimate difference of interpretation.

Source Text

ويثني تكبير آخره، كباقي ألفاظه، ولا تَرْجِيعَ في الشَّهادتينوالمعنى مثل ما قبله أي أسرعوا إلى النجاة والسعادة، فإن الصلاة سبب للنجاة والسعادة فأقيموها لتنجوا من عذابه، والفلاح هو : الفوز بالبقاء، والخلود في النعيم. يقال للفائز مفلح، ولكـل مـن أصاب خيراً مفلح، وأصل الكلمة من قول العرب عن دعائهم إلى الطعام: حي على الثريد، أي:هلموا إلى تناول الثريد وأكله. يقال: حي إلى كذا، وحي على كذا، أي: أقبل بـعـــد التكبير أربعاً في أوله تُثنى، وقد ذكرناها، وقيل: الحكمة في تكرير كلماته تعظيم شأن الصلاة في نفس السامعين ورجاء الثواب من الله لأنا نتكلم به، ولا تَرجيع هو أن يخفض بالشهادتين صوته، ثم يرجع فأمره النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بالترجيع حالة التعلم، ليحسن تعليمه، وهو كان عادة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في التعليم، فظن أنه أمره بالترجيع، أو لكونــه كــان في جاهليته يبغض النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أشد ،بغض، ففعله لزيادة محبته بعد إسلامه، وزيادة إخلاصه في إيمانه، وقيل غير ذلك، وقال صاحب ( البحر » : الظاهر من عباراتهم، أي مشايخنا أن الترجيع عندنا مباح فيه، ليس بسنة ولا مكروه. وكان للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ثلاثة مؤذنين، بلال وأبو محذورة، [ واسمه . سمرة، وابن أم مكتوم واسمه عمرو، فإذا غاب بلال أذن أبو محذورة ] )، وإذا غاب أبو محذورة أذن عمرو
And he repeats the takbir at its end, like the rest of its phrases, and there is no tarji' in the two shahadahs. The meaning is like what preceded, i.e., hurry to salvation and happiness, for prayer is a cause of salvation and happiness, so establish it to be saved from His punishment. Al-falah is: achieving permanence and eternity in bliss. The one who succeeds is called muflih, and everyone who attains good is muflih. The root of the word is from the Arabs' invitation to food: 'Come to the tharid,' i.e., come to eat tharid. And there is no tarji' in the two shahadahs, because the narrations agree that Bilal did not practice tarji', and because the purpose of the adhan is the words 'hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah,' and there is no tarji' in them, so in what is other than them it is even more appropriate. The author of al-Bahr said: The apparent from their statements, i.e., our scholars, is that tarji' is permissible according to us, it is not sunnah nor makruh. The Prophet had three mu'adhdhins: Bilal, Abu Mahdhura, and Ibn Umm Maktum.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the structure of the adhan. It first confirms that the final takbir is repeated twice (tathniya) like the other phrases of the adhan. Then it addresses the issue of tarji' in the shahadatayn: tarji' means lowering the voice in the shahadatayn and then raising it again. The Hanafi position is that tarji' is not part of the authentic adhan because reliable narrations confirm that Bilal did not do it. Moreover, the essential call 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah' already fulfill the purpose of the adhan. The tarji' of Abu Mahdhura is considered a special concession for him, either for teaching purposes or to increase his love after embracing Islam. According to later Hanafi scholars like the author of al-Bahr, tarji' is mubah (permissible) – neither sunnah nor makruh. The passage also notes that the Prophet had three mu'adhdhins, Bilal, Abu Mahdhura, and Ibn Umm Maktum, and they took turns.

Key Terms
ترجيع (tarjī‘): A practice in the adhan where the mu'adhdhin lowers his voice in the shahadatayn and then raises it again.
تثنية (tathniyah): The repetition of the phrases of the adhan twice, except the final takbir which is also repeated.
مُؤذِّن (mu'adhdhin): The person who calls the adhan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on tarji' (lowering then raising the voice) in the shahadatayn of the adhan?
A) It is a sunnah of the adhan.
B) It is haram because it contradicts the practice of Bilal.
C) It is mubah (permissible) but not sunnah.
D) It is wajib.

Key Takeaway
Tarji' in the adhan is not from the sunnah; it is merely permissible (mubah), and the preferred practice follows the example of Bilal without tarji'.

The Iqamah and Its Wording
Explains the iqamah's similarity to adhan and the addition of 'qad qamat al-salah' and Fajr phrase.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling and wording of the iqamah, including the Fajr addition, and explain the evidence for its recommended status.

Core Idea
The iqamah mirrors the adhan; 'qad qamat al-salah' is said twice, and for Fajr, 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' is recommended.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains that the iqamah follows the same structure as the adhan, with the takbir quadrupled and other phrases doubled. It details the addition of 'qad qamat al-salah' and the recommended phrase for Fajr, resolving an intra-Hanafi dispute on the placement of 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The iqamah is a sunnah muakkadah (strongly recommended), not obligatory. The phrase for Fajr is also recommended (nadb).
2
Break down the wording of the iqamah
The takbir is said four times, and all other phrases (including 'qad qamat al-salah') are said twice, as per the hadith of the descending angel.
The phrase 'qad qamat al-salah' is the distinguishing feature of the iqamah.
3
Understand the Fajr addition
After 'hayya 'ala al-falah' in the Fajr adhan, the muadhdhin says 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' twice. This is specific to Fajr because it is a time of sleep and heedlessness.
The proof is the hadith of Bilal.
4
Examine the evidence for recommendation
The Prophet's response 'How beautiful this' and his instruction to 'do it in your adhan' indicate recommendation (nadb) because of the qarina (indication) of approval.
In Hanafi usul, a command with such a qarina indicates recommendation, not obligation.
5
Resolve the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa held the phrase is said after the adhan, while Imam al-Tahawi said it is within the adhan. The relied-upon position is al-Tahawi's, based on practice and hadith of Abu Mahdhurah.
The mufta bihi is that 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' is part of the adhan, said after 'hayya 'ala al-falah'.

(وَ) يزيد (بعدَ فلاحِ الإقامة: قد قامتِ الصَّلاةُ)، ويقولها (مَرَّتين). لما روينا في حديث الملك النازل، ولحديث أبي محذورة، وفيه قال: « علمني رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الإقامة سبع عشرة كلمة ) (). ولأنه المقصود منها، وقد سميت به كما ذكرناه. ولا تكــره إقـامـة غـيـر المؤذن برضاه عندنا، والأفضل أن يكون المقيم هو المؤذن، لما ورد في ذلك من الحديث (۳).
And the iqamah is like it) in quadrupling the takbir at the beginning, and doubling the remaining words and their order, as the descending angel did by mutawatir reports: he called the adhan in twos and the iqamah in twos, and because if they were single, he would have singled out the phrase 'qad qamat al-salah', since it is the origin in both, and it was only called iqamah because of it, naming the whole by part. And Ibrahim al-Nakha'i said: The iqamah was like the adhan until these kings made it single for speed when they leave, meaning the Umayyads. (And the muadhdhin adds) after the falah of Fajr, i.e. after his saying 'hayya 'ala al-falah' (the prayer is better than sleep), and says it (twice) due to the narration that Bilal came to the chamber of Aisha after the adhan and said: The prayer, O Messenger of Allah. She said: The Messenger is asleep. He said: The prayer is better than sleep. When he woke up, she informed him of that, and the Prophet approved it and said: 'Do it in your adhan.' And in the Mu'jam of al-Tabarani from Aisha: Bilal came to the Prophet to inform him of the Fajr prayer and found him asleep, so he said: The prayer is better than sleep, and it was established in the adhan of Fajr. In another narration: The Prophet said: 'How beautiful this is, O Bilal, put it in your adhan.' And it is for recommendation by the indication of his saying 'How beautiful this', and in another narration: 'When you give the adhan for Fajr...' and because it is a time of sleep and heedlessness, so it was specified with increased notification unlike Isha, because sleep before Isha is disliked and rare. Sleep is associated with prayer in goodness because it can be worship when it is a means to attaining obedience or abandoning disobedience, and because it is comfort in this world, and prayer is comfort in the Hereafter, and the comfort of the Hereafter is better. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that his saying: 'The prayer is better than sleep' is after the adhan, not within it, and this is the choice of the eminent Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Bukhari. And Imam al-Tahawi said: The tathwib (the phrase) is within the adhan itself, and this is what is taken. And upon it is the practice of the people, as in al-Mustasfa, due to the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah that the Prophet said: 'When you are in the Fajr prayer, say: The prayer is better than sleep, Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illa Allah.' Narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i. And from Anas: It is from the Sunnah that when the muadhdhin in the Fajr prayer says 'hayya 'ala al-falah', he says 'the prayer is better than sleep' twice. Narrated by al-Daraqutni, and the saying of a companion 'from the Sunnah' its ruling is marfu' according to the correct view, and due to continuous practice from the time of the Prophet until today. Custom and habit are what have settled in souls from intellectual matters and sound natures accepted them. The Prophet was asked about the yeast that neighbors use, and he said: 'What Muslims see as good is good with Allah.' (And) he adds (after the falah of the iqamah: qad qamat al-salah), and says it (twice). Due to what we narrated in the hadith of the descending angel, and the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah in which he said: 'The Messenger of Allah taught me the iqamah as seventeen words.' And because it is the purpose of it, and it was named for it as we mentioned. And it is not disliked for someone other than the muadhdhin to give the iqamah with his permission according to us, and it is better that the one giving the iqamah is the muadhdhin, due to the hadith reported about that.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the iqamah (second call to prayer). It states that the iqamah is similar to the adhan in structure: the takbir is said four times, and the other phrases are said twice, following the practice of the angel who came down (in the hadith of 'Abd Allah ibn Zayd). The phrase 'qad qamat al-salah' is said twice, and it is the distinguishing feature of the iqamah, named after it. The author mentions a historical note from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that the iqamah was originally like the adhan, but the Umayyad rulers shortened it for speed. For Fajr, the phrase 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' is added after 'hayya 'ala al-falah', said twice. This is established by the hadith of Bilal, where the Prophet approved the phrase and instructed it to be used in the Fajr adhan. The ruling is recommended (nadb), not obligatory, as indicated by the Prophet's words 'How beautiful this'. There is a difference of opinion on whether this phrase is said within the adhan or after it: Abu Hanifa reportedly said it is after the adhan, while Imam al-Tahawi said it is within the adhan, and the latter is the practiced view. The passage then returns to the iqamah, confirming that 'qad qamat al-salah' is said twice, supported by hadith. Finally, it rules that it is not disliked for someone other than the muadhdhin to give the iqamah with his permission, though it is preferable that the muadhdhin does it himself.

Key Terms
إقامة (iqamah): The second call to prayer, which signals the immediate commencement of the congregational prayer.
تثويب (tathwib): The phrase 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' in the Fajr adhan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Once
B) Twice
C) Three times
D) Four times

Key Takeaway
The iqamah is a sunnah with specific wording; the Fajr addition is recommended, and the mufta bihi places it within the adhan.

Virtues of the Adhan and the Muadhdhin
Narrates hadiths encouraging the adhan and its performer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state at least three hadithic rewards for the muadhdhin and explain the Hanafi-preferred interpretation of 'atwalu a'naqan'.

Core Idea
A muadhdhin receives immense rewards: testimony of creation, forgiveness matching his voice, and a distinguished rank on Judgment Day.

This passage is a tanbih (note) that gathers multiple authentic hadiths to encourage the call to prayer. While adhan is a confirmed sunnah, the focus here is on the extraordinary merits that motivate both the caller and the listener. Understanding these rewards deepens one's appreciation for this sacred act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the passage structure
The passage begins as a tanbih (note) and then lists a series of hadiths from various sources (Bukhari, Muslim, Ahmad, etc.) about the virtues of adhan and the muadhdhin.
Note the chain of narrations and the variety of rewards mentioned.
2
List the rewards for the muadhdhin
Extract each distinct reward: (1) everything that hears him testifies for him; (2) people would compete for the call if they knew; (3) forgiveness for the extent of his voice; (4) he gets the reward of all who pray with him; (5) Allah's hand is over his head; (6) he will emerge from his grave calling adhan; (7) he will have the longest necks; (8) he is among the three on mounds of musk.
These rewards are not legal obligations but motivation (targhib).
3
Examine the interpretation of 'longest necks'
The text provides several interpretations from 'al-Bahr': (a) longest in hope of followers; (b) most followers; (c) necks long so sweat does not cover them; (d) fastest in walking (from 'i'naq'). The Hanafi-preferred view is having more followers or being swift to Paradise.
The linguistic discussion shows how scholars derive meaning from ambiguous phrases.
4
Recognize the purpose of the passage
This passage is purely encouragement (targhib) to perform the sunnah of adhan and to value the muadhdhin. It does not establish new legal rulings; rather, it reinforces the high status of the adhan.
Do not confuse rewards with obligations; adhan remains a highly recommended sunnah.
5
Distinguish between reward and ruling
Although the rewards are immense, adhan is not obligatory (fard). The hadiths are from ahad sources (zanni al-thubut), so they confirm merit, not legal compulsion. The ruling of adhan is sunnah mu'akkadah, established elsewhere.
This lesson focuses on fadl (virtue), not on fiqh rulings of validity or conditions.

A note to explain the virtue of its performer. He said: 'Nothing hears the range of the voice of the muadhdhin, whether jinn, human, or anything, except that it will testify for him on the Day of Judgment.' Narrated by al-Bukhari. And Imam Ahmad narrated from him: 'If people knew what is in the call, they would fight over it with swords.' And he narrated with a sound chain: 'Forgiveness is granted to the muadhdhin as far as his voice reaches, and every moist and dry thing that hears him asks forgiveness for him.' Narrated by al-Bazzar, except that he said: 'And every moist and dry responds to him.' And in al-Nasa'i: 'He has the reward of those who pray with him.' And from al-Tabarani in al-Awsat: 'The hand of the Merciful is over the head of the muadhdhin, and indeed forgiveness is granted to him as far as his voice reaches.' And in it: 'The muadhdhinun and those who say labbayk will come out of their graves, the muadhdhin calling the adhan and the one saying labbayk saying labbayk.' And from Muslim: 'The muadhdhinun will have the longest necks on the Day of Judgment.' And from Imam Ahmad and al-Tirmidhi from Ibn Umar, raising it: 'Three persons are on mounds of musk - I think he said on the Day of Judgment - the earlier and later generations will envy them: a slave who fulfilled the rights of Allah and his masters, a man who led a people and they were pleased with him, and a man who calls the five prayers every day and night.' And he said: 'Three persons will not be terrified by the greatest fright, nor will they be subjected to the reckoning, and they are on a sand dune of musk until the reckoning of the creatures is completed: a man who recited the Quran seeking the face of Allah, a caller who calls to Allah seeking the face of Allah, and a slave who did well in what is between him and his Lord and between him and his masters, and a man who led a people and they were pleased with him.' So said al-Kamal. And his saying 'longest necks' is interpreted as: longest in hope of followers; or most followers; or their necks will be long so that sweat will not cover them; or they will be the fastest in walking. As in al-Bahr.

Commentary
This passage is a 'tanbih' (note) highlighting the tremendous virtues of the adhan and the muadhdhin. The compiler gathers multiple authentic hadiths showing the immense reward. First, the muadhdhin's voice will testify for him. Second, people would compete for it if they knew. Third, everything that hears him asks forgiveness for him. Fourth, he has the reward of all who pray with him. Fifth, Allah's mercy is over his head. Sixth, muadhdhinun will emerge from graves calling adhan. Seventh, they will have the longest necks (interpreted as most followers or distinguished). Also includes hadith about three categories on musk: the muadhdhin among them. The commentary ends with linguistic explanations of 'longest necks' from al-Bahr. This section is purely for encouragement (targhib) and does not add new legal rulings.

Key Terms
أطول أعناقاً (atwalu a'naqan): Literally 'longest necks'; interpreted as having more followers, being distinguished, or being saved from sweat of Judgment Day.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The adhan carries extraordinary rewards for the muadhdhin, motivating both performer and listener, though the act itself remains a sunnah, not an obligation.

Turning Face and Standing Still During the Adhan
Rulings on turning face and standing still during adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on turning the face and keeping the feet still during adhan, and identify the dalil for each.

Core Idea
Turning the face is sunnah; keeping the feet still is wajib—both proven by the practice of Bilal and a direct command.

In this passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah, we learn two important etiquettes for the mu'adhdhin: turning the face right and left during the adhan, and not moving the feet. The author provides proof from the practice of Bilal (RA) and a hadith from al-Daraqutni. We'll distinguish between sunnah and wajib, and see how istidarah (turning around) is permitted when necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage presents two rulings: (a) turning the face to the right for 'hayya ala al-salah' and left for 'hayya ala al-falah', and (b) not moving the feet during the adhan/iqamah.
The first is sunnah, the second is wajib.
2
Trace the dalil for turning the face
The proof is the practice of Bilal (RA) who turned his face without turning his body. The author states this has become a sunnah of the adhan.
Al-Halwani disagreed if alone, but the correct view is that it remains sunnah.
3
Trace the dalil for not moving the feet
The hadith from al-Daraqutni: the Prophet (SAWS) commanded not to move the feet. In Hanafi usul, an imperative indicates wujub (obligation) unless there is a contrary indication.
This hadith is zanni in both transmission and meaning, but sufficient for wujub in the madhhab.
4
Understand the exception for istidarah
If turning the face alone does not make the call reach all directions (e.g., in a minaret), the mu'adhdhin may turn his whole body around (istidarah) to achieve completeness.
This is a permissible means, not the normal practice. Historically, there were no minarets in the Prophet's time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَنْ يُحَوِّلَ وَجْهَهُ يَمِينًا بِالصَّلَاةِ، وَيَسَارًا بِالْفَلَاحِ. لِأَنَّ بِلَالًا رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ لَمَّا بَلَغَ حَيَّ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ حَيَّ عَلَى الْفَلَاحِ حَوَّلَ وَجْهَهُ يَمِينًا وَشِمَالًا وَلَمْ يَسْتَدِرْ. وَيُحَوِّلُ وَلَوْ كَانَ وَحْدَهُ فِي الصَّحِيحِ، لِأَنَّهُ صَارَ سُنَّةَ الْأَذَانِ. وَقَالَ الْحَلْوَانِيُّ: إِذَا كَانَ وَحْدَهُ لَا يُحَوِّلُ. وَكَيْفِيَّتُهُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الصَّلَاةُ فِي الْيَمِينِ وَالْفَلَاحُ فِي الْيَسَارِ. وَلَا يُحَوِّلُ وَرَاءَهُ، وَلَا أَمَامَهُ. وَلَا يُزِيلُ قَدَمَيْهِ، لِمَا رَوَاهُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيُّ عَنْ بِلَالٍ قَالَ: أَمَرَنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ إِذَا أَذَّنَّا أَوْ أَقَمْنَا أَنْ لَا نُزِيلَ أَقْدَامَنَا عَنْ مَوَاضِعِهَا. وَيَسْتَدِيرُ فِي صَوْمَعَتِهِ، يَعْنِي: إِنْ لَمْ يَتِمَّ الْإِعْلَامُ بِتَحْوِيلِ وَجْهِهِ مَعَ ثَبَاتِ قَدَمِهِ، فَإِنَّهُ يَسْتَدِيرُ فِي الْمِئْذَنَةِ، لِيَحْصُلَ التَّمَامُ. وَالصَّوْمَعَةُ: الْمَنَارَةُ. وَلَمْ يَكُنْ فِي زَمَنِهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مِئْذَنَةٌ، وَكَانَ بِلَالٌ يَأْتِي سَحَرًا لِأَطْوَلِ بَيْتٍ حَوْلَ الْمَسْجِدِ لِامْرَأَةٍ مِنْ بَنِي النَّجَّارِ، فَيَجْلِسُ عَلَيْهِ، يَنْظُرُ إِلَى الْفَجْرِ، فَإِذَا رَآهُ أَذَّنَ.
And that he turns his face to the right during 'al-salah' and to the left during 'al-falah'. Because Bilal, may Allah be pleased with him, when he reached 'hayya ala al-salah, hayya ala al-falah', turned his face right and left, and did not turn around completely. And he turns even if he is alone according to the correct [view], because it has become a sunnah of the adhan. Al-Halwani said: when he is alone, he does not turn. Its manner is that 'al-salah' is on the right and 'al-falah' on the left. He does not turn behind him nor in front of him. And he does not move his feet, because of what al-Daraqutni narrated from Bilal: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, commanded us when we called the adhan or iqamah not to move our feet from their places.' And he turns around in his minaret, meaning: if the announcement is not complete by turning his face while his feet are fixed, then he turns around in the minaret to achieve completeness. 'Al-Sawma'ah' is the minaret. There was no minaret in his time, peace be upon him, and Bilal used to come at dawn to the tallest house around the mosque belonging to a woman from Banu al-Najjar, and sit on it, looking for the dawn, and when he saw it, he called the adhan.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah discusses the recommended actions for the mu'adhdhin regarding turning his face and staying still during the adhan. It is a ruling with proof (ruling_with_proof). The author begins by stating the ruling: the mu'adhdhin should turn his face to the right when saying 'hayya ala al-salah' and to the left when saying 'hayya ala al-falah'. The proof is the practice of Bilal (RA), who did not turn his entire body but only his face. The author notes that this is sunnah even if he is alone, though al-Halwani held that it is not required when alone. The manner is that 'al-salah' is on the right side and 'al-falah' on the left. He should not turn his back to the qibla nor face it completely forward. He also should not move his feet from their place, based on a hadith from al-Daraqutni where the Prophet (SAWS) commanded Bilal and others not to move their feet during adhan or iqamah. If the announcement is not sufficiently achieved by turning the face alone, such as in a minaret, the mu'adhdhin may turn his entire body around in the minaret to reach all directions. This is called istidarah. The author mentions that there were no minarets in the Prophet's time; Bilal used to climb a tall house. The Hanafi ruling is that turning face is sunnah, not moving feet is wajib (as per the hadith), and turning in the minaret is a means to complete the announcement.

Key Terms
تحويل الوجه (tahwil al-wajh): Turning the face to the right for 'hayya ala al-salah' and left for 'hayya ala al-falah' during adhan.
استدارة (istidarah): Turning the whole body around in the minaret to ensure announcement reaches all directions.
صومعة (sawma'ah): Minaret or high place from which adhan is called.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Wajib to keep feet still
C) Mubah to move or not
D) Haram to move

Key Takeaway
Turning the face during adhan is an emphasized sunnah; not moving the feet is a wajib based on a direct command.

Separation Between Adhan and Iqamah
Rulings on the interval between adhan and iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the interval between adhan and iqamah, identify its proof from the hadith, and apply the exceptions for maghrib and for a person in need.

Core Idea
The interval is sunnah, flexible in duration, with exceptions for maghrib and for those in haste.

After calling the adhan, the mu'adhdin should wait before giving the iqamah. This interval allows people to prepare for prayer. But how long should it be? The Hanafi school provides guidelines based on the sunnah and practical needs. Let's explore the ruling, its proof, and the special cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the first line: 'وَ يَفْصِلُ بَيْنَ الْأَذَانِ وَالْإِقَامَةِ'. This is the obligation to separate. Determine the hukm level: is it fard, wajib, or sunnah?
The author uses the imperative form, but the context and further details indicate it is sunnah, not obligatory.
2
Analyze the general separation
The text says the interval should be enough for regular attenders to come, while observing the preferred time. This shows flexibility.
The phrase 'مَعَ مُرَاعَاةِ الْوَقْتِ الْمُسْتَحَبِّ' means one must not delay beyond the preferred time.
3
Examine the maghrib exception
For maghrib, the separation is a short pause – the length of three short verses or three steps. Why such a short time? Because the time for maghrib is short.
This is based on the necessity to pray maghrib early.
4
Review the hadith proof
The author cites the Prophet's instruction to Bilal: 'Make between your adhan and iqamah the amount of time for the eater to finish his meal.' This indicates a general leniency, not a fixed time.
The command 'اجعل' is for desirability, not obligation.
5
Apply the exception for a needy person
If it is known that a weak or hurried person is waiting, the iqamah should be given for him, not delayed for a prominent person. This prioritizes the need of the individual.
This shows the Hanafi consideration of actual circumstances over rigid custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَفْصِلُ بَيْنَ الْأَذَانِ وَالْإِقَامَةِ بِقَدْرِ مَا يَحْضُرُ الْمُلَازِمُونَ لِلصَّلَاةِ مَعَ مُرَاعَاةِ الْوَقْتِ الْمُسْتَحَبِّ. وَفِي الْمَغْرِبِ بِسَكْتَةٍ قَدْرَ قِرَاءَةِ ثَلَاثِ آيَاتٍ قِصَارٍ، أَوْ قَدْرَ مَا يَخْطُو ثَلَاثَ خَطَوَاتٍ. لِمَا رُوِيَ مِنْ قَوْلِهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لِبِلَالٍ: وَاجْعَلْ بَيْنَ أَذَانِكَ وَإِقَامَتِكَ قَدْرَ مَا يَفْرُغُ الْآكِلُ مِنْ أَكْلِهِ. فَإِنْ عُلِمَ بِضَعِيفٍ مُسْتَعْجِلٍ أُقِيمَ لَهُ، وَلَا يُنْتَظَرُ رَئِيسُ الْمَحَلَّةِ.
And he separates between the adhan and the iqamah by an amount sufficient for those who are regular to attend, while observing the preferred time. And in maghrib, by a pause of the length of reciting three short verses, or three steps. Because of what was narrated from the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him, to Bilal: 'Make between your adhan and iqamah the amount of time for the eater to finish his meal.' If it is known that there is a weak person who is in a hurry, the iqamah is made for him, and the head of the district is not waited for.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage expands on the ruling of the interval (fasl) between adhan and iqamah. The default ruling is that connecting them without a gap is makruh. The author states that the separation should be long enough for those who are regular in prayer to attend. However, one must also observe the preferred time for prayer (e.g., not delaying until dislikable time). For maghrib prayer, the separation is only a short pause, about the time to recite three short verses or take three steps, because the time for maghrib is short. The proof is the hadith where the Prophet (SAWS) instructed Bilal to allow enough time for a person to finish eating. The author then adds a nuance: if it is known that a weak or hurried person is waiting, the iqamah should be given promptly for him, not delayed for a prominent person (sayyid al-mahallah). This is based on consideration of need. The Hanafi position is that the fasl is sunnah, not obligatory, but should be observed as per the hadith.

Key Terms
الفصل (alfasl): The interval between adhan and iqamah.
سكتة (saktah): A short pause; specifically in maghrib a brief silence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it is a short prayer
B) Because the time for maghrib is short
C) Because people are in a hurry
D) Because it is sunnah to be quick

Key Takeaway
The interval between adhan and iqamah is a sunnah that is flexible in duration, with exceptions for maghrib (short pause) and for accommodating a needy person promptly.

Tathwib: The Call After Adhan
Ruling on tathwib with proof by istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on tathwib, including its basis in istihsan, its timing, and the flexibility of its wording according to local custom.

Core Idea
Tathwib is a later Hanafi practice justified by istihsan, not a sunnah from the Prophet.

In this lesson, we examine tathwib — an additional call after the adhan that urges people to prayer. The passage distinguishes between the old tathwib (specific to Fajr) and the new one adopted by later Hanafi scholars. Understanding the role of istihsan and the authority of Qadi Khan will help you grasp how the school accommodates communal needs while preserving continuity with established practice.

Guided Path
1
Define tathwib linguistically and technically
Identify the root meaning (return) and how it applies to making a second announcement after the adhan.
Note the connection to 'thawab' (reward).
2
Differentiate old and new tathwib
The old tathwib ('al-salahu khayrun min al-nawm') was only for Fajr. The new one ('hayya ala al-salah...') was introduced later for all prayers.
The new tathwib is the subject of this ruling.
3
Analyze the justification using istihsan
Later scholars adopted it due to prevalent negligence. This is a case of istihsan overriding the original limitation to Fajr.
İstihsan is a key Hanafi tool for balancing textual evidence and public interest.
4
Determine the timing: after adhan or after iqamah?
Review the intra-Hanafi dispute. Qadi Khan holds it is after adhan; the author agrees. Some hold it after both.
The reasoning: 'return to announcement' implies after the first announcement ends.
5
Note the flexibility in wording
The exact phrasing is not fixed; each locality follows its custom (e.g., 'al-salah, al-salah, ya musalleen'). The mu'adhdhin himself performs it.
This reflects Hanafi accommodation of 'urf (custom).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُثَوِّبُ. التَّثْوِيبُ لُغَةً: الْعَوْدُ، وَمِنْهُ الثَّوَابُ. وَهُوَ هُنَا الْعَوْدُ إِلَى الْإِعْلَامِ بَعْدَ الْإِعْلَامِ الْأَوَّلِ. وَيُثَوِّبُ بَعْدَ الْأَذَانِ فِي جَمِيعِ الْأَوْقَاتِ، اسْتَحْسَنَهُ الْمُتَأَخِّرُونَ، لِظُهُورِ التَّوَانِي فِي الْأُمُورِ الدِّينِيَّةِ، فَزِيدَ لِلْمُبَالَغَةِ فِي الْإِعْلَامِ لِجَمِيعِ النَّاسِ. وَهَذَا هُوَ التَّثْوِيبُ الْحَادِثُ، وَالْقَدِيمُ: الصَّلَاةُ خَيْرٌ مِنَ النَّوْمِ مَرَّتَيْنِ، وَكَانَ فِي أَذَانِ الْفَجْرِ بَعْدَ الْفَلَاحِ. فَأَحْدَثَ النَّاسُ هَذَا التَّثْوِيبَ: حَيَّ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ، حَيَّ عَلَى الْفَلَاحِ مَرَّتَيْنِ، بَعْدَ الْأَذَانِ وَالْإِقَامَةِ. وَهُوَ اخْتِيَارُ عُلَمَاءِ الْكُوفَةِ. وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ قَاضِي خَانْ: الْأَصَحُّ أَنَّهُ بَعْدَ الْأَذَانِ، لِأَنَّهُ مَأْخُوذٌ مِنَ الرُّجُوعِ وَالْعَوْدِ إِلَى الْإِعْلَامِ، وَذَلِكَ إِنَّمَا يَكُونُ بَعْدَ الْفَرَاغِ. وَتَثْوِيبُ كُلِّ بَلَدٍ عَلَى مَا تَعَارَفَ أَهْلُهَا. كَقَوْلِهِ: الصَّلَاةَ، الصَّلَاةَ، يَا مُصَلِّينَ، قُومُوا إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ. وَقَيَّدَ بِكَوْنِ الْمُثَوِّبِ هُوَ الْمُؤَذِّنُ.
And he performs tathwib. Tathwib linguistically means returning, and from it comes 'thawab' (reward). It here means returning to the announcement after the first announcement. And he performs tathwib after the adhan in all times; the later scholars deemed it good (istihsan), due to the prevalence of negligence in religious matters, so it was added for emphasis in announcing to all people. This is the new tathwib. The old one was 'al-salahu khayrun mina al-nawm' twice, and it was in the adhan of fajr after 'al-falah'. The people introduced this tathwib: 'Hayya ala al-salah, hayya ala al-falah' twice, after the adhan and iqamah. This is the choice of the Kufan scholars. Imam Qadi Khan said: the most correct is that it is after the adhan, because it is derived from returning and coming back to the announcement, and that is only after completion. And the tathwib of each town is according to the custom of its people. Like his saying: 'al-salah, al-salah, O people of prayer, stand up for prayer.' And it is restricted that the one who performs tathwib is the mu'adhdhin.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage discusses tathwib, which is an additional call after the adhan to urge people to prayer. It is a ruling with proof (ruling_with_proof) and an expansion of the matn. Linguistically, tathwib means to return, and here it means returning to announce again. The later Hanafi scholars (mutakkhirin) adopted istihsan to perform tathwib after every adhan because people had become lazy. Historically, there was an old tathwib specific to fajr: 'al-salahu khayrun mina al-nawm' after 'hayya ala al-falah'. Later, people introduced a new tathwib saying 'hayya ala al-salah, hayya ala al-falah' twice after the adhan and iqamah. This was the choice of Kufan scholars. Imam Qadi Khan stated the most correct view that tathwib is after the adhan (not after iqamah) because it is a return to announcement after finishing the first one. Importantly, the exact wording is not fixed; each locality follows its custom, such as saying 'al-salah, al-salah, ya musalleen.' The one who performs tathwib should be the mu'adhdhin himself. This shows flexibility in the Hanafi school regarding the form of tathwib.

Key Terms
التثويب (al-tathwib): An additional call after the adhan urging people to prayer; literally 'returning' to announcement.
استحسان (istihsan): A juristic preference based on need and custom, overriding strict qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is tathwib performed?
A) Only in the fajr adhan
B) After the adhan in all prayers
C) Before the iqamah only
D) It is not performed at all

Key Takeaway
Tathwib is a recommended Hanafi practice after every adhan, justified by istihsan, with wording determined by local custom.

The Recommended Acts After Adhan: Turning, Pause, and Tathwib
Explaining three recommended acts after adhan with evidence and variations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunnah acts after the adhan according to the Hanafi school and explain the evidence and details for each.

Core Idea
Three sunnah acts after adhan: turning, pausing, and tathwib – each rooted in prophetic practice and later custom.

This lesson covers the sunnah acts that follow the adhan: turning in the minaret, pausing between adhan and iqamah, and performing tathwib. These practices are recommended (mustahabb) in the Hanafi school, with specific details for Maghrib and differences among mujtahids. Understanding these sunnan completes the picture of the adhan as a call that not only announces time but also maximizes congregation readiness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three recommended acts
Read the passage and list the three actions: 1) turning in the minaret (istidarah), 2) pausing between adhan and iqamah (fasl), 3) performing tathwib (a second call after the adhan). These are sunnah/mustahabb according to the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the evidence for the pause
The passage cites the Prophet's ﷺ instruction to Bilal: 'Place between your adhan and iqamah the amount that the eater finishes his eating.' Recognize that this hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and the imperative is interpreted as recommendation (nadb) due to other evidence.
3
Note the specific rule for Maghrib
For Maghrib the pause is shorter: the length of reciting three short verses or taking three steps. This is because Maghrib time is brief and people are near the mosque breaking fast.
4
Distinguish tathwib: earlier vs later practice
Tathwib originally was only in Fajr ('al-salat khayrun min al-nawm'). Later scholars added 'hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah' after every adhan due to laziness. The wording can vary by local custom.
5
Apply the rulings in a modern context
Consider how a mu'adhdhin today would implement these: turn in the minaret (or move the microphone head), pause appropriately (especially for Maghrib), and add tathwib after the adhan in all prayers. Note that the mu'adhdhin himself should say it.
The text prefers not to turn for iqamah (al-Siraj's view).

Source Text

ويستدير في صَوْمَعَتِهِ، ويَفْصل بين الأذان والإقامةِ بِقَدْرِ ما يحضُرُ الملازمونَ للصَّلاة؛ مع مراعاة الـ مستحب، وفي المغرب بسكتةٍ قَدْرَ قراءة ثلاث آيات قصار، أو ثلاث خطواتٍ، ويُثَوِّبُ. كقوله - بعد الأذان: الصَّلاةَ، الصَّلاةَ، يا مُصلَّينَ.

(ويُثَوِّبُ)، التثويب لغة: العود، ومنه الثواب، لأن منفعة عمله تعود إليه، والمثابة، ﴿وَإِذْ جَعَلْنَا الْبَيْتَ مَثَابَةً لِلنَّاسِ﴾ لأن الناس يعودون إليه، وسمّيتِ المرأة ثيباً، لأنها ترجع إلى أهلها بوجه غير الأول، وهو هنا العود إلى الإعلام، بعد الإعلام الأول. ويثـوب بـعـد الأذان في جميع الأوقات، استحسنه المتأخرون، لظهور التواني في الأمور الدينية، وقلما يقومون عند سماع الأذان، فزيد للمبالغة في الإعلام لجميع الناس لا يختص به أحد. ولذا أطلقنا، وهـذا هـو التثويب الحادث والقديم، الصلاة خير من النوم مرتين، وكان في أذان الفجر بعد الفلاح كمـا ذكـر نــاه، فأحدث الناس هذا التثويب حي على الصلاة، حي على الفلاح مرتين، بعد الأذان والإقامة. وهـو اختيــار عـلـمـاء الكوفة، وهو حسن. وقال الإمام قاضي خان: الأصح أنه بعد الأذان، لأنه مأخوذ من الرجوع والعود إلى الإعلام، وذلك إنما يكون بعد الفراغ، وتثويب كل بلد على ما تعارف أهلها، (كَقَوْلِهِ) أي المؤذن بَعْدِ الأذان: الصَّلاةَ الصَّلاةَ، يا مُصلّينَ)، قوموا إلى الصلاة، وقيد بكون المثـوب هـو المؤذن،
He turns around in his minaret, and separates between the adhan and the iqamah by the amount that the regular attendees of the prayer can attend, while observing the preferred time, and in Maghrib with a pause of the length of reciting three short verses, or three steps, and he performs tathwib. Such as his saying after the adhan: 'The prayer, the prayer, O worshippers.' In al-Qunyah: He turns also for the iqamah. In al-Siraj: He does not turn in it, because it is for informing the present, unlike the adhan which informs the absent. And it is said: He turns if the place is spacious. (He turns around in his minaret) means: if the information is not completed by turning his face while his feet are fixed, then he turns around in the minaret to achieve completeness. And al-sawma'ah is the minaret, originally the monk's cell, as mentioned by al-Ayni. There was no minaret in the time of the Prophet ﷺ; Bilal used to come at dawn to the tallest house around the mosque belonging to a woman from Banu al-Najjar, sit on it, watch the dawn, and when he saw it he called the adhan. (And he separates between the adhan and the iqamah) because connecting them is makruh. (By the amount that the regular attendees come) due to what we narrated from the Prophet's ﷺ saying to Bilal: 'Place between your adhan and your iqamah the amount that the eater finishes his eating.' Hadith. If he knows of a weak and hasty person, he establishes for him, and does not wait for the leader of the neighborhood. So in al-Fath. Al-Wabra was asked: The mu'adhdhin waits for an evil person for breaking his evils, and there is ample time, so he said: I consider the most beneficial, and he is excused. Abu Dharr said: He delays. (While observing the preferred time) because it is not permissible to delay into the disliked time. (And he separates between the adhan and the iqamah in Maghrib with a pause) that is the length of reciting three short verses, or one long verse, as in Jami' Qadi Khan and al-Timurtashi from the Imam, or as also narrated from him: the amount of three steps or four. So in al-Fath. (And he performs tathwib). Tathwib linguistically means returning, hence al-thawab (reward), because the benefit of his action returns to him, and al-mathabah (place of return). And the woman is called thayyib because she returns to her family with a different face than the first. Here it means returning to the call after the first call. And he performs tathwib after the adhan in all times; the later scholars considered it good due to the apparent laziness in religious matters, and they rarely stand up upon hearing the adhan, so it was added for emphasis in informing all people, not specific to anyone. Hence we have generalised. And this is the later and earlier tathwib: 'al-salat khayrun min al-nawm' twice. It was in the Fajr adhan after 'al-falah' as mentioned by [؟], so people invented this tathwib 'hayya 'ala al-salah, hayya 'ala al-falah' twice after the adhan and iqamah. This is the choice of the Kufan scholars, and it is good. Imam Qadi Khan said: The correct is that it is after the adhan, because it is derived from returning and coming back to the call, and that is only after finishing. The tathwib of each land follows the custom of its people. (Such as his saying, i.e., the mu'adhdhin after the adhan: 'The prayer, the prayer, O worshippers,' 'stand up for the prayer,' with the condition that the one doing tathwib is the mu'adhdhin.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the recommended actions (sunan) of the mu'adhdhin after completing the adhan. The author first discusses the practice of turning (istidarah) in the minaret to ensure the call reaches all directions. He notes that this was not done in the Prophet's time but became necessary as mosques grew. The key ruling is that there must be a pause (fasl) between the adhan and iqamah, based on the Prophet's instruction to Bilal to allow enough time for people to finish eating. For Maghrib, the pause is brief—about the length of reciting three short verses or taking three steps. The text then addresses tathwib, which is a second call after the adhan to alert the negligent. The author explains its linguistic root (returning) and traces its development: the original tathwib in Fajr was 'al-salat khayrun min al-nawm' (prayer is better than sleep), while later scholars added 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah' to rouse people. Importantly, tathwib is a recommended practice (mustahabb) according to later Hanafi authorities, and its wording can vary by local custom. The mu'adhdhin should say 'al-salat, al-salat, ya musalleen' after the adhan. The passage also notes an intra-Hanafi difference: some scholars hold that the mu'adhdhin should turn for the iqamah, others disagree, but the preferred view is not to turn because iqamah is for those already present.

Key Terms
التثويب (al-tathwib): Linguistically means returning; here it refers to a second call after the adhan to alert the negligent, such as saying 'الصلاة الصلاة يا مصلين' or 'حي على الصلاة حي على الفلاح'.
الصومعة (al-sawma'ah): The minaret (manarah) from which the adhan is called; originally a monk's cell.
الفصل (al-fasl): The separation or pause between the adhan and iqamah, recommended to allow people to come.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The length of reciting three short verses or taking three steps.
B) A pause long enough for someone to eat a full meal.
C) No pause is recommended; the adhan and iqamah should be connected.
D) A pause equal to the time it takes to recite Surah al-Fatiha.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends three acts after adhan: turning, pausing, and tathwib, based on prophetic instruction and later practice to ensure effective congregation.

The Prohibition of Talhin in Adhan and Quran
Explanation of the definition and ruling of talhin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of talhin, explain why it is haram in adhan and Quran, and distinguish it from permissible beautification of the voice.

Core Idea
Talhin — altering the words of adhan through melody — is haram; beautification without distortion is commendable.

The adhan is a sacred call to prayer, and it must be delivered with clarity and respect. This lesson explores the prohibition of talhin (melodic chanting) in adhan and Quran, distinguishing it from the desirable act of beautifying one's voice without altering the words. The source passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah defines talhin, presents its ruling, and gives guidance on proper recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its linguistic roots
The passage defines talhin as التطريب والترنم (singing and melodiousness). It contrasts it with lahn (اللحن), which means intelligence or grammatical error. Note that talhin here is a specific type of melodic alteration.
Lahn can also mean error in grammar, but talhin is the act of making melodic changes.
2
Extract the precise meaning in this context
Talhin is defined as التغني الذي يؤدي إلى تغيير كلمات الأذان (singing that leads to changing the words of the adhan) by altering vowels, consonants, omitting letters, or adding them. This goes beyond mere beautification.
Any change to the prescribed wording due to melody constitutes talhin.
3
State the ruling
The text explicitly says: 'إنه لا يحل فيه ولا في قراءة القرآن، ولا يحل سماعه' — it is not halal (i.e., haram) in adhan or Quran recitation, and listening to it is also haram. The reason given is resemblance to the actions of sinners (الفسقة).
The ruling is consistent across both adhan and Quran recitation.
4
Distinguish from permissible beautification
Beautifying the voice (تحسين الصوت) is desirable (مطلوب). The passage clarifies that there is no necessary connection between beautification and talhin or grammatical error. Inserting elongation (مد) in the hay'alah phrases is specifically allowed by Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani.
Grammatical error (الخطأ في الإعراب) in adhan words is disliked (مكروه), but not as severe as talhin.

(ويُكْرَهُ التَّلحينُ)، وهو التطريب والترنم يقال: لحن في قراءته تلحيناً، طرب فيها و ترنم. وأما اللَّحَنُ فهو : الفطنة والفهم، لما لا يفطن له غيره. ومنه الحديث: «لَعَلَّ بَعْضَكُمْ الْحَنُ بِحُجَّتِهِ مِنْ بَعْض»، واللَّحْن أيضاً : الخطأ في الإعراب، والتلحين التخطئة، والمراد هنا: التغني، بحيث يؤدي إلى تغيير كلمات الأذان وكيفيتها بالحركات والسكنات، ونقص بعض حروفها، أو زيادة فيها. وإنه لا يحل فيه ولا في قراءة القرآن، ولا يحل سماعه، ولأن فيه تشبهاً بفعل الفسقة في حال فسقهم بالتغني، وكذا يكره الخطأ في الإعراب في كلمات الأذان، وأما تحسين الصوت فهو مطلوب، ولا تلازم بينه وبين الخطأ والتلحين، وقيده شمس الأئمة الحلواني، بأن هذا في الأذكار، فأما إدخال المد في الحيعلتين فلا بأس به. (وَ) يكره (إقامةُ المُحْدِثِ، وأذانُهُ)؛ لما رويـنـا مـن قوله : « لا يُؤذِّنُ إلا متوضئ» ولما فيه من الدعاء إلى ما لا يجيب بنفسه، واتبعت هذه الرواية لموافقتها لنص الحديث، وإن صححت الرواية الثانية بعدم كراهة أذان المحدث؛ لأنهم فرقوا بين كراهة أذان الجنب، وعدم كراهة أذان المحدث على الرواية الثانية، بأن للأذان شبهاً بالصلاة، من حيث أن كل واحد منهما يشترط له دخول الوقت، واستقبال القبلة، وشبهاً بغيرها من حيث الحقيقة، فيشترط الطهارة عن أغلظ الحدثين دون أخفهما عملاً بالشبهين. انتهى. وذلك تعليل في مقابلة النص. (و) يكره أذانُ الجُنُبِ كإقامته، رواية واحدة، لما ذكرنا، (وَ) يـكـره، بل لا يصح أذان ( صبي لا يعقل ) لما قدمنا في شروطه، ولما روينا: «ليُؤَذَنَ لَكُمْ خِيَارُكُمْ، ولأن صوته كصوت الطيور. وقيل: يكره أذان الذي يعقل أيضاً، لما روينا، وقيل: البالغ أولى. And disliked is talhin (melodic chanting), and the iqamah of the one in minor impurity, and his adhan, and the adhan of the junub, and a child who does not understand, and an insane person, and a drunkard, and a woman; because it is not fitting for anyone to say to someone above him in knowledge and status that the prayer time has come, except the mu'adhdhin, because that is self-preference. And disliked is talhin, which is singing and melodiousness. It is said: he used talhin in his recitation, i.e., sang and melodized. As for lahn, it is intelligence and understanding of what others do not perceive. From it is the hadith: 'Perhaps one of you is more eloquent in his argument than another.' Lahn also means error in grammar, and talhin means making an error. What is meant here is singing that leads to changing the words of the adhan and their form by movements and pauses, and omitting some letters or adding to them. It is not permissible in it nor in Quran recitation, nor is it permissible to listen to it, because it resembles the actions of sinners in their sinfulness by singing. Likewise, error in grammar in the words of the adhan is disliked. As for beautifying the voice, it is desirable, and there is no necessary connection between it and error and talhin. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani restricted this to dhikr, but inserting elongation in the two phrase 'hayya 'alas' is fine. And disliked is the iqamah of the one in minor impurity and his adhan; due to what we narrated from his saying: 'None should call the adhan except one with wudu.' And because there is in it a call to what he himself does not answer. This narration was followed because it agrees with the text of the hadith, even if the second narration that the adhan of the one in minor impurity is not disliked was authenticated. Because they differentiate between the dislike of the adhan of the junub and the non-dislike of the adhan of the one in minor impurity according to the second narration, stating that the adhan resembles the prayer in that each requires the entry of time and facing the qibla, and resembles other acts in reality, so purity from the major impurity is required but not the minor, acting on both similarities. End. This reasoning is in opposition to the text. And disliked is the adhan of the junub like his iqamah, in one narration, due to what we mentioned. And disliked, rather the adhan is not valid from a child who does not understand, as we presented in its conditions, and because we narrated: 'Your best ones should call the adhan for you,' and because his voice is like the voice of birds. And it is said: the adhan of one who understands is also disliked, due to what we narrated, and it is said: an adult is preferable. And (disliked is the adhan of) an insane person and one with diminished intellect, and a drunkard, due to their lack of discernment. And disliked is the adhan of a woman; because if she lowers her voice, she fails to inform, and if she raises it, she commits a sin, because it is 'awrah. And it is not transmitted from the early generations when the congregation was in
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage lists various disliked (makruh) or invalid conditions for the adhan. It begins with talhin (melodic chanting), which is defined as singing that alters the words or form of the adhan. The author emphasizes that this is prohibited (la yahillu) whether in adhan or Quran recitation, and even listening to it is forbidden because it resembles sinful behavior. Beutifying the voice without distortion is, however, commendable. Next, the adhan by one with minor impurity (muhdith) is disliked, based on the hadith 'None should call the adhan except one with wudu.' The text acknowledges a second narration that it is not disliked, justifying the first by analogy with prayer: just as prayer requires wudu because of its resemblance to the prayer in terms of time and qibla, but major impurity is required due to the stronger resemblance. Nonetheless, the first narration is preferred as it follows the explicit text. The adhan of a junub is disliked by consensus. For a child who does not understand, the adhan is invalid (la yasihh) because he lacks discernment; his voice is compared to a bird's chirping. Similarly, insane persons, drunkards, and women are disqualified due to their inability to properly convey the call. A woman's adhan is disliked because she either fails to make the call heard or commits a sin by raising her voice (since a woman's voice is 'awrah according to the text). The author cites that there is no precedent from the early generations for a woman giving adhan when the congregation was present.

Key Terms
التلحين (al-talhin): Melodic chanting or singing that alters the words of the adhan or Quran by changing vowels, omitting letters, or adding embellishments.
المحدث (al-muhdith): A person in a state of minor impurity (without wudu).
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
اللحن (al-lahn): Intelligence/finesse of understanding, or grammatical error; contrasted with talhin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on talhin in the adhan according to the Hanafi school as presented in this text?
A) Permissible if done nicely.
B) Disliked (makruh) but not haram.
C) Prohibited (haram) and even listening to it is haram.
D) Recommended because it beautifies the call.

Key Takeaway
Talhin—any melodic chanting that alters the words of adhan or Quran—is strictly prohibited, and the believer must distinguish between prohibited melodic distortion and permissible beautification of the voice.

Talhin in Adhan: Ruling and Distinctions
Explains the ruling on melodious singing (talhin) in adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talhin in adhan, distinguish it from tahsin al-sawt, and apply the distinction to cases of melodic recitation.

Core Idea
Talhin that alters the words of adhan is impermissible; beautifying the voice without alteration is recommended.

In this lesson, we explore the concept of talhin (melodious singing) in the adhan. The Hanafi school distinguishes between impermissible alteration of the words and recommended beautification of the voice. We will examine the definitions, the ruling, and the evidence from the text.

Guided Path
1
Define talhin and lahn
Understand the terminological distinction: talhin is singing that alters words; lahn can mean sharpness or grammatical error.
The hadith uses 'alhan' to mean eloquent, not singing.
2
Identify the ruling
Talhin that changes letters or words of adhan is not permissible (la yahillu). The passage uses 'yukrah' but later says 'la yahillu' for altering talhin.
The ruling is makruh tahrimi (close to haram).
3
Recognize the exception
Beautifying the voice (tahsin al-sawt) without altering words is recommended (sunnah). There is no necessary connection between beautification and talhin.
Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani restricts the prohibition to regular dhikr; elongation in hay'alahs is allowed.
4
Apply the distinction
Given a scenario, decide whether it is talhin or tahsin al-sawt and state the ruling.
Focus on whether the words are changed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُكْرَهُ التَّلحينُ، وهو التطريب والترنم يقال: لحن في قراءته تلحيناً، طرب فيها و ترنم. وأما اللَّحَنُ فهو : الفطنة والفهم، لما لا يفطن له غيره. ومنه الحديث: «لَعَلَّ بَعْضَكُمْ الْحَنُ بِحُجَّتِهِ مِنْ بَعْض» (١) ، واللَّحْن أيضاً : الخطأ في الإعراب، والتلحين التخطئة، والمراد هنا: التغني، بحيث يؤدي إلى تغيير كلمات الأذان وكيفيتها بالحركات والسكنات، ونقص بعض حروفها، أو زيادة فيها. وإنه لا يحل فيه ولا في قراءة القرآن، ولا يحل سماعه، ولأن فيه تشبهاً بفعل الفسقة في حال فسقهم بالتغني، وكذا يكره الخطأ في الإعراب في كلمات الأذان، وأما تحسين الصوت فهو مطلوب، ولا تلازم بينه وبين الخطأ والتلحين، وقيده ( شمس الأئمة الحلواني»، بأن هذا في الأذكار، فأما إدخال المد في الحيعلتين فلا بأس به.
And it is disliked the talhin, which is modulation and singing. It is said: he performed talhin in his recitation, i.e., he modulated and sang. As for al-lahn, it is sharpness and understanding of what others do not perceive. From it is the hadith: 'Perhaps some of you are more eloquent in argument than others.' And al-lahn also means grammatical error, and talhin means making an error. What is meant here is singing that leads to changing the words of the adhan and their form in vowels and pauses, and omitting some letters or adding to them. And it is not permissible in it nor in reciting the Quran, and it is not permissible to listen to it, and because it resembles the actions of the wicked in their wickedness through singing. Likewise, grammatical error in the words of the adhan is disliked. As for beautifying the voice, it is sought after, and there is no necessary connection between it and error and talhin. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani restricted this to dhikr; as for inserting elongation in the two hay'alahs, there is no harm.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling of talhin (melodious singing) in the adhan. The author first defines talhin as vocal modulation (tatrib) and singing (tarannum). He distinguishes it from lahn, which can mean linguistic acumen (as in the hadith) or grammatical error. Here, talhin refers specifically to singing that alters the words of the adhan, by changing vowels, omitting letters, or adding them. Such alteration is not permissible (la yahillu) in adhan or Quran recitation, and listening to it is also impermissible. The reason given is that it resembles the behavior of sinners (fasaqah) who sing. Grammatical errors (khat' fi al-i'rab) are also disliked. However, beautifying the voice (tahsin al-sawt) is recommended and is distinct from talhin. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani restricts this prohibition to regular dhikr; inserting elongation (madd) in the hay'alahs (the phrases 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' etc.) is not disliked. This ruling is based on the principle that adhan is a form of worship requiring dignity, and talhin compromises that.

Key Terms
التلحين (al-talhin): Vocal modulation/singing that changes the words of adhan
اللحن (al-lahn): Grammatical error or sharpness of understanding

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on inserting elongation (madd) in the hay'alahs?
A) It is makruh
B) It is haram
C) There is no harm
D) It is sunnah

Key Takeaway
The key distinction in the Hanafi school is between talhin (alteration of words) which is prohibited, and tahsin al-sawt (beautification) which is recommended; a mu'adhdhin should aim for a clear, respectful recitation.

Who Should Not Call the Adhan: Conditions of the Mu'adhdhin
Lists types of people whose adhan is disliked or invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify at least six categories of people whose adhan is disliked or invalid according to the Hanafi school, and state the primary proof (dalil) and rationale for each ruling.

Core Idea
An adhan that fails to achieve effective notification is disliked; purification, sanity, and suitability of the caller are essential.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah expands on the conditions of the mu'adhdhin. You have already learned the basic prerequisites for adhan; now we explore which callers render the adhan disliked or invalid. The rulings are derived from a single root principle: adhan is for public notification (i'lam). When the caller cannot effectively notify—due to impurity, lack of reason, gender, moral corruption, or posture—the adhan becomes makruh or, in some cases, invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories and their rulings
Go through the passage and list each person mentioned: muhdith, junub, non-reasoning child, insane, drunkard, woman, fasiq, and sitting person. Note which are disliked (makruh) and which is invalid (la yasihh).
Only the child who does not reason renders the adhan invalid; all others are disliked (makruh tanzih).
2
Locate the primary proofs (dalil)
Two hadiths are cited: 'Only one with wudu should call the adhan' and 'Let the best among you call the adhan for you.' Identify which categories each proof addresses.
The first hadith directly addresses the muhdith and junub; the second addresses the child, insane, drunk, and fasiq.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (how the proofs apply)
Explain how each hadith imposes a condition: the first explicitly conditions adhan on wudu (tahara); the second implies that the caller must be free from disqualifying traits (sanity, adulthood, justice).
For the woman, the proof is not a hadith but the principle of 'awrah and the purpose of notification.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The passage mentions a second narration that the adhan of a muhdith is not disliked, based on qiyas (adhan resembles prayer in requiring time and qibla, so only major impurity matters). Recognize this as an ikhtilaf within the school.
The author follows the first narration because it agrees with the explicit hadith text.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
Understand why the author prefers the first narration: textual evidence (nas al-hadith) outweighs qiyas. This is a standard Hanafi principle: a clear text overrides analogical reasoning.
The mufta bihi is the first narration, making the adhan of a muhdith makruh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And it is disliked the iqama of the one in hadath and his adhan, due to what we related from his saying: 'Only one with wudu should call the adhan.' And because it contains calling to what he himself does not answer. And this narration is followed because it agrees with the text of the hadith. Even if the second narration is authenticated that the adhan of the one in hadath is not disliked, because they distinguished between the dislike of the junub's adhan and the non-dislike of the adhan of the one in hadath according to the second narration, by [saying] that the adhan resembles the prayer in that both require the entry of time and facing the qibla, and resembles other things in reality, so purification from the greater of the two hadaths is required, not the lesser, acting on the two resemblances. End. That is a reasoning in opposition to the text. And it is disliked the adhan of the junub, like his iqama, in one narration, due to what we mentioned. And it is disliked, rather it is not valid, the adhan of a child who does not reason, due to what we presented in its conditions, and due to what we narrated: 'Let the best among you call the adhan for you,' and because his voice is like the voice of birds. And it is said: the adhan of one who does reason is also disliked, due to what we narrated. And it is said: the adult is better. And the insane and the drunkard, due to their lack of discrimination, and it is disliked the adhan of a woman, because if she lowers her voice, she fails in notification, and if she raises it, she commits a sin, because it is 'awrah. And it is not transmitted from the Salaf when the congregation was permissible for them. And it is disliked the adhan of a fasiq, because his statement is not accepted in religious matters, and it does not oblige anyone, so notification is not achieved. And the adhan of a sitting person, because it opposes the attribute of the descending angel, and because standing is more effective. But there is no harm if he calls adhan for himself while sitting, observing the sunnah of the adhan and the lack of need for notification.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the rulings regarding the state of the mu'adhdhin. It covers multiple categories: (1) The adhan of a person in hadath (minor impurity) is disliked according to the relied-upon narration due to the hadith 'Only one with wudu should call the adhan.' A second narration says it is not disliked, arguing that adhan resembles prayer in requiring time and qibla, so only major impurity (janabah) matters, but the author follows the text. (2) The adhan of a junub (major impurity) is disliked by all narrations because of the hadith. (3) The adhan of a child who does not reason is disliked, in fact not valid, because he cannot intend properly and his voice is like a bird. (4) The insane and drunkard are similarly incapable. (5) A woman's adhan is disliked because she cannot fulfill the purpose: if quiet, she fails to notify; if loud, her voice is 'awrah. (6) A fasiq's adhan is disliked because his word is not accepted. (7) A sitting person's adhan is disliked because the angel descends standing. However, if he calls for himself while sitting, it is allowed. The primary proof is the hadith and the principle that adhan is for notification (i'lam); if the caller cannot achieve that, it is disliked.

Key Terms
المحدث (al-muhdith): A person in a state of minor impurity (without wudu)
الجنب (al-junub): A person in major impurity requiring ghusl
عورة ('awrah): Something that must be concealed; here, the woman's voice is deemed 'awrah for adhan
إعلام (i'lam): Notification, the purpose of adhan

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because her voice is 'awrah under all circumstances
B) Because she cannot fulfill the obligation of i'lam without sin
C) Because women are not allowed to enter the mosque
D) Because her adhan is invalid

Key Takeaway
The adhan is disliked when the caller cannot effectively notify the community, whether due to impurity, lack of reason, gender, moral status, or posture, based on the hadith 'Only one with wudu should call the adhan' and the principle of i'lam.
