Speaking During Adhan and Iqama: Rulings and When to Restart
Ruling on speech during adhan/iqama and restart conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on speech during adhan and iqama, distinguish between adhan and iqama regarding repetition, and evaluate the dispute over whether restarting adhan is wajib or mustahabb.

Core Idea
Speech during adhan/iqama is makruh; repeating adhan is mustahabb, not wajib, and iqama is never repeated.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah examines the rules governing speech during the call to prayer. It declares speech disliked and discusses whether the adhan must be restarted if interrupted. A key intra-Hanafi dispute arises over the nature of the obligation to restart: is it wajib or merely mustahabb? The later preferred view settles on mustahabb, drawing on multiple authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon (speech during adhan/iqama) and the legal category (makruh tanzih). Note that even replying to salam is included.
The ruling applies to both adhan and iqama equally for dislike.
2
Locate the Proof (Dalil)
Find the reasoning given: adhan and iqama are like the khutbah (sermon) in reverence, and speech breaks the recommended continuity (muwalat). This is a qiyas to khutbah.
The proof is not a direct nass but an analogy based on the nature of the acts.
3
Distinguish Between Adhan and Iqama for Restart
Note that if speech occurs, it is recommended (mustahabb) to repeat the adhan, but not the iqama. The reason is that adhan repetition is legislated in general (e.g., Friday), unlike iqama.
This distinction is based on established practice and maqasid.
4
Analyze the Five Cases and the Dispute
Examine the five cases (fainting, death, hadath, confusion, muteness) from al-Khulasa where some earlier texts indicated wajib restart. Consider the later authorities' reinterpretation that 'wajib' means 'confirmation' (thubut) rather than literal obligation.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf resolved by later tarjih.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
Conclude that the relied-upon position for fatwa is that restarting the adhan in these cases is mustahabb (preferable), not wajib. This is supported by al-Bahr, al-Dhahiriyya, and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
The earlier literal reading of wajib is not operative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُكْرَهُ الكلام في خلال الأذان، ولو برد السلام، ولا يرد في نفسه ولا بعد الفراغ، هو الصحيح. (و) يـكـره الـكــلام في الإقامَةِ، لأنهما ذكران معظَّمان كالخطبة، فيكره الكلام فيهما، ولأنــه يـفــوت الموالاة المسنونة. ويُسْتَحَبُّ إعادتُهُ) أي: الأذان بالكلام فيه، دُونَ الإِقَامَةِ)، وفي ( الخلاصة» ولا ينبغي أن يتكلم في الأذان والإقامة وإن تكلم يسيراً لا يلزمه الاستقبال. انتهى. فلا يستحب إعادتها بـه، لأن تكرار الأذان مشروع في الجملة، كما في يوم الجمعة، بخلاف الإقامة، وهذا أشبه من رواية إعادتهما جميعاً، ومن رواية عدم إعادتها جميعاً لما ذكرنا من الفرق. وقال « الكمال» عن « الخلاصة : خمس خصال إذا وجدت في الأذان والإقامة وجب الاستقبال: إذا غشي على المؤذن [ في أحدهما ، أو مات، أو سبقه حدث، فذهب ليتوضأ ، أو حصر [ فيه ] (۳) ولا ،ملقن أو خرس قال الكمال: فإن حمل الوجوب على ظاهره يعني فيأثم تاركه احتيج إلى الفرق بين نفس الأذان، فإنه سنة وبين استقباله بعد الشروع فيه، قد تحقق العجز عن إتمامه، وقد يقال فيه: إنه إذا شرع فيه [ قطع ] تبادر إلى ظن السامعين أن قطعه للخطأ في الوقت فينتظرون الأذان الحق، وقد تفوت بذلك الصلاة، فوجب إزالة ما يقتضي ذلك، بخلاف ما إذا لم يكن أذان الصلاة أصلاً، حيث لا ينتظرون، بل يراقب كل منهم وقت الصلاة بنفسه، أو ينصبون لهم مراقباً، إلا أن هذا يقتضي وجوب الإعادة، فيمن ذکر ناهم آنفاً، إلا الجنب، ولو قال قائل فيهم: إن عَلِمَ الناس حالهم وجبت، وإلا استحبت، ليقـع فعل الأذان معتبراً وعلى وجه السنة، لم يبعد، وعكسه في الخمسة المذكورة في « الخلاصة» انتهى. وقال في « البحر » بعد نقله الظاهر: إن الوجوب ليس على حقيقته، بل بمعنى الثبوت لما في المجتبى»، وإذا غشي عليه في الأذان، أو أحدث فتوضأ، أو مات، أو ارتد، فالأحب استقبال الأذان وكذا صرح بالاستحباب في ( الظهيرية » و « السراج الوهاج .انتهى. وكذا قال في « التجنيس والمزيد » ، وإن رعف المؤذن في خلال الأذان أو أحدث حدثاً آخر، فذهب وتوضأ، ثم جاء، فأحب إلي أن يبتدئ من أوله، لأن له شبهاً بالصلاة، ولو أحدث في الصلاة، فالأولى إلي أن يبتدئ بها، ولــو بنى عليها جاز، كذا ها هنا انتهى. وفي ( القنية ) : وقف في الأذان لتنحنح أو سعال، لا يعيد، وإن
And it is disliked speech during the adhan, even replying to salam, and he does not reply in himself nor after finishing; this is the correct view. And it is disliked speech during the iqama, because both are great remembrances like the khutbah, so speech is disliked in them, and because it loses the recommended continuity. It is recommended to repeat it (the adhan if speech occurred), but not the iqama. In al-Khulasa: 'It is not proper to speak in the adhan and iqama, and if he speaks little, he is not required to restart.' It is not recommended to repeat it (the iqama) because repetition of adhan is generally legislated, as on Friday, unlike the iqama. This is more appropriate than the narration of repeating both, or the narration of not repeating both, due to the difference mentioned. Al-Kamal said from al-Khulasa: 'Five qualities if they occur in the adhan or iqama, restarting becomes obligatory: if the mu'adhdhin faints in one of them, or dies, or a hadath precedes him so he goes to make wudu, or he becomes confused, or there is no prompter, or he becomes mute.' Al-Kamal said: 'If the obligation is taken literally (i.e., the one who leaves it sins), one would need to differentiate between the adhan itself (which is sunnah) and restarting after beginning it; there is confirmed inability to complete it. It may be said: if he starts it and then cuts off, the listeners may think the cut is due to a mistake in the time, so they wait for the correct adhan, and thus prayer may be missed, so it is obligatory to remove that (doubt), unlike if there was no adhan at all, where they do not wait but each monitors the time themselves, or they appoint a monitor. However, this implies the obligation of repetition for those we mentioned except the junub. If someone says about them: if people know their state, repetition is obligatory; otherwise recommended, so that the adhan occurs correctly and in accordance with sunnah, it is not far-fetched. The opposite applies to the five mentioned in al-Khulasa.' End. And in al-Bahr after quoting the apparent: 'Obligation is not real, but means confirmation (thubut) as in al-Mujtaba. If he faints during the adhan, or has a hadath and does wudu, or dies, or apostatizes, the preferred view (ahab) is to restart the adhan.' Similarly in al-Dhahiriyya and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. End. And in al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid: 'If the mu'adhdhin has a nosebleed during the adhan or has another hadath, goes for wudu, then returns, I prefer him to start from the beginning, because adhan resembles prayer; if he has a hadath in prayer, it is better to start over, though if he resumes it, it is permissible. So here too.' End. And in al-Qunyah: 'If he pauses in the adhan due to clearing throat or coughing, he does not repeat.'
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the rulings of speech during adhan and iqama, and when to restart. The author states that speech during adhan is disliked (makruh), even replying to salam. The correct view is that he does not reply even mentally afterwards. Similarly, speech during iqama is disliked because both are great dhikr like the khutbah and break the sunnah of continuity. If speech occurs, it is recommended (mustahabb) to repeat the adhan but not the iqama. Al-Khulasa adds that little speech does not require restart. The author explains that adhan repetition is legislated in general (e.g., Friday), unlike iqama. Then a discussion from Al-Kamal: Five cases (fainting, death, hadath leading to wudu, confusion, muteness) require restarting the adhan. However, later authorities like al-Bahr, al-Dhahiriyya, and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj say that restart is 'ahab' (preferable) not wajib. Similarly, in al-Tajnis, if a hadath occurs, starting over is preferable but resumption is permissible. Al-Qunyah says that pausing for coughing etc. does not require repetition. The overall ruling is that speech is makruh and repeating the adhan is recommended but not obligatory, based on the principle that adhan resembles prayer in its dignity.

Key Terms
الموالاة (al-muwalat): Continuity without significant pause in adhan/iqama
الاستحباب (al-istihbab): Recommendation; a ruling that is encouraged but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on replying to salam during adhan?
A) It is obligatory
B) It is allowed
C) It is disliked
D) It invalidates adhan

Key Takeaway
Speech during adhan/iqama is disliked; if speech occurs, restarting adhan is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory, and iqama is not restarted.

Makruh Aspects of Adhan and Iqamah: Fasiq, Sitting, and Talking
Rulings on makruh adhan and repetition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the makruh aspects of adhan and iqamah, explain the reasoning for each ruling, and apply the ruling on repetition after talking.

Core Idea
Adhan from a fasiq or sitting person is makruh; talking during adhan/iqamah is disliked and only the adhan is recommended to be repeated.

This lesson examines three specific actions that render the adhan or iqamah makruh tanzihi (disliked but not sinful). The commentary provides the underlying logic for each ruling, from the unreliability of a fasiq's notification to the sunnah of standing and the importance of continuity. Understanding these nuances helps the mu'adhdhin perform the call properly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three makruh aspects
Read the passage and list the three matters declared makruh: adhan of a fasiq, adhan of a sitting person, and talking during adhan or iqamah.
Talking is also disliked in iqamah, as noted.
2
Examine the proof for each
For each makruh case, find the reason given. Fasiq: his word is not accepted in religious matters. Sitting: contradicts the angel's descent. Talking: breaks continuity (muwalat) and treats the dhikr lightly.
The proofs are rational (dalil aqli) based on the purpose of adhan.
3
Note the exception for private adhan
The text states there is no harm if one gives adhan for himself while sitting, because the need for public notification is absent.
This shows the ruling is context-dependent.
4
Understand the ruling on repetition
If talking occurs, it is mustahabb to repeat the adhan but not the iqamah. The text explains that repetition of adhan is legislated in general (e.g., Fridays), whereas iqamah has no such precedent.
This is the preferred view over narrations that both or neither be repeated.
5
State the mufta bihi
The operative ruling: talking is makruh tanzihi; repeating the adhan is mustahabb; repeating iqamah is not recommended.
This is based on the later Hanafi authorities cited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفاسق، وقاعد، والكلام في خلال الأذان، وفي الإقامة، ويُسْتَحَبُّ إعادته دونَ الإقامة .
حقهن مشروعة لهن، (وَ) يكره أذان (فَاسِقِ)، لأنه لا يقبل قوله في الديانات، ولا يلزم أحداً، فلم يوجد الإعلام، (و) أذان (قاعِد)، لمخالفته صفة الملك النازل به؛ ولأن القائم به أبلغ، ولا بأس أن يؤذن لنفسه قاعداً مراعاة لسنة الأذان، وعدم الحاجة إلى الإعلام. (وَ) يـكــره (الكــلام فـي خــلال الأذان)، ولو برد السلام، ولا يرد في نفسه ولا بعد الفراغ، هو الصحيح. (و) يـكــره الـكــلام (في الإقامَةِ)، لأنهما ذكر ان معظَّمان كالخطبة، فيكره الكلام فيهما، ولأنــه يـفــوت الموالاة المسنونة. ويُسْتَحَبُّ إعادتُهُ) أي: الأذان بالكلام فيه، دُونَ الإِقَامَةِ)، وفي ( الخلاصة» ولا ينبغي أن يتكلم في الأذان والإقامة وإن تكلم يسيراً لا يلزمه الاستقبال. انتهى. فلا يستحب إعادتها بـه، لأن تكرار الأذان مشروع في الجملة، كما في يوم الجمعة، بخلاف الإقامة، وهذا أشبه من رواية إعادتهما جميعاً، ومن رواية عدم إعادتها جميعاً لما ذكرنا من الفرق. وقال « الكمال» عن « الخلاصة : خمس خصال إذا وجدت في الأذان والإقامة وجب الاستقبال: إذا غشي على المؤذن [ في أحدهما ]، أو مات، أو سبقه حدث، فذهب ليتوضأ ، أو حصر [ فيه ] (۳) ولا ،ملقن أو خرس قال الكمال: فإن حمل الوجوب على ظاهره يعني فيأثم تاركه احتيج إلى الفرق بين نفس الأذان، فإنه سنة وبين استقباله بعد الشروع فيه، قد تحقق العجز عن إتمامه، وقد يقال فيه: إنه إذا شرع فيه [ قطع ] تبادر إلى ظن السامعين أن قطعه للخطأ في الوقت فينتظرون الأذان الحق، وقد تفوت بذلك الصلاة، فوجب إزالة ما يقتضي ذلك، بخلاف ما إذا لم يكن أذان الصلاة أصلاً، حيث لا ينتظرون، بل يراقب كل منهم وقت الصلاة بنفسه، أو ينصبون لهم مراقباً، إلا أن هذا يقتضي وجوب الإعادة، فيمـن ذکر ناهم آنفاً، إلا الجنب، ولو قال قائل فيهم: إن عَلِمَ الناس حالهم وجبت، وإلا استحبت، ليقـع فعل الأذان معتبراً وعلى وجه السنة، لم يبعد، وعكسه في الخمسة المذكورة في « الخلاصة» انتهى. وقال في « البحر » بعد نقله الظاهر: إن الوجوب ليس على حقيقته، بل بمعنى الثبوت لما في المجتبى»، وإذا غشي عليه في الأذان، أو أحدث فتوضأ، أو مات، أو ارتد، فالأحب استقبال الأذان وكذا صرح بالاستحباب في ( الظهيرية » و « السراج الوهاج .انتهى. وكذا قال في « التجنيس والمزيد » ، وإن رعف المؤذن في خلال الأذان أو أحدث حدثاً آخر، فذهب وتوضأ، ثم جاء، فأحب إلي أن يبتدئ من أوله، لأن له شبهاً بالصلاة، ولو أحدث في الصلاة، فالأولى إلي أن يبتدئ بها، ولــو بنى عليها جاز، كذا ها هنا انتهى. وفي ( القنية ) : وقف في الأذان لتنحنح أو سعال، لا يعيد، وإن كانت الوقفة كثيرة يعيد انتهى. وقال ( الكمال » : يكره التنحنح عند الأذان والإقامة، لأنه بدعة. انتهى. وهو جواب عن صلاة المؤذن على النبي الله الله في ابتداء الإقامة، لأنه بدعة.

تنبيه اختلف المشايخ هل يختم الإقامة في مكانه، أو يتمها ماشياً. قال بعضهم: يختمها على مكانه، سواء كان المؤذن إماماً أو غيره، وكذا روي عن أبي يوسف، وقال أبـــو يـوسـف: يتمها ماشياً، الفقيه « أبي جعفر الهندواني أنه إذا بلغ قوله قد قامت الصلاة، فهو بالخيار إن شاء مشي، وإن شاء وقف، إماماً كان أو غيره، وبه أخذ الفقيه « أبو الليث». وما روي عن أبي يوسف أصح، كذا في « البدائع » . واقتصر في ( الخلاصة» على قول الفقيهين من غير إسناد لأحد.
And the adhan of a fasiq (sinner), and of a sitting person, and talking during the adhan, and during the iqamah, and it is recommended to repeat it (the adhan) but not the iqamah.
Their rights are legislated for them. (And) the adhan of a fasiq is disliked, because his statement is not accepted in religious matters, and it is not binding on anyone, so notification (i'lam) has not occurred. (And) the adhan of a sitting person is disliked, because it contradicts the description of the angel who descended with it; and because standing is more effective. There is no harm if he gives adhan for himself while sitting, out of consideration for the sunnah of adhan and the lack of need for notification. (And) talking during the adhan is disliked, even if replying to salam. He should not reply in his mind nor after finishing; that is the correct view. (And) talking during the iqamah is disliked, because both (adhan and iqamah) are glorified dhikr like the sermon, so talking during them is disliked, and because it breaks the recommended continuity (muwalat). It is recommended to repeat it (that is, the adhan because of talking during it) but not the iqamah. And in Al-Khalasa: 'It is not proper to talk during the adhan and iqamah. If he talks a little, restart is not incumbent.' End. So it is not recommended to repeat it (the iqamah) because repetition of the adhan is legislated in general, as on Friday, unlike the iqamah. This (view) is more appropriate than the narration that both should be repeated, and than the narration that neither should be repeated, due to the distinction we mentioned. Al-Kamal said from Al-Khalasa: 'Five characteristics if found in the adhan and iqamah necessitate restart: if the mu'adhdhin faints in either of them, or dies, or is overcome by a hadath and goes to perform wudu, or is halted (unable to continue) and there is no prompter, or becomes mute.' Al-Kamal said: 'If the obligation (wujub) is taken literally, meaning the one who leaves it sins, then a distinction is needed between the adhan itself, which is sunnah, and restarting it after beginning it. Since inability to complete it has occurred, it may be said: when he starts it (then stops), it occurs to the listeners that his stopping is due to a mistake in the time, so they wait for the correct adhan, and thus the prayer may be missed. So removing what necessitates that is obligatory, unlike when there was no adhan for the prayer at all, for they do not wait, rather each person watches the time of prayer himself, or they appoint a timekeeper for them. However, this would imply obligation of repetition for those we mentioned previously, except the junub. If someone said regarding them: if people know their situation, it becomes obligatory, otherwise it is recommended, so that the performance of adhan may be considered valid and in accordance with sunnah, this would not be far-fetched. And the opposite applies to the five mentioned in Al-Khalasa.' End. And in Al-Bahr after quoting Al-Zahir: 'Obligation is not real, but rather in the sense of confirmation (thubut), as in Al-Mujtaba. If he faints during the adhan, or has a hadath and performs wudu, or dies, or apostasizes, the most beloved is to restart the adhan.' Similarly, it is clearly stated as recommended in Al-Dhuhayriyya and Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. End. Similarly in Al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid: 'If the mu'adhdhin has a nosebleed during the adhan or has another hadath, goes and performs wudu, then comes back, the most beloved to me is that he starts from the beginning, because it resembles the prayer. If he has a hadath during prayer, the best is to start from the beginning, though if he builds upon it, it is permissible. The same here.' End. In Al-Qunyah: 'If he pauses in the adhan for clearing the throat or coughing, he does not repeat. If the pause is long, he repeats.' End. Al-Kamal said: 'Clearing the throat during adhan and iqamah is disliked because it is a innovation (bid'ah).' End. And this is a response to the mu'adhdhin's sending salawat upon the Prophet at the beginning of the iqamah, because it is an innovation.

Note: The scholars differed on whether he should finish the iqamah in his place or complete it walking. Some said: he finishes it in his place, whether the mu'adhdhin is the imam or someone else. It is also narrated from Abu Yusuf. Abu Yusuf said: he completes it walking. The jurist Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani said: when he reaches his saying "qad qamat al-salah", he has the choice: if he wishes, he walks, and if he wishes, he stands, whether he is the imam or someone else. The jurist Abu al-Layth adopted this. The narration from Abu Yusuf is more authentic, as in Al-Bada'i. Al-Khalasa restricted itself to the statement of the two jurists without attributing it to anyone.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, discusses multiple rulings of adhan and iqamah that are considered makruh (disliked) and related provisions. The author begins by enumerating disliked aspects: adhan from a fasiq (open sinner), adhan while sitting, and talking during either adhan or iqamah. He then addresses whether the adhan should be repeated if talk occurs.

For the fasiq, the reasoning is that his statement is not accepted in religious matters (shahada, etc.) and his call does not legally oblige anyone, so the purpose of notification (i'lam) is not achieved. For the sitting position, it contradicts the sunnah because the angel (Jibril) descended standing. However, if one gives adhan for himself alone, sitting is permissible as there is no need for public notification. Talking during adhan is makruh even for replying salam; the correct view is not to reply even mentally or after finishing. The same applies to iqamah, as both are forms of glorified dhikr akin to the khutbah. Talking breaks the recommended continuity (muwalat).

If one talks, repeating the adhan is mustahabb (recommended) but not the iqamah. The reason: repetition of adhan is generally legislated in some contexts (e.g., Friday), whereas repetition of iqamah has no similar basis. This is the preferred view over narrations that both or neither be repeated.

The text then addresses a detailed scenario from Al-Khalasa: five situations requiring restart (istiqbal) of adhan or iqamah: fainting, death, hadath (ritual impurity), inability to continue without a prompter, or muteness. However, later authorities clarify that this obligation is not literal; rather, restart is recommended. The cited texts (Al-Bahr, Al-Mujtaba, Al-Dhuhayriyya, etc.) emphasize istihbab (recommendation). The discussion uses analogy with prayer: as one who has a hadath in prayer is advised to restart but may build upon it, similarly for adhan.

Finally, a note (tanbih) discusses a scholarly difference: should the mu'adhdhin finish the iqamah standing in place or while walking? The preferred narration from Abu Yusuf is to complete it walking, though some jurists give a choice after 'qad qamat al-salah'. The commentator notes that Al-Khalasa only mentions the two jurists' opinion without attribution, but Al-Bada'i considers Abu Yusuf's view more authentic.

Key Terms
فاسق (fāsiq): A Muslim who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, whose testimony is rejected in legal matters.
قاعد (qā‘id): One who gives adhan while sitting, contrary to the sunnah of standing.
موالاة (muwālāh): Continuity between the parts of adhan or iqamah without lengthy pauses or interruptions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on repeating the adhan if the mu'adhdhin talks during it?
A) It is wajib to repeat both adhan and iqamah.
B) It is mustahabb to repeat the adhan but not the iqamah.
C) It is mustahabb to repeat both.
D) It is not recommended to repeat either.

Key Takeaway
Talking during adhan/iqamah is makruh tanzihi; repeating the adhan is mustahabb, but not the iqamah.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
10 min
The Five Situations Requiring Restart of Adhan/Iqamah
Five situations requiring restart and the preferred ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five situations requiring restart of adhan or iqamah, explain the Hanafi preferred view that restart is mustahabb (not wajib), and apply the ruling to modern scenarios.

Core Idea
The five critical interruptions (fainting, death, hadath, halt, muteness) require restart; the Hanafi school holds it recommended, not obligatory.

This lesson delves into a specific scenario from Al-Khalasa: five severe interruptions that necessitate restarting the adhan or iqamah. The commentary clarifies that the 'obligation' mentioned in earlier texts is interpreted as recommendation (istihbab) by later authorities, based on analogy with prayer and the principle that adhan itself is a sunnah. The lesson also touches on a related difference: whether the mu'adhdhin should finish the iqamah walking or standing.

Guided Path
1
List the five situations
From the passage, identify the five events: fainting, death, hadath (requiring wudu), inability to continue without a prompter (hassr), and muteness.
These are from Al-Khalasa as quoted.
2
Analyze the ruling of 'wujub'
The text from Al-Khalasa says 'wajab al-istiqbal'. Note that later authorities (Al-Bahr, Al-Mujtaba, etc.) clarify this is not literal obligation but confirmation (thubut) or recommendation.
The passage provides reasons against literal obligation.
3
Understand the analogy to prayer
The text analogizes the situation to prayer: if one has a hadath during prayer, it is recommended to restart but permissible to build upon it. Similarly for adhan.
This qiyas supports the view of istihbab.
4
Note the exception for janub
A janub (in state of major impurity) is excepted from the obligation even in the strict view, because he was not fit to begin with.
This nuance is mentioned in the commentary.
5
Apply the tanbih on finishing iqamah
The scholars differed: finish standing in place or walking? The preferred narration from Abu Yusuf is to complete it walking; some give choice after 'qad qamat al-salah'.
This is a separate issue but related to iqamah.

وفاسق، وقاعد، والكلام في خلال الأذان، وفي الإقامة، ويُسْتَحَبُّ إعادته دونَ الإقامة .
حقهن مشروعة لهن، (وَ) يكره أذان (فَاسِقِ)، لأنه لا يقبل قوله في الديانات، ولا يلزم أحداً، فلم يوجد الإعلام، (و) أذان (قاعِد)، لمخالفته صفة الملك النازل به؛ ولأن القائم به أبلغ، ولا بأس أن يؤذن لنفسه قاعداً مراعاة لسنة الأذان، وعدم الحاجة إلى الإعلام. (وَ) يـكــره (الكــلام فـي خــلال الأذان)، ولو برد السلام، ولا يرد في نفسه ولا بعد الفراغ، هو الصحيح. تنبيه اختلف المشايخ هل يختم الإقامة في مكانه، أو يتمها ماشياً. قال بعضهم: يختمها على مكانه، سواء كان المؤذن إماماً أو غيره، وكذا روي عن أبي يوسف، وقال أبـــو يـوسـف: يتمها ماشياً، الفقيه « أبي جعفر الهندواني أنه إذا بلغ قوله قد قامت الصلاة، فهو بالخيار إن شاء مشي، وإن شاء وقف، إماماً كان أو غيره، وبه أخذ الفقيه « أبو الليث». وما روي عن أبي يوسف أصح، كذا في « البدائع » . واقتصر في ( الخلاصة» على قول الفقيهين من غير إسناد لأحد.
And the adhan of a fasiq (sinner), and of a sitting person, and talking during the adhan, and during the iqamah, and it is recommended to repeat it (the adhan) but not the iqamah.
Their rights are legislated for them. (And) the adhan of a fasiq is disliked, because his statement is not accepted in religious matters, and it is not binding on anyone, so notification (i'lam) has not occurred. (And) the adhan of a sitting person is disliked, because it contradicts the description of the angel who descended with it; and because standing is more effective. There is no harm if he gives adhan for himself while sitting, out of consideration for the sunnah of adhan and the lack of need for notification. (And) talking during the adhan is disliked, even if replying to salam. He should not reply in his mind nor after finishing; that is the correct view. (And) talking during the iqamah is disliked, because both (adhan and iqamah) are glorified dhikr like the sermon, so talking during them is disliked, and because it breaks the recommended continuity (muwalat). It is recommended to repeat it (that is, the adhan because of talking during it) but not the iqamah. And in Al-Khalasa: 'It is not proper to talk during the adhan and iqamah. If he talks a little, restart is not incumbent.' End. So it is not recommended to repeat it (the iqamah) because repetition of the adhan is legislated in general, as on Friday, unlike the iqamah. This (view) is more appropriate than the narration that both should be repeated, and than the narration that neither should be repeated, due to the distinction we mentioned. Al-Kamal said from Al-Khalasa: 'Five characteristics if found in the adhan and iqamah necessitate restart: if the mu'adhdhin faints in either of them, or dies, or is overcome by a hadath and goes to perform wudu, or is halted (unable to continue) and there is no prompter, or becomes mute.' Al-Kamal said: 'If the obligation (wujub) is taken literally, meaning the one who leaves it sins, then a distinction is needed between the adhan itself, which is sunnah, and restarting it after beginning it. Since inability to complete it has occurred, it may be said: when he starts it (then stops), it occurs to the listeners that his stopping is due to a mistake in the time, so they wait for the correct adhan, and thus the prayer may be missed. So removing what necessitates that is obligatory, unlike when there was no adhan for the prayer at all, for they do not wait, rather each person watches the time of prayer himself, or they appoint a timekeeper for them. However, this would imply obligation of repetition for those we mentioned previously, except the junub. If someone said regarding them: if people know their situation, it becomes obligatory, otherwise it is recommended, so that the performance of adhan may be considered valid and in accordance with sunnah, this would not be far-fetched. And the opposite applies to the five mentioned in Al-Khalasa.' End. And in Al-Bahr after quoting Al-Zahir: 'Obligation is not real, but rather in the sense of confirmation (thubut), as in Al-Mujtaba. If he faints during the adhan, or has a hadath and performs wudu, or dies, or apostasizes, the most beloved is to restart the adhan.' Similarly, it is clearly stated as recommended in Al-Dhuhayriyya and Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. End. Similarly in Al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid: 'If the mu'adhdhin has a nosebleed during the adhan or has another hadath, goes and performs wudu, then comes back, the most beloved to me is that he starts from the beginning, because it resembles the prayer. If he has a hadath during prayer, the best is to start from the beginning, though if he builds upon it, it is permissible. The same here.' End. In Al-Qunyah: 'If he pauses in the adhan for clearing the throat or coughing, he does not repeat. If the pause is long, he repeats.' End. Al-Kamal said: 'Clearing the throat during adhan and iqamah is disliked because it is a innovation (bid'ah).' End. And this is a response to the mu'adhdhin's sending salawat upon the Prophet at the beginning of the iqamah, because it is an innovation.

Note: The scholars differed on whether he should finish the iqamah in his place or complete it walking. Some said: he finishes it in his place, whether the mu'adhdhin is the imam or someone else. It is also narrated from Abu Yusuf. Abu Yusuf said: he completes it walking. The jurist Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani said: when he reaches his saying "qad qamat al-salah", he has the choice: if he wishes, he walks, and if he wishes, he stands, whether he is the imam or someone else. The jurist Abu al-Layth adopted this. The narration from Abu Yusuf is more authentic, as in Al-Bada'i. Al-Khalasa restricted itself to the statement of the two jurists without attributing it to anyone.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, discusses multiple rulings of adhan and iqamah that are considered makruh (disliked) and related provisions. The author begins by enumerating disliked aspects: adhan from a fasiq (open sinner), adhan while sitting, and talking during either adhan or iqamah. He then addresses whether the adhan should be repeated if talk occurs.

For the fasiq, the reasoning is that his statement is not accepted in religious matters (shahada, etc.) and his call does not legally oblige anyone, so the purpose of notification (i'lam) is not achieved. For the sitting position, it contradicts the sunnah because the angel (Jibril) descended standing. However, if one gives adhan for himself alone, sitting is permissible as there is no need for public notification. Talking during adhan is makruh even for replying salam; the correct view is not to reply even mentally or after finishing. The same applies to iqamah, as both are forms of glorified dhikr akin to the khutbah. Talking breaks the recommended continuity (muwalat).

If one talks, repeating the adhan is mustahabb (recommended) but not the iqamah. The reason: repetition of adhan is generally legislated in some contexts (e.g., Friday), whereas repetition of iqamah has no similar basis. This is the preferred view over narrations that both or neither be repeated.

The text then addresses a detailed scenario from Al-Khalasa: five situations requiring restart (istiqbal) of adhan or iqamah: fainting, death, hadath (ritual impurity), inability to continue without a prompter, or muteness. However, later authorities clarify that this obligation is not literal; rather, restart is recommended. The cited texts (Al-Bahr, Al-Mujtaba, Al-Dhuhayriyya, etc.) emphasize istihbab (recommendation). The discussion uses analogy with prayer: as one who has a hadath in prayer is advised to restart but may build upon it, similarly for adhan.

Finally, a note (tanbih) discusses a scholarly difference: should the mu'adhdhin finish the iqamah standing in place or while walking? The preferred narration from Abu Yusuf is to complete it walking, though some jurists give a choice after 'qad qamat al-salah'. The commentator notes that Al-Khalasa only mentions the two jurists' opinion without attribution, but Al-Bada'i considers Abu Yusuf's view more authentic.

Key Terms
استقبال (istiqbāl): Restarting the adhan or iqamah from the beginning due to a significant interruption or defect.
حصر (hasr): Being unable to continue the adhan due to forgetting or stumbling, with no one to prompt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi ruling on restarting the adhan if the mu'adhdhin faints during it?
A) It is wajib (obligatory) to restart.
B) It is mustahabb (recommended) to restart.
C) The adhan is invalid and must be made up later.
D) He must continue from where he stopped.

Key Takeaway
The five severe interruptions during adhan/iqamah make restart recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory, as clarified by later Hanafi authorities.

Adhan and Iqamah for Friday Zuhr and for Missed Prayers
Rulings on adhan/iqamah for Friday Zuhr and missed prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on adhan and iqamah for Friday Zuhr in a city and for missed prayers, and identify the proof from the hadith of al-Ta'ris.

Core Idea
For Friday Zuhr in a city, adhan and iqamah are makruh; for missed prayers, they are sunnah.

This passage addresses two distinct situations involving adhan and iqamah. First, on Friday in a city where Jumu'ah is held, it is disliked to call adhan and iqamah for the Zuhr prayer, based on a narration from Ali. Second, when making up a missed prayer (qada), it is sunnah to call adhan and iqamah, as demonstrated by the Prophet when he missed Fajr during the journey of al-Ta'ris. We will examine both rulings and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts
The passage discusses two acts: (1) adhan and iqamah for Zuhr on Friday in a city, and (2) adhan and iqamah for a missed prayer (qada). Recognize that these are separate rulings.
2
State the ruling for each
For Friday Zuhr in a city, the ruling is makruh tanzihi (disliked). For missed prayers, it is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah). Note the exception for an excused person according to some Hanafi authorities.
The makruh includes both adhan and iqamah.
3
Locate the dalil for missed prayers
The proof is the hadith of al-Ta'ris, where the Prophet ordered Bilal to call adhan and iqamah for the missed Fajr. The hadith is cited in the passage.
Hadith: Muwatta' Malik, Bab al-Nawm 'an al-Salah wa al-Ta'ris.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's explicit command to Bilal ('أمر بلالاً أن ينادي للصلاة ويقيم') indicates that adhan and iqamah are prescribed when making up a missed prayer. The Prophet's action (fi'l) serves as evidence for sunnah.
The command is direct and unambiguous.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
For Friday Zuhr, there is a difference: al-Tafariq holds that the excused person (e.g., one who missed Jumu'ah) may pray Zuhr with adhan and iqamah, but the majority view, based on the narration from Ali, is that it is makruh. The mufta bihi is makruh.
The ikhtilaf does not affect the general ruling for the city dweller.

(۱) عن زيد بن أسلم قال: عرس رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ليلة بطريق مكة. ووكل بلالاً أن يوقظهم للصلاة فـرقــد بـلال، ورقـدوا حتى استيقظوا وقد طلعت عليهم الشمس وقد فزعوا فأمرهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يركبوا حتى يخرجوا من ذلك الوادي وقال : ( إن هذا وادٍ به شيطان فركبوا حتى خرجوا من ذلك الوادي ثم أمرهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن ينزلوا وأن يتوضؤوا وأمر بلالاً أن ينادي للصلاة، ويقيم فصلى رسول الله الله بالناس وقد رأى من فزعهم فقال: «يا أيها الناس إن الله قبض أرواحنا ولو شاء لردَّها إلينا في حين غير هذا، فإذا رقد أحدكم عن الصلاة أو نسيها ثم فزع إليها فليصلها كما كان يصليها في وقتها ثم التفت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى أبي بكر الصديق فقال: « إن الشيطان أتي بلالاً وهو قائم يصلي فأضجعه ثم لم يزل يهدئه كما يهدأ الصبي حتى نــام ثم دعــا رســول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بلالاً فأخبر بلال رسول الله له مثل الذي أخبر به رسول الله له أبا بكر فقال أبو بكره : أشهد أنك رسول الله » ، أخرجه مالك في الموطأ (١٤/١) ، باب النوم عن الصلاة والتعريس: النزول آخر الليل للاستراحة والنوم.
(And they are disliked) that is, the adhan and iqamah for Zuhr on Friday in the city. This is narrated from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), and it includes the excused person and others, said al-Zayla'i. And in al-Dhuhayriyya: 'A group who missed Friday, they pray Zuhr without adhan, iqamah, and congregation.' And in al-Walwaljiyya, it clearly states what is included in the narration from Ali: 'One should not pray Zuhr on Friday in congregation in a city, nor give adhan, nor give iqamah in a prison or elsewhere for Zuhr prayer.' But it is mentioned in al-Bahr from al-Tafariq that the excused person prays Zuhr with adhan and iqamah, even if congregation is not recommended. End. This contradicts the narration from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him).
(And one gives adhan for the missed prayer and gives iqamah) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) made up the Fajr prayer on the morning of the night of al-Ta'ris with adhan and iqamah. The general application includes the qada in the mosque and in the house, but in al-Mujtaba, attributed to al-Halwani: 'It is sunnah to make qada in houses, not in mosques, because that involves disfigurement and severity.' End. The author of al-Bahr said: 'Since they explicitly stated that a missed prayer is not performed in the mosque because it shows laziness in taking the prayer out of its time, then hiding the adhan for the missed prayer in the mosque is obligatory, and it is more deserving of prohibition.' End.
(1) From Zayd ibn Aslam that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) camped one night on the road to Makkah. He appointed Bilal to wake them for prayer. Bilal slept, and they slept until they woke up and the sun had risen over them, and they were startled. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ordered them to ride until they left that valley and said: 'This is a valley with a devil.' So they rode until they left that valley. Then he ordered them to descend and perform wudu, and ordered Bilal to call the adhan for prayer and give iqamah. Then the Messenger of Allah led the people in prayer. He saw their fear and said: 'O people, Allah took our souls, and if He willed, He would have returned them to us at a time other than this. So if any of you sleeps through the prayer or forgets it, then when he remembers, he should pray it as he would pray it in its time.' Then the Messenger of Allah turned to Abu Bakr al-Siddiq and said: 'The devil came to Bilal while he was standing in prayer and laid him down, and then kept soothing him as a child is soothed until he slept.' Then the Messenger of Allah called Bilal and Bilal informed him of what he had informed Abu Bakr. Abu Bakr said: 'I bear witness that you are the Messenger of Allah.' Recorded by Malik in al-Muwatta' (1/14), Chapter on sleeping through the prayer and al-Ta'ris: al-nuzul at the end of the night for rest and sleep.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage discusses two distinct rulings: (1) The dislike of calling adhan and iqamah for Zuhr on Friday in a city that has the Friday prayer, and (2) the sunnah of calling adhan and iqamah for missed prayers (faa'itah).

The first ruling is based on a narration from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that adhan and iqamah for Friday Zuhr are disliked. The commentator notes that this includes even those who are excused from Friday (e.g., travelers, sick). Al-Zayla'i generalizes it to all. However, there is a contrary view from al-Tafariq (in al-Bahr) that an excused person should pray Zuhr with adhan and iqamah, though congregation is not recommended. The passage leaves this as a disagreement.

The second ruling: For making up a missed prayer, one should give adhan and iqamah. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) when he and his companions missed Fajr due to sleep. He ordered Bilal to call adhan and iqamah, and then they prayed. This hadith is a strong sunnah evidence. However, there is a nuance: the qada should ideally be performed at home, not in the mosque, to avoid showing negligence. In the mosque, if one must, it is better to give adhan quietly (ikhfa) to avoid the appearance of laziness, as stated by the author of al-Bahr.

Key Terms
المصر (al-miṣr): A major city or town where Friday prayer is established with the ruler's permission.
الفائتة (al-fā'itah): A missed obligatory prayer that must be made up (qada) after its time.
التعريس (al-ta'rīs): Stopping at the end of the night for rest and sleep during a journey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is wajib to call adhan and iqamah.
D) It is permissible only if prayed in the mosque.

Key Takeaway
Adhan and iqamah for Friday Zuhr in a city are makruh; for making up any missed obligatory prayer, they are sunnah.

Dislike of Adhan and Iqama for Zuhr on Friday in a Major City
Ruling on adhan/iqama for Friday Zuhr in a city

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqama for Zuhr on Friday in a congregational city and identify the exception for the excused person within the school.

Core Idea
Adhan and iqama for Friday Zuhr in a major city is disliked for all, including the excused.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Nur al-Idah: the dislike of calling the adhan and iqama for the Zuhr prayer on Friday in a city where Friday prayer is held. The ruling is based on a narration from Ali (RA) and applies to everyone, including those who miss the Friday prayer. The passage also touches on related adhan practices like clearing the throat and walking during iqama, but our focus is on the primary ruling and its scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (adhan and iqama for Zuhr on Friday in a misr) and the hukm level (makruh).
The matn uses the dual form 'yukrahan' indicating both adhan and iqama are disliked.
2
Identify the authority and scope
Note that the ruling is attributed to a narration from Ali (RA) and applies to all, including the excused person (e.g., traveler, prisoner).
Al-Zayla'i explains that the narration includes the excused.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Notice that al-Tafariq allows adhan/iqama for the excused, but this contradicts the narration from Ali. The school follows the narration from Ali as the relied-upon position.
The commentator sides with the narration from Ali, so the general dislike stands.
4
Understand the practical implication
Apply the ruling: In a city where Friday is held, even if one misses the Friday prayer, one should not call adhan/iqama for the make-up Zuhr prayer.
Some later Hanafi texts clarify that even congregation is not recommended.

تنبيه اختلف المشايخ هل يختم الإقامة في مكانه، أو يتمها ماشياً. قال بعضهم: يختمها على مكانه، سواء كان المؤذن إماماً أو غيره، وكذا روي عن أبي يوسف، وقال أبو يوسف: يتمها ماشياً، الفقيه أبو جعفر الهندواني أنه إذا بلغ قوله قد قامت الصلاة، فهو بالخيار إن شاء مشي، وإن شاء وقف، إماماً كان أو غيره، وبه أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث. وما روي عن أبي يوسف أصح، كذا في البدائع. واقتصر في الخلاصة على قول الفقيهين من غير إسناد لأحد.

They are disliked for Zuhr on Friday in the congregational city. If the pause is long, he repeats (the adhan). And al-Kamal said: Clearing the throat is disliked during adhan and iqama, because it is an innovation. End. And it is an answer regarding the mu'adhdhin's prayer upon the Prophet (ﷺ) at the beginning of the iqama, because it is an innovation.
Note: The scholars differed whether he completes the iqama in his place or completes it while walking. Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Nur al-Idah, which the author of Imdad al-Fattah is explaining. The matn states: 'They are disliked for Zuhr on Friday in the congregational city.' The commentator explains that 'they' refers to both adhan and iqama. The proof for this is a narration from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that it is disliked. The ruling applies to both the excused person (such as a traveler) and others. The commentator then adds a note about the issue of clearing the throat during adhan, citing al-Kamal that it is disliked as an innovation, and this also addresses the practice of some mu'adhdhins who send salawat on the Prophet at the beginning of iqama. Another note deals with whether the mu'adhdhin should complete the iqama standing in one place or while walking. There are three positions: (1) complete it standing, (2) complete it walking, (3) at the phrase 'qad qamat al-salah' he may choose. The author mentions that the narration from Abu Yusuf (walking) is more correct. The main ruling is then reaffirmed, with the additional detail that it includes the excused person, but al-Bahr reports from al-Tafariq an exception for the excused person who may pray with adhan and iqama, though congregation is not recommended. This exception conflicts with the narration from Ali. The Hanafi school follows the narration from Ali as the relied-upon position, so the general ruling is makruh.

Key Terms
المصر (al-misr): A major city where Friday prayer is obligatory and congregational prayers are established.
التنحنح (al-tanahnuh): Clearing the throat deliberately during adhan or iqama.
المعذور (al-ma'dhur): The excused person, e.g., a traveler, prisoner, or one who missed Friday due to a valid excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Adhan and iqama for Zuhr on Friday in a city where Friday is held is disliked for all, including the excused, based on a narration from Ali (RA).

Salah — Prayer

Adhan and Iqama for Missed Prayers: Rulings and Evidence
Ruling with proof on adhan/iqama for missed prayers, including intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqama for missed prayers, explain the evidence from the hadith of al-Ta'ris, and apply the ruling when making up multiple prayers in one session.

Core Idea
Adhan and iqama for missed prayers are Sunnah, not wajib; first missed prayer gets both, subsequent ones at least iqama.

When making up missed prayers, one might wonder whether adhan and iqama are needed. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position, based on the Prophet's actions when he overslept Fajr and during the Battle of the Trench. You will learn the ruling, the evidence, and how it applies when making up multiple prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is calling adhan and iqama for missed prayers. The Hanafi school considers it Sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah), not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of the night of al-Ta'ris, where the Prophet ordered Bilal to call adhan and iqama for the missed Fajr. Additional evidence comes from the Day of al-Ahzab.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's explicit action and his statement 'let him pray it as he would pray it in its time' indicate that the sunan of the prayer, including adhan and iqama, are to be preserved in qada.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a difference within the Hanafi school on whether to call adhan for each subsequent missed prayer in the same sitting. Some narrations have adhan for each, others only iqama after the first.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Al-Bada'i' prefers the narration with adhan for each (ziyada) as it is better in worship. The mufta bihi is adhan+iqama for the first, and at least iqama for each subsequent; adhan for later is recommended but not required.

(ويُؤَذِّنُ للفائتة ويُقيمُ)؛ لأنه صلى الله عليه وسلم قَضَى الفَجْرَ غَدَاةَ ليلة التعريس بأذان وإقامة. والإطلاق يشمل القضاء في المسجد والبيت ولكن في المجتبى معزياً إلى الحلواني أنه سنة القضاء في البيوت دون المساجد، فإن فيه تشويهاً وتغليظاً. انتهى. قال صاحب البحر: وإذا كانوا قد صرحوا بأن الفائتة لا تقضى في المسجد، لما فيه من إظهار التكاسل في إخراج الصلاة عن وقتها، فالواجب الإخفاء في الأذان للفائتة في المسجد، وهو أولى بالمنع، انتهى.
(1) عن زيد بن أسلم قال: عرس رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ليلة بطريق مكة. ووكل بلالاً أن يوقظهم للصلاة فـرقـد بـلال، ورقـدوا حتى استيقظوا وقد طلعت عليهم الشمس وقد فزعوا فأمرهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يركبوا حتى يخرجوا من ذلك الوادي وقال: إن هذا وادٍ به شيطان فركبوا حتى خرجوا من ذلك الوادي ثم أمرهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن ينزلوا وأن يتوضؤوا وأمر بلالاً أن ينادي للصلاة، ويقيم فصلى رسول الله بالناس وقد رأى من فزعهم فقال: يا أيها الناس إن الله قبض أرواحنا ولو شاء لردها إلينا في حين غير هذا، فإذا رقد أحدكم عن الصلاة أو نسيها ثم فزع إليها فليصلها كما كان يصليها في وقتها ثم التفت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى أبي بكر الصديق فقال: إن الشيطان أتي بلالاً وهو قائم يصلي فأضجعه ثم لم يزل يهدئه كما يهدأ الصبي حتى نـام ثم دعا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بلالاً فأخبر بلال رسول الله مثل الذي أخبر به رسول الله أبا بكر فقال أبو بكر: أشهد أنك رسول الله، أخرجه مالك في الموطأ.
وكذا لأُولى الفوائتِ. وكُرَهَ تَرْكُ الإقامة دونَ الأذانِ في البواقي، إنِ اتَّحد مجلس القضاء. وإذا سمع المسنون منه أَمْسَكَ.
لكن إذا كان التفويت لأمر عام، فالأذان في المسجد لا يكره، لانتفاء العلة، كفعلـه غـداة ليلة التعريس، قال الكمال: وقد صح. وروى أصحاب الإملاء عن أبي يوسف بإسناده إلى رسول الله: أنه حين شَغَلَهم الكفار قضاهن بأذان وإقامة، يعني الكل من الأربع صلوات، (وَكَذَا) يؤذن ويقيم (لأُولَى الفوائتِ)، ويؤذن لكل واحد بعدها، ويقيم على الوجه الأكمل، كمـا فـعـلـه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم حين شغله الكفار يوم الأحزاب عن أربع صلوات الظهر والعصر والمغرب والعشاء، فقضاهن مرتباً على الولاء وأمر بلالاً أن يؤذن، ويقيم لكل واحدة منهن. كذا في الفتح.
(وكُرِهَ ترك الإقامة دون الأذانِ في البَوَاقِي من الفوائت إنِ اتَّحد مجلس القضاء)؛ لاتفاق الروايات على أنَّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أتى بالإقامة في جميع الصلوات التي قضاها، فتكره مخالفته، بخلاف ترك الأذان فيما بقي، إن أتى به فحسن، وإلا فهو جائز، لأنه قد اختلفت الروايات في قضاء رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الصلوات التي فاتته يوم الخندق، ويسمى يوم الأحزاب، وكان في السنة الرابعة من الهجرة. في بعض الروايات: أنه أمر بلالاً فأذن وأقام لكل صلاة على ما رويناه عن الكمال. وفي بعضها: أنه اقتصر على الإقامة لكل صلاة بعد الأذان والإقامة في الأولى، وعليه اقتصر الزيلعي. قال في البدائع بعد تنبيهه على اختلاف الرواية: ولاشك أن الأخذ برواية الزيادة أولى، خصوصاً في باب العبادات. انتهى. وقد اختلف في الذي فاته في الموطأ الظهر والعصر، وفي البخاري فاته العصر فقط. والذي رواه الكمال وغيره أربع قد علمتها.
(وإذا سمع أحد المسنونَ مِنْهُ)، أي الأذان، وهو ما لا لحن فيه ولا تلحين، (أَمْسَكَ) حتى عن التلاوة ليجيب المؤذن، ولو في المسجد كما قال الكمال في العيون: قارئ سمع النداء فالأفضل أن يمسك ويستمع. وبه ورد الأثر. وفي فوائد الرستغفني يمضي في قراءته إن كان في المسجد، وإن كان في بيته، فكذلك إن لم يكن أذان مسجده. انتهى. زاد في مجمع الروايات كذا ذكره الإمام التمرتاشي. وإذا كان يتكلم في الفقه.
(He calls adhan for the missed prayer and establishes iqama) because the Prophet (ﷺ) made up the Fajr on the morning of the night of al-Ta'ris with adhan and iqama. The absolute wording includes making it up in the mosque and at home, but in al-Mujtaba, attributed to al-Halwani, it is Sunnah to make it up at home, not in mosques, for that involves distortion and severity. End. The author of al-Bahr said: Since they explicitly stated that the missed prayer is not made up in the mosque, due to the display of laziness in taking the prayer out of its time, then it is obligatory to conceal the adhan for the missed prayer in the mosque, and it is more deserving of prohibition. End.
(1) From Zaid ibn Aslam: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) camped one night on the road to Mecca. He appointed Bilal to wake them for prayer. Bilal slept, and they slept until they woke up and the sun had risen upon them, and they were alarmed. The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) ordered them to ride until they left that valley and said: "This is a valley with a devil." So they rode until they left that valley, then he ordered them to descend, perform wudu, and ordered Bilal to call the adhan and iqama. Then he led the people in prayer. Seeing their alarm, he said: "O people, Allah took our souls, and if He willed, He would have returned them to us at another time. So if any of you oversleeps prayer or forgets it, then let him pray it as he would pray it in its time." Then he turned to Abu Bakr al-Siddiq and said: "The devil came to Bilal while he was standing in prayer and laid him down, and he continued to soothe him as a child is soothed until he slept." Then he called Bilal and he informed him similar to what he had informed Abu Bakr. Abu Bakr said: "I bear witness that you are the Messenger of Allah." Recorded by Malik in al-Muwatta.
Similarly for the first of the missed prayers. And it is disliked to leave the iqama without the adhan in the remaining (missed prayers) if the place of making them up is one. And when one hears the proper (adhan), he desists.
But if the loss was due to a general reason, then the adhan in the mosque is not disliked, because the reason is absent, like his action on the morning of the night of al-Ta'ris. Al-Kamal said: It is authentic. And the companions of al-Imla narrated from Abu Yusuf with his chain to the Messenger of Allah: that when the disbelievers preoccupied him, he made them up with adhan and iqama, meaning all four prayers. (And likewise) he calls adhan and iqama (for the first of the missed prayers), and he calls adhan for each one after it, and establishes iqama in the most complete manner, as the Prophet (ﷺ) did when the disbelievers preoccupied him on the Day of al-Ahzab from four prayers: Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha. He made them up in order and ordered Bilal to call adhan and iqama for each one. So in al-Fath.
(And it is disliked to leave the iqama without the adhan in the remaining missed prayers if the place of making them up is one) because the narrations agree that the Prophet (ﷺ) performed the iqama in all the prayers he made up. So opposing it is disliked. Unlike leaving the adhan in the remaining (prayers); if he does it, it is good, otherwise it is permissible, because the narrations differ regarding the Messenger of Allah's (ﷺ) making up the prayers he missed on the Day of al-Khandaq, also called the Day of al-Ahzab, which was in the fourth year of the Hijra. In some narrations: he ordered Bilal to call adhan and iqama for each prayer, as we narrated from al-Kamal. In others: he restricted to iqama for each prayer after the adhan and iqama for the first, and al-Zayla'i relied on this. Al-Bada'i' said after noting the difference: There is no doubt that taking the narration of excess (adhan) is better, especially in the chapter of acts of worship. End. And there is disagreement about what he missed: in al-Muwatta, it was Zuhr and Asr; in al-Bukhari, he missed only Asr. And what al-Kamal and others narrated is four, as you know.
(And when one hears the proper from it), i.e., the adhan, which is without error or melody, (he desists) even from recitation to respond to the mu'adhdhin, even in the mosque, as al-Kamal said in al-Uyun: A reciter who hears the call, the best is to stop and listen. And the tradition supports this. In Fawa'id al-Rustaghfani, he continues his recitation if he is in the mosque, and likewise if he is in his house, similarly if it is not the adhan of his mosque. End. Added in Majma' al-Riwayat, as mentioned by Imam al-Tamartashi. And if he is speaking about fiqh.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding adhan and iqama for missed prayers. The matn states that one should call adhan and establish iqama for the missed prayer. The proof is the hadith of the night of al-Ta'ris (camping), where the Prophet (ﷺ) made up Fajr prayer after oversleeping and ordered Bilal to call adhan and iqama. The commentary notes that this absolute wording includes making up the prayer in the mosque or at home, but some scholars consider it Sunnah to do it at home to avoid the appearance of negligence. However, if the missed prayer is due to a general reason (like war), then adhan in the mosque is not disliked, as in the hadith. The passage then details: for the first missed prayer, one does adhan and iqama; for subsequent prayers in the same sitting, it is disliked to leave the iqama (i.e., one should still do iqama for each), but leaving the adhan for the later ones is permissible. This is because there is disagreement in the narrations about the Prophet's practice when he missed four prayers on the Day of al-Ahzab. Some narrations say he did adhan and iqama for each; others say he did adhan and iqama only for the first and then iqama for the rest. The relied-upon position (as per al-Bada'i') is to take the narration with the extra adhan, as it is better for acts of worship. Finally, the passage covers the etiquette of hearing the adhan: when one hears the proper adhan (without melody or error), one should stop even from reciting Quran to respond to it, whether in the mosque or at home, with some differences reported. The commentary by the author of Imdad al-Fattah clarifies these rulings as the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
الفائتة (al-fa'itah): A prayer that was missed and is being made up (qada).
المسنون من الأذان (al-masnun min al-adhan): The proper, sunnah-based adhan without melodic alteration or errors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on calling adhan for the second missed prayer when making up multiple prayers in one sitting?
A) It is obligatory (wajib).
B) It is disliked (makruh).
C) It is recommended (mustahabb) but not required.
D) It is prohibited (haram).

Key Takeaway
The sunnah for missed prayers is to include adhan and iqama for the first, and at least iqama for subsequent, with the preferred practice to call adhan for all.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Responding to the Hay'alah with Hawqalah
Ruling and proof for saying la hawla wa la quwwata at hay'alah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on responding to the hay'alah in the adhan and explain the proof from the hadith of Umar.

Core Idea
At the hay'alah, say hawqalah, not repetition, per the Prophet's instruction to Umar.

In the adhan, the mu'adhdhin calls people to prayer with the phrases 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'Hayya 'ala al-falah'. These are not praises but summons, and the Hanafi school teaches a unique response: instead of repeating them, you say 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' (hawqalah). This lesson unpacks the evidence from the hadith of Umar and the reasoning behind this distinction, as well as the inter-madhhab disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds about responding to the hay'alah. The listener should say 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' (hawqalah) instead of repeating the words of the mu'adhdhin.
This applies to both hay'alatayn: 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'Hayya 'ala al-falah'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Shafi'i school holds that the listener should repeat the hay'alah exactly as said by the mu'adhdhin, based on the general command to say similar.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof is the general hadith: 'When you hear the mu'adhdhin, say similar to what he says.' This includes all phrases of the adhan.
Also, they cite the hadith of Abu Umama which encourages repeating the hay'alah.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the general command is specified by the hadith of Umar, where the Prophet explicitly instructed to say hawqalah at the hay'alah. Repeating the hay'alah would resemble mockery because it is a command, not a dhikr.
The Hanafi usul principle: a specific textual proof (khas) can specify a general (amm) even if later.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi followers say 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' at the hay'alah, while Shafi'i followers repeat the mu'adhdhin's words. Both are valid, but the Hanafi view is based on a direct prophetic instruction.

وقال مِثْلَهُ، وحَوْقَلَ فِي الخَيْعَلَتَيْن، حي أو في الأصول، فسمع، يجب عليه الإجابة. وإن سمعه وهو يمشي فالأولى أن يقف ساعة ويجيب، وإذا تعدد الأذان يجيب الأول. انتهى. (وَقَالَ) مجيباً له (مِثْلَهُ)، أي: مثل ألفاظه، (وَ) لكن (حَوْقَلَ)، أي قال: لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله أي لا حول لنا عن معصية، ولا قوة لنا على طاعة، إلا بفضل الله (في) سماعه ( الحَيْعَلَتَيْنِ)، وهما حي . على الصلاة . على الفلاح، لأنه لو قال مثلهما، صار كالمستهزئ، لأن من حكى لفظ الأمر بشيء كان مستهزئاً به، بخلاف سائر الكلمات، لأنها ثناء، وأما الحوقلـة عـنـد الحيعلتين فهو وإن خالف ظاهر قوله الله : « فَقُولُوا مِثْلَ مَا يَقُولُ ) (۳) لكنه ورد فيه حديث عمر . مُفَسِّر لذلك، عن عمر بن الخطاب الله قال : « قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : إِذَا قَالَ الْمُؤَذِّنُ: اللَّهُ أَكْبَرُ، اللَّهُ أَكْبَرُ، فَقَالَ: أحَدُكُمْ اللهُ أَكْبَرُ اللَّهُ أَكْبَرُ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: أَشْهَدُ أنْ لا إِلَهَ إِلا اللَّهُ، فَقَالَ: أَشْهَدُ أَنْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: أشْهَدُ أَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا رَسُولُ اللهِ، قَالَ: أَشْهَدُ أَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا رَسُولُ اللهِ، ثُمَّ قَالَ حَى عَلَى الصَّلاةِ، قَالَ: لا حَوْلَ وَلا قُوَّةَ إِلا بِاللهِ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: حَيَّ عَلَى الْفَلاح، قَالَ : لا حَوْلَ وَلا قُوَّةَ إِلا بِاللهِ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: الله أكبر، الله أَكْبَرُ، قَالَ: اللَّهُ أَكْبَرُ، اللَّهُ أَكْبَرُ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ، قَالَ: لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ مِنْ قَلْبِهِ دَخَلَ الْجَنَّةَ . رواه مسلم. فحملوا ذلك العام، -يعني: قولوا مثل ما يقول المؤذن على ما سوى هاتين الكلمتين، يعني: الحيْعَلتين، وهو غير جـار عـلـى قـاعدة، لأن عندنا المخصص الأول ما لم يكن متصلاً، لا يخصص، بل يعارض، فيجري حكم المعارضة أو يقدم العام، والحق الأول، وإنمـا قـدم الـعـام فـي مواضع لاقتضاء حكم المعارضة، ذلك في خصوص : تلك المواضع، وعلى قول من لم يشترط ذلك، فإنما يلزم التخصيص، إذا لم يكن الجمع، بأن تحقق معارضاً للعام في بعض الأفراد، بأن يوجب نفي الحكم المعلق بالعام عنها فيخرجها عنه، وها هنا لم يلزم من وعده لمــن أجــاب كذلك، وقال عند الحيعلة الحوقلة، ثم هلل في الآخر من قلبه بدخول الجنة، بقي أن يحيعل المجيب مطلقاً، ليكون مجيباً على الوجه المسنون وتعليل الحديث المذكور، بأن إعادة لفظ الحَيْعَلتين يشبه الاستهزاء، كما يفهم في الشاهد، بخلاف ما سوى الحيعلتين، فإنه ذكر يثاب عليه من قاله لا يتم إذ لا مانع من صحة اعتبار المجيب بهما، داعياً لنفسه، محركاً منها السواكن مخاطباً لها، فكيف وقد ورد في بعض الصور طلبها، أي: طلب النطق بالحيعلتين صريحاً. في مسند أبي يعلى عن أبي أمامة : « عـنــه ، إذا نــادى المُنَادِي  ِللصَّلاةِ فُتِحَتْ أبواب السَّمَاءِ، وَاسْتَجِيْبَ الدُّعاء، فيمَنْ نَزَلَ بِهِ كَرْبُ، أَو شِدَّةٌ، فَلْيَتحين المنادِي، إذا كبر، كبر، وإذا تشهد، تشهد ، وإذا قال: حيَّ على الصَّلاةِ، قال: حي على الصلاة، وإذا قال: حي على الفلاح، قال: حي على الفلاح. ثم يقول - يعني بعد ما يتمه، متابعاً - اللهم رب هذه الدعــوة الحق المستجابة إليه المستجاب لها، دعوة الحق، وكلمة التقوى، أحينا عليها، وأميتنـا عـلـيـهـا، وابعثنـا عليها، واجعلنا من خيارِ أهْلِهَا، مَحَيانا ومَماتنا، ثمَّ يسألُ الله تعالى حَاجَتَهُ ). رواه الطبراني في كتاب الدعاء، فساقه، ورواه الحاكم وقال : صحيح الإسناد. فهذا يفيد أن عموم الأول معتبر، أي: عموم قوله : ( إِذَا سَمِعْتُمُ الْمُؤَذَنَ فَقُولُوا مِثْلَ مَا يَقُولُ ) (۳). وقد رأينا من مشايخ السلوك مـن كـان يجمع بينهما، فيدعو نفسه بأن يقول: حيَّ على الصلاة، مرتين، حي على الفلاح، مرتين، بعد قول المؤذن، ثـــم يتبرأ من الحول والقوة فيقول: لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله ؛ ليعمل بالحديثين، وفي حديــث عـمـر وأبـي أمامة التنصيص على أن لا يسبق المؤذن، بل يعقب كل جملة منه بجملة منه. انتهى.
And he said similarly, and he said hawqalah at the two hay'alatayn, [regarding the one who hears], it is obligatory for him to respond. If he hears it while walking, it is better to stop for a moment and respond. If there are multiple adhans, he responds to the first. End. And he said, responding to him, similarly, i.e., like his words, but he hawqala, i.e., he said: 'There is no power and no strength except with Allah' at hearing the two hay'alatayn, which are: 'Come to prayer, come to success', because if he said similar to them, he would become like a mocker, for whoever repeats the wording of a command to something is mocking it, unlike other words, for they are praise. As for saying hawqalah at the hay'alatayn, even though it contradicts the apparent meaning of His saying: 'So say similar to what he says', but the hadith of Umar came as an explanation of that: from Umar ibn al-Khattab, he said: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: When the mu'adhdhin says: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, and one of you says: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, then he says: I bear witness that there is no god but Allah, and he says: I bear witness that there is no god but Allah, then he says: I bear witness that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, and he says: I bear witness that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, then he says: Come to prayer, and he says: There is no power and no strength except with Allah, then he says: Come to success, and he says: There is no power and no strength except with Allah, then he says: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, and he says: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, then he says: There is no god but Allah, and he says: There is no god but Allah, from his heart, enters Paradise.' Narrated by Muslim. So they carried that general statement—meaning: say similar to what the mu'adhdhin says—to everything other than these two words, meaning the hay'alatayn. And this is not in accordance with the principle, because according to us, the first specifier, if it is not connected, does not specify but rather conflicts, so the rule of conflict applies or the general takes precedence, and the first is correct. The general is given precedence in some places due to the requirement of conflict, specifically in those places. According to the one who does not stipulate that, specification is necessary only if combination is not possible, as it conflicts with the general in some individuals, necessitating the negation of the ruling attached to the general for them, thereby excluding them. Here, from His promise to whoever responds thus, and says hawqalah at the hay'alah, then says tahlil at the end from his heart, entering Paradise, it remains that the responder should say hay'alah absolutely, to respond in the sunna manner. The reasoning of the mentioned hadith that repeating the wording of the hay'alatayn resembles mockery, as understood in the [legal] witness, unlike other than the hay'alatayn, for they are remembrance that one is rewarded for saying—this does not stand, for there is no impediment to the correctness of considering the responder by them, calling to himself, moving the saakinah letters, addressing her. How can that be, when it has been reported in some forms to demand them, i.e., clear demand to utter the hay'alatayn? In the Musnad of Abu Ya'la from Abu Umama: 'When the caller calls for prayer, the doors of heaven are opened and supplication is answered. So whoever has a distress or hardship, let him await the caller: when he says takbir, he says takbir; when he says tashahhud, he says tashahhud; when he says Hayya 'ala al-salah, he says Hayya 'ala al-salah; when he says Hayya 'ala al-falah, he says Hayya 'ala al-falah. Then he says—after completing it, following—O Allah, Lord of this complete call, and the prayer that is established, grant Muhammad the intercession and virtue, and raise him to the praised station which You have promised him...' He narrated it. This indicates that the generality of the first is considered, i.e., the generality of his saying: 'When you hear the mu'adhdhin, say similar to what he says.' And we have seen some of the shaykhs of suluk who combined both: he calls to himself by saying: Hayya 'ala al-salah twice, Hayya 'ala al-falah twice, after the mu'adhdhin's saying, then he disavows power and strength by saying: There is no power and no strength except with Allah, to act on both hadiths. And in the hadith of Umar and Abu Umama, the explicit text is that one should not precede the mu'adhdhin, but should follow every sentence with a sentence from him. End.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the proper response to the hay'alah (حي على الصلاة, حي على الفلاح) in the adhan. The Hanafi position, derived from the hadith of Umar (narrated by Muslim), is that the responder should say 'لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله' (hawqalah) instead of repeating the hay'alah. The reason is that repeating the command-like phrases could resemble mockery. The text acknowledges that this seems to contradict the general command to say similar to what the mu'adhdhin says, but the hadith of Umar specifies and explains the general command. The text then discusses the principle of takhsis (specification) in usul al-fiqh, arguing that the general command is not absolutely overridden but is specified by the hadith. It also mentions the hadith of Abu Umama, which seems to support repeating the hay'alah, leading some mashayikh to combine both by saying the hay'alah softly and then the hawqalah. The relied-upon Hanafi position is to say hawqalah at the hay'alah, though some Shafi'is hold that repeating the hay'alah is correct.

Key Terms
الحَيْعَلَتَيْن (al-hay'alatayn): The two phrases 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'Hayya 'ala al-falah' in the adhan.
الحَوْقَلَة (al-hawqalah): Saying 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' (there is no power and no strength except with Allah).
التَّخْصِيص (al-takhsis): Specification of a general ruling by a specific proof. Here, the general command to repeat is specified by the hadith of Umar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should one say when the mu'adhdhin says 'Hayya 'ala al-salah'?
A) Repeat the same words as the mu'adhdhin.
B) Say 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah'.
C) Remain silent.
D) Say 'sadaqta wa bararta'.

Key Takeaway
At the hay'alah in the adhan, the Hanafi school teaches to say 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' (hawqalah), based on the specific hadith of Umar which specifies the general command to repeat.

Situations Where Responding to the Adhan is Suspended
Lists situations where responding to the adhan is suspended

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the situations where responding to the adhan is suspended and explain why a junub may respond while a ha'idh may not.

Core Idea
Responding to the adhan is suspended during prayer, khutbah, eating—yet a junub responds, while a ha'idh does not.

The adhan calls believers to prayer, and it is generally recommended to respond by repeating its words. However, the Hanafi school identifies specific situations where this response is not performed. This passage from Nur al-Idah lists those situations and clarifies the rulings for those in states of impurity.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Recognize that responding to the adhan is normally recommended (mandub) or wajib according to some, but here we learn exceptions.
2
List the suspended situations
Read the text and enumerate: prayer (even janazah), khutbah (and listening), seasonal sermons, learning/teaching knowledge, eating, intercourse, relieving oneself.
These are all acts that occupy the person.
3
Distinguish between junub and ha'idh
The text says a junub may respond because the response is not an act of worship requiring purity. But a ha'idh (and nufasa') do not respond because they are not qualified for the prayer itself.
The ruling differs because the ha'idh cannot pray even after purification until her period ends.
4
Apply the principle
Reflect: inability to perform the actual prayer removes the obligation to respond verbally. A junub can pray after ghusl, so he is still addressed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجيب في مواطن وهي: الصلاة ولــو جـنــازة، والخطبة واستماعها، وخطب الموسم، وتعلم العلم، وتعليمه، والأكل، والجماع، وقضاء الحاجة. ويجيب الجنب، لأنها ليست أذاناً)، ونص على أن الحائض والنفساء لا تجيب، والفرق أنهما ليستا من أهل الإجابة بالفعل، لعدم قدرتهما عليه، فكذا بالقول بخلاف الجنب فإنه مخاطب بالصلاة، فيجيب بالفعل بعد تطهره.
And he does not respond in situations, which are: prayer, even janazah prayer; the khutbah and listening to it; the sermons of the season; learning knowledge and teaching it; eating; intercourse; and answering the call of nature. And the junub responds, because it is not an adhan. And it is explicitly stated that the ha'idh and nufasa' do not respond. The difference is that they are not qualified for response by action due to their inability, so also by speech. Contrary to the junub, for he is addressed with prayer, so he responds by action after his purification.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage enumerates the situations where responding to the adhan is not prescribed. It is a ruling statement without explicit proofs. The list includes: prayer (even funeral prayer), delivering or listening to the khutbah, sermons of 'Eid or season, studying or teaching knowledge, eating, sexual intercourse, and relieving oneself. The text then addresses the state of janabah: a junub person may respond because his state does not prevent him from speaking the words, unlike the ha'idh (menstruating woman) and nufasa' (postpartum woman), who are not qualified to respond by action (since they cannot pray) and thus should not respond by speech either. This reflects the Hanafi principle that response to the adhan is a form of worship, and those unable to perform the physical worship should also refrain from the verbal response.

Key Terms
الجُنُب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
الحَائِض (al-ha'idh): A menstruating woman.
النُّفَسَاء (al-nufasa'): A woman in the postpartum period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
May a person who is junub respond to the adhan?
A) Yes, because the response is verbal and does not require purity.
B) No, because junub is a state of impurity and all worship is prohibited.
C) Only if he silently repeats the words.
D) Only if he has made wudu.

Key Takeaway
Responding to the adhan is suspended during specific acts; a junub may still respond but a ha'idh may not, due to their ability to perform the prayer.

Responding to the Taswib in Fajr Adhan
Ruling on responding to the Fajr adhan taswib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on responding to 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' and apply the underlying principle of avoiding mockery.

Core Idea
Do not repeat the mu'adhdhin's statement; instead affirm it to avoid mockery.

This lesson addresses the specific response to the taswib phrase in the Fajr adhan. Unlike the hay'alah which is repeated, the Hanafi school teaches that the listener should not repeat 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' because it resembles mockery. Instead, one says a phrase of affirmation.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the taswib
The phrase 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' is called taswib and is part of the Fajr adhan in the Hanafi school.
This phrase is not said in other adhans.
2
Identify the prohibition of repetition
Repeating the exact phrase could be seen as mocking since it is a statement of fact rather than a call.
This is based on avoiding resemblance to mockery (al-tahāshī ʿan mā yushbihu al-istihzāʾ).
3
Learn the prescribed responses
The listener may say 'sadaqta wa bararta' (you have spoken truth and done good) or 'ma sha' Allah kana wa ma lam yasha' lam yakun' (whatever Allah wills happens, whatever He does not will does not happen).
Both are recommended (mustahabb).
4
Understand the evidence
These responses are reported from some Salaf and mentioned in works like al-Tajnis and al-Mazid.
The ruling is based on weak evidence but is the practice of the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالَ: صَدَقْتَ وَبَرَرْت)، بفتح الراء الأولى، وكسرها، مروي ذلك عـن بعـض السلف، كذا في التجنيس والمزيد » ، (أو ) يقول: (مَا شَاءَ اللهُ كان، وما لم يشأ الله لم يكن، (عند قول المؤذنِ) في أذان الفجر : ( الصلاة خير من النَّوم، لما ذكرناه، تحاشياً عما يشبه الاستهزاء.
And he said: 'You have spoken truth and you have done good' (with fatha on the first ra and kasra, narrated from some Salaf), even as in al-Tajnis and al-Mazid. Or he says: 'Whatever Allah wills will be, and whatever He does not will will not be,' when the mu'adhdhin says in the Fajr adhan: 'Prayer is better than sleep,' for the reason we mentioned, to avoid what resembles mockery.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for responding to the specific phrase in the Fajr adhan: 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm'. Unlike the hay'alah, here the listener should not repeat the phrase because it could be seen as mocking (since it is a statement of fact, not a call). Instead, the prescribed responses are either 'sadaqta wa bararta' (you have spoken truth and done good) or 'ma sha' Allah kana wa ma lam yasha' lam yakun' (whatever Allah wills happens, whatever He does not will does not happen). The reason given is to avoid any resemblance to mockery, consistent with the earlier reasoning for the hay'alah. This ruling is based on reports from some Salaf and is recorded in works like al-Tajnis and al-Mazid.

Key Terms
التَّثْوِيب (al-tathwib): The phrase 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' said in the Fajr adhan.
صَدَقْتَ وَبَرَرْت (sadaqta wa bararta): A phrase meaning 'You have spoken truth and you have done good', said in response to the taswib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a listener say when the mu'adhdhin says 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm'?
A) Repeat the same phrase.
B) Say 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah'.
C) Say 'sadaqta wa bararta' or 'ma sha' Allah'.
D) Remain silent.

Key Takeaway
When the mu'adhdhin says 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm', the listener should respond with 'sadaqta wa bararta' or 'ma sha' Allah' to avoid resembling mockery.
