Ruling on Responding to the Adhan: Wajib or Mustahabb?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on verbal response to adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on responding to the adhan, identify their proofs, and explain why the preponderant position is mustahabb.

Core Idea
Repeating the adhan is mustahabb, not wajib; the imperative is overridden by the promise of forgiveness.

This passage navigates an internal Hanafi debate over the legal weight of responding to the adhan verbally. While some early authorities considered it obligatory (wajib), the school's later consensus settled on recommendation (mustahabb). You will learn to trace the arguments from the primary texts and understand the reasoning behind the tarjih.

Guided Path
1
State the preponderant Hanafi position
Identify that the relied-upon ruling (mufta bihi) is mustahabb: verbal repetition of the adhan is recommended but not obligatory.
This is the view of al-Hidayah, al-Halwani, and the author of this text.
2
Identify the opposing view within the school
Some Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Bada'i', al-Kamal, al-Khulasah) considered it wajib, citing the command 'say similar' and the 'four acts of harshness' hadith.
The opposing view does not consider omission sinful, however.
3
Examine the opposing proof
The imperative 'qulu' (say) is taken at face value; the harshness hadith lists 'hearing the adhan and not responding' as harshness.
The harshness hadith is ambiguous: does it mean verbal or physical response?
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The command is contextualized by the forgiveness hadith ('Whoever says… is forgiven') which indicates reward, not punishment. The harshness hadith is interpreted as referring to coming to the mosque (foot response), because iqamah is included yet its verbal response is not wajib.
Thus, the imperative is not absolute; it is overridden by the context of forgiveness.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If wajib, leaving it would be sinful; if mustahabb, there is no sin but loss of reward. The mufta bihi (mustahabb) means no sin for omission.
This practical consequence guides fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه: اختلفت عبارة أئمتنا رحمهم الله في حكم الإجابة، صرح بالوجوب في « البدائع»، قال: الواجب على السامعين عند الأذان الإجابة، لما روي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: «أربعٌ مِنَ الجَفَاءِ: مَنْ بَالَ قَائِمَاً، وَمَنْ مَسَحَ جَبْهَتَهُ قَبْلَ الفَرَاغِ مِنَ الصَّلاةِ، وَمَنْ سَمِعَ الأذان ولمْ يُجب، ومَنْ سَمِعَ ذكري ولم يصل علي » ) . انتهى. وقال « الكمال » : ظاهر « الخلاصة»، و « الفتاوى»، و« التحفة»، وجوبها. وقـــال الحلواني»: الإجابة بالقدم، فلو أجاب بلسانه ولم يمش لا يكون مجيباً، ولو كان في المسجد، فليس عليه أن يجيب باللسان حاصله ففي وجوب الإجابة باللسان، وبه صرح جماعة، وأنه مستحب، قالوا: إن قال نال الثواب الموعود، وإلا لم ينل، أما أنه يأثم، أو يـكــره فـلا. انتهى. قلت: ومنهم صاحب « الهداية » ، قال في ( التجنيس والمزيد » : ويستحب لمن سمع الأذان أن يقول مثل ما يقول المؤذن، لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «مَنْ قَالَ مِثْلَ مَا يَقُولُ المُؤذِّنُ غُفِرَ لَهُ». انتهى. ثم قال الله: وفي « التجنيس» لا يكره الكلام عند الأذان بالإجماع، استدلالاً باختلاف أصحابنا في كراهية الكلام في أذان الخطبة يوم الجمعة، فإن أبا حنيفة رحمه الله، إنمـا قــــال بالكراهية، لأنه يلحق هذه الحالة بحالة الخطبة، فكان هذا اتفاقاً على أنه لا يـكــره الـكــلام فـي غـيـر هذه الحالة، كذا ذكر شمس الأئمة السرخسي فيما قرؤوا عليه. انتهى. ثم عقبه الكمال بقوله: لكن ظاهر الأمر في قوله : ( إِذَا سَمِعْتُمُ الْمُؤَدِّنَ فَقُولُوا مِثْلَ مَا يَقُولُ) الوجوب، إذ لا تظهر قرينة تصرفه عنه، بل ربما يظهر استنكار تركه، لأنه يشبه عدم الالتفات إليه والتشاغل عنه. انتهى. إلا إذا أجاب بالفعل، كما بحثه العلامة الشيخ علي المقدسي رحمه الله، ثم قال ( الكمال » : وفي « التحفة» ينبغي أن لا يتكلم، ولا يشتغل بشيء حال الأذان والإقامة. وفي النهاية » : يجب عليهم الإجابة لقوله : ( أربع مِنَ الجَفَاءِ » ) ومن جملتها ومَنْ سَمِعَ الأذَانَ أوِ الإِقَامَةِ وَلَمْ يُجِبْ» انتهى. وهـو غير صريح في إجابة اللسان، إذ يجوز كون المراد الإجابة بالإتيان إلى الصلاة، وإلا لكان جواب الإقامة واجباً، ولم يعلم فيه عنهم إلا أنه مستحب، والله أعلم. قلت: إلا أن الإقامة لم تذكر في الحديث على ما قدمناه عن ( البدائع » ، فيكون صريحاً في الإجابة باللسان.
Warning: The statements of our imams (may Allah have mercy on them) differed regarding the ruling of responding (to the adhan). In al-Bada'i', obligation was explicitly stated: It is obligatory upon the listeners at the time of the adhan to respond, due to what was narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There are four acts of harshness: urinating while standing, wiping the forehead before finishing the prayer, hearing the adhan and not responding, and hearing my mention and not sending blessings upon me.' End quote. Al-Kamal said: The apparent meaning of al-Khulasah, al-Fatawa, and al-Tuhfah is that it is obligatory. Al-Halwani said: Responding is with the feet; if one responds with the tongue but does not walk, he is not considered a responder, and if he is in the mosque, he does not have to respond with the tongue. In summary, regarding the obligation of responding with the tongue, a group explicitly stated it, and that it is recommended (mustahabb). They said: If he says it, he obtains the promised reward; otherwise he does not, but he is not sinful or disliked. End quote. I (the author) say: Among them is the author of al-Hidayah, who said in al-Tajnisi wal-Mazid: It is recommended for one who hears the adhan to say similar to what the mu'adhdhin says, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever says similar to what the mu'adhdhin says, he is forgiven.' End quote. Then he said: And in al-Tajnis, speaking during the adhan is not disliked by consensus, using as evidence the disagreement of our companions regarding the dislike of speaking during the adhan of the Friday sermon. Abu Hanifah (may Allah have mercy on him) only said it is disliked because he likens this situation to the sermon, so this is agreement that speaking is not disliked in other situations. As Shams al-A'imah al-Sarakhsi mentioned in what they read before him. End quote. Then al-Kamal followed it by saying: But the apparent command in his statement 'When you hear the mu'adhdhin, say similar to what he says' indicates obligation, since there is no context to divert it, rather leaving it seems objectionable because it resembles disregard and inattention. End quote. Unless one responds with action, as researched by Shaykh Ali al-Maqdisi. Then al-Kamal said: In al-Tuhfah, one should not speak or engage in anything during the adhan and iqamah. In al-Nihayah: It is obligatory upon them to respond due to his statement: 'Four acts of harshness,' including 'whoever hears the adhan or the iqamah and does not respond.' End quote. This is not explicit regarding the tongue response, because it is possible that the intended meaning is responding by coming to prayer; otherwise the response to the iqamah would be obligatory, and we do not know from them except that it is recommended. And Allah knows best. I say: Except that the iqamah was not mentioned in the hadith according to what we presented from al-Bada'i', so it is explicit about responding with the tongue.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on responding to the adhan verbally by repeating the mu'adhdhin's words. The author presents differing views from Hanafi sources: Al-Bada'i' states it is wajib, citing a hadith listing four acts of harshness, including not responding to the adhan. Al-Kamal notes that al-Khulasah, al-Fatawa, and al-Tuhfah also indicate obligation. However, al-Halwani distinguishes between foot response (going to the mosque) and tongue response, stating that only foot response counts; if one responds with the tongue only, he is not considered a responder. A group says tongue response is mustahabb (recommended) and not sinful if omitted. The author of al-Hidayah explicitly says it is mustahabb, supported by a hadith promising forgiveness. There is consensus that speaking during the adhan is not disliked except during the Friday sermon adhan due to its connection to the khutbah. Al-Kamal argues that the command 'say similar to what he says' prima facie indicates obligation, as there is no contrary context, and leaving it appears like disregard. However, the author counters that the hadith 'four acts of harshness' may refer to coming to the mosque (foot response), not tongue response, as evidenced by the fact that the iqamah is also mentioned in that hadith but responding to iqamah with tongue is only mustahabb, not wajib. The author concludes that since the iqamah is not in the hadith as per al-Bada'i', the hadith is explicit about tongue response. Yet the preponderant view in the school is mustahabb, as the text indicates with 'wa Allah a'lam' and the earlier statements. The mufta bihi position is that verbal repetition is mustahabb, not wajib.

Key Terms
الإجابة (al-ijaabah): Responding to the adhan, either verbally by repeating the mu'adhdhin's words or physically by going to the mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preponderant Hanafi view, what is the ruling on verbally repeating the adhan?
A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Mustahabb (recommended)
C) Makruh (disliked)
D) Haram (forbidden)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon view is that verbal response to the adhan is mustahabb, not wajib, as the evidence for obligation is ambiguous and the forgiveness hadith indicates recommendation.

Supplication After the Adhan (al-Waseelah)
Describes the recommended supplication after the adhan, with proofs from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the supplication after the adhan, recite its prescribed wording, and identify its proofs from authentic hadith.

Core Idea
The supplication after the adhan is a confirmed sunnah, asking for al-Waseelah for the Prophet.

After the mu'adhdhin completes the call to prayer, the Hanafi school recommends a beautiful supplication: asking Allah to grant the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) a special station in Paradise called al-Waseelah. This lesson unpacks the exact wording, the hadith supporting it, and the reward promised for those who recite it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the text describes a recommended supplication after the adhan. Determine its legal status in the Hanafi school.
The ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib.
2
Examine the prescribed wording
Read the Arabic text of the supplication as transmitted from Jabir (RA): 'Allahumma Rabba hadhihi ad-da‘wati at-tammah...' Understand the key phrases: al-Waseelah, al-Fadilah, al-Maqam al-Mahmud.
The wording is established through authentic hadith.
3
Analyze the dalil (proof)
Identify the hadiths quoted: from Ibn Umar (command to ask for al-Waseelah), from Jabir (exact wording), from Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas (additional testimony), and from Ibn Mas'ud (ask after saying like the mu'adhdhin). Understand how each supports the recommended practice.
The dalil is ahad but very authentic; the meaning is clear (dalalah qati'ah).
4
Note the ikhtilaf on response
The text mentions al-Kamal's inclination toward the obligation of responding to the adhan. Recognize that this is a separate issue; the supplication itself is universally considered sunnah.
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that repeating after the mu'adhdhin is sunnah, not wajib.
5
Understand the reward
The hadith promises intercession for the one who asks for al-Waseelah, and forgiveness for the one who recites the testimony after the adhan.
This motivates consistent practice.

ثم دعا بالوسيلة، فيقولُ: اللّهم، ربَّ هذه الدَّعوةِ التَّامَّةِ، والصَّلاةِ القائمة، آتِ محمداً الوسيلة، والفضيلة، وابعثه مقاماً محموداً الَّذِي وعدتَهُ. من قال حين يسمع المؤذن: وأنا أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له، وأن محمداً عبده ورسوله، رضيت بالله رباً، وبالإسلام ديناً، وبمحمد نبياً ورسولاً، غفر له ذنوبه. وحاصل كلام ( الكمال ) : الميل إلى القول بوجوب الإجابة. ثم دعا بالوسيلة) بعد صلاته على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعقب الإجابة، لما روي عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما: إِذَا سَمِعْتُمُ الْمُؤَذِّنَ فَقُولُوا مِثْلَ مَا يَقُولُ، ثُمَّ صَلُّوا عَلَيَّ، فَإِنَّهُ مَنْ صَلَّى عَلَيَّ صَلاةً، صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ بِهَا عَشْرًا، ثُمَّ سَلُوا لِيَ الْوَسِيلَةَ، فَإِنَّهَا مَنْزِلَةٌ فِي الْجَنَّةِ لا تَنْبَغِي إِلا لِعَبْدٍ مُؤْمِنٍ مِنْ عِبَادِ اللَّهِ، وَأَرْجُو أَنْ أَكُونَ أَنَا هُوَ، فَمَنْ سَأَلَ لِيَ الْوَسِيلَةَ، حَلَّتْ لَهُ الشَّفَاعَةُ . رواه مسلم وغيره. ثم بين كيفية الدعاء بقوله: (فَيَقُولُ) كما رواه جابر رضي الله عنه، عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: اللهم رب هذه الدعوة التَّامَّةِ والصَّلاةِ القائمة، آتِ سيدنا محمداً الوسيلة والفضيلة وابعثه مقاماً محموداً الذي وعدتَهُ حلت له شفاعتي يوم القيامة. رواه البخاري وغيره والبيهقي، وزاد في آخره: إنَّكَ لا تُخْلِفُ المِيعَادَ. وعن سعد بن أبي وقاص رضي الله عنه: من قال حين يسمع المؤذن: وأنا أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له، وأن محمداً عبده ورسوله، رضيت بالله رباً، وبالإسلام ديناً، وبمحمد نبياً ورسولاً، غفر له ذنوبه. رواه مسلم والترمذي. وعن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه أن رجلاً قال: يا رسول الله، إن المؤذنين يفضلوننا، فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: قل كما يقولون، فإذا انتهيت فسل تعطه. رواه أبو داود والنسائي وابن حبان.
Then he supplicates for al-Waseelah, saying: O Allah, Lord of this perfect call and the established prayer, grant Muhammad al-Waseelah and the virtue, and raise him to a praiseworthy station which You have promised him. Whoever says when he hears the mu'adhdhin: And I bear witness that there is no god but Allah alone, no partner for Him, and that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger, I am pleased with Allah as Lord, with Islam as religion, and with Muhammad as Prophet and Messenger, his sins are forgiven. The summary of the words of al-Kamal: inclination toward the opinion of obligation of response. Then he supplicates for al-Waseelah after sending blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him) and after the response, due to what was narrated from Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them): When you hear the mu'adhdhin, say similar to what he says, then send blessings upon me, for whoever sends blessings upon me one time, Allah sends blessings upon him ten times, then ask for al-Waseelah for me, for it is a station in Paradise which only one of Allah's believing servants deserves, and I hope that I will be that one. Whoever asks for al-Waseelah for me, intercession becomes permissible for him. Narrated by Muslim and others. Then he explains the manner of the supplication by his saying: (he says) as Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'O Allah, Lord of this perfect call and the established prayer, grant our master Muhammad al-Waseelah and the virtue, and raise him to a praiseworthy station which You have promised him, intercession for me is permitted for him on the Day of Resurrection.' Narrated by al-Bukhari and others and al-Bayhaqi, and he added at the end: 'Indeed You do not break the promise.' And from Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Whoever says when he hears the mu'adhdhin: And I bear witness that there is no god but Allah alone, no partner for Him, and that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger, I am pleased with Allah as Lord, with Islam as religion, and with Muhammad as Prophet and Messenger, his sins are forgiven.' Narrated by Muslim and al-Tirmidhi. And from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that a man said: O Messenger of Allah, the mu'adhdhins are preferred over us. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Say as they say, and when you finish, ask and you will be given.' Narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn Hibban.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage provides the recommended supplication after the adhan, along with its proofs. The author first states the supplication: after responding verbally to the adhan, one sends blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him) and then asks Allah to grant him al-Waseelah (a high station in Paradise) and al-Fadilah (virtue/excellence), and to raise him to the Maqam Mahmud (praiseworthy station) promised in the Qur'an. The basis is the hadith from Ibn Umar: upon hearing the adhan, repeat after the mu'adhdhin, send blessings, and ask for al-Waseelah for the Prophet, promising intercession. Another hadith from Jabir gives the exact wording of the supplication. Additional authentic reports mention alternative phrasings such as bearing witness and expressing satisfaction with Allah as Lord, Islam as religion, and Muhammad as Prophet, along with a promise of forgiveness. The hadith from Ibn Mas'ud encourages asking after saying the like of the adhan. The text also includes a note from al-Kamal (a scholar) who is inclined to say that responding to the adhan is obligatory (i.e., the repetition), which is a different opinion as discussed earlier. However, the focus here is on the supplication, which is uniformly considered mustahabb. The supplication after the adhan is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) based on these hadiths. The Hanafi school recommends it as part of the etiquette of hearing the adhan.

Key Terms
الوسيلة (al-waseelah): A special station in Paradise reserved for the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), for which Muslims are encouraged to ask after the adhan.
المقام المحمود (al-maqam al-mahmud): The praiseworthy station (the highest intercession) promised to the Prophet in the Qur'an (17:79).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To ask for worldly wealth
B) To ask for al-Waseelah for the Prophet and send blessings
C) To announce the start of prayer
D) To ask for forgiveness for the mu'adhdhin

Key Takeaway
Asking for al-Waseelah for the Prophet after the adhan is a recommended sunnah that brings immense reward and hope of his intercession.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Supplication for al-Wasilah after the Adhan
Expands on the ruling to pray for al-Wasilah after adhan with multiple hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on supplicating for al-Wasilah after the adhan and identify the key hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Asking for al-Wasilah after adhan is a confirmed sunnah that earns the Prophet's intercession.

After the mu'adhdhin finishes the call to prayer, the listener is encouraged to repeat the words, send blessings on the Prophet, and then ask for al-Wasilah. This lesson examines the evidence from multiple authentic hadiths and clarifies the Hanafi position that this act is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), not obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is supplicating for al-Wasilah for the Prophet after hearing the adhan. According to the Hanafi school, this is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah).
2
Locate the primary dalil
The main evidence is the hadith of Ibn Umar (narrated by Muslim) which commands to repeat the adhan, send blessings on the Prophet, and then ask for al-Wasilah.
Additional hadith from Jabir (Bukhari) provides the exact wording and mentions intercession as a reward.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'salu' (ask) is interpreted according to Hanafi usul as indicating recommendation (nadb) rather than obligation, because no qarina (evidence) raises it to wujub.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., from other schools) consider the du'a obligatory, but the Hanafi school maintains it is sunnah. The difference stems from interpreting the imperative's strength.
The Hanafi view is based on the absence of a qarina indicating obligation.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The majority Hanafi position is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah. The many hadith emphasize its virtue but do not impose a penalty for omission, confirming its recommended status.
The mufta bihi is that it is sunnah to say this du'a after the adhan.

And he has in al-Kabir: 'Whoever hears the call and says: I bear witness that there is no god but Allah alone, no partner for Him, and that Muhammad is His servant and messenger, O Allah send blessings on Muhammad and raise him to the degree of al-Wasilah with You, and make us included in his intercession on the Day of Resurrection, intercession becomes obligatory for him.' Hadiths on this topic are many, the aim is encouragement to good and conveying the hadith of the Messenger of Allah to his ummah to attain what they hope thereby. May Allah grant us His fear in all circumstances by His bounty and mercy, as al-Kamal asked in 'Fath al-Qadir'. Note: The mu'adhdhin also supplicates for al-Wasilah like others so that he may attain the virtue.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding the original ruling that after the adhan, one should supplicate for al-Wasilah for the Prophet. The author presents multiple hadiths proving the recommendation. The first hadith from Ibn Umar mentions the sequence: repeating the adhan, sending blessings on the Prophet, then asking for al-Wasilah. The second from Jabir specifies the wording of the du'a. Additional narrations add variations and emphasize forgiveness and intercession. The commentator notes that some scholars lean towards obligation of answering the mu'adhdhin. A note clarifies that the mu'adhdhin also makes this supplication for himself. The passage thus firmly establishes the sunnah of this du'a with strong evidence.

Key Terms
الوسيلة (al-wasilah): A special station in Paradise reserved for the Prophet Muhammad, which is the highest rank.
الشفاعة (al-shafa'ah): Intercession of the Prophet on the Day of Judgment for the believers.
الإجابة (al-ijabah): Responding to the mu'adhdhin by repeating his words.

Responding to the Iqamah and When the Imam Begins: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on iqamah response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi response to 'qad qamat al-salah' and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding when the imam should start the prayer.

Core Idea
The imam's starting time during iqamah is disputed: Abu Hanifa says at hay'alah, Abu Yusuf says after completion.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah presents a hadith about the proper response to the iqamah. It then records an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the timing of the imam beginning the congregational prayer. Understanding this dispute helps appreciate the scope of valid practice within the Hanafi school and the methodology of tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and the response to 'qad qamat al-salah'
The hadith from Abu Dawud shows the Prophet's specific response: 'Aqamaha Allah wa adamaha'.
This is the sunnah response, not the hawqalah.
2
Understand the general response to the rest of iqamah
For other phrases, the response is similar to the adhan, including saying 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' at the hay'alah.
This practice aligns with Abu Yusuf's view.
3
Locate the dispute
Abu Hanifa: imam starts at hay'alah. Abu Yusuf: imam waits until end of iqamah.
Both are within the Hanafi school.
4
Note the tarjih
The author of al-Majma' prefers Abu Yusuf's view as more just (a'dal).
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وروى أبو داود بإسناده إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: أنَّ بلالاً أخذَ في الإقامة فلما قال: قد قامتِ الصَّلاةُ، قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : أقامها الله وأدامها ، وقال في سائر الإقامة كنحو حديث عمر في الأذان)، وفيه الحوقلة عندَ الحَيْعَلة، وهذا يتأتى عند أبي يوسف، وإلا فعند أبي حنيفة يكون الإمام عند الحَيْعَلة أخذ في الشروع في الصلاة. وقال صاحب « المجمع » : قــول بي ! يوسف أعدل، وهو كما قال كذا بخط شيخ أستاذي العلامة « المقدسي) رحمه الله. فائدة جليلة : قوله : ( ثُمَّ سَلُوا لِي الوَسِيْلَةَ فَإِنَّهَا مَنْزِلَةٌ فِي الجنَّة» (۳) الحديث، اعلـــم وفقنا الله وإياك أن من هذه المنزلة تتفرع جميع الجنات، وهي في جنة عدن دار المقامة، ولها شعيبة في كل جنة من الجنان، ومن تلك الشعبة يظهر محمد لأهل تلك الجنة، وهي في كل جنة أعظم منزلـة فيها، وأما منزلته يومَ الزَّوْرِ الأعظم على اليمين من حيث التجلي، ومنزلته يوم القيامة بـيـن يــدي الحكم العدل لتنفيذ الأوامر الإلهية والأحكام في العالم، فالكل عنه يأخذ في ذلك الموطن، وهـو وجه كلُّهُ يُرَى من جميع جهاته، وله من كل جانب إعلام عن الله، يفهم عنه، يرونه لساناً، ويسمعونه صوتاً وحرفاً فاعلم ذلك. كذا في تفسير الحديث بلسان القوم، نقلته مختصراً مــن خـط مؤلفه شـيـخ أستاذي طريقة العارف بالله تعالى الشيخ عبد الوهاب الشعراني ) (4)، عن شيخه العارف بالله سيدي علي الخواص ( ) (0) أعاد الله علينا من بركاتهما، ومددهما، ونقلته أيضاً ضمن رسالة سميتها: إكرام أولي الألباب بشريف الخطاب».
And Abu Dawud narrated with his chain to the Prophet: that Bilal began the iqamah, and when he said 'Qad qamat al-salah', the Prophet said: 'Aqamaha Allah wa adamaha', and he said regarding the rest of the iqamah similar to the hadith of Umar on the adhan, and in it is the hawqalah at the hay'alah. And this is applicable according to Abu Yusuf, otherwise according to Abu Hanifa, the imam at the hay'alah has begun starting the prayer. The author of al-Majma' said: The statement of Abu Yusuf is more just, and it is as he said, as in the handwriting of my teacher's teacher, the scholar al-Maqdisi, may Allah have mercy on him. A great benefit: His saying: 'Then ask for al-Wasilah for me, for it is a station in Paradise.' Know, may Allah grant us success, that from this station all gardens branch out, and it is in Jannat 'Adn, the abode of residence, and it has a branch in every garden, and from that branch Muhammad appears to the people of that garden, and it is in every garden the greatest station therein. As for his station on the day of the great visit on the right side in terms of manifestation, and his station on the Day of Resurrection before the Just Judge to execute divine commands and judgments in the world, so everyone takes from him in that situation, and he is all face, seen from all directions, and from every side he has an announcement from Allah, understood from him, they see it as a tongue, and hear it as a voice and letter. So know that. Such is in the interpretation of the hadith in the language of the people, I transmitted it abridged from the handwriting of its author, the shaykh of my teacher, the knower of Allah, Shaykh Abd al-Wahhab al-Sha'rani, from his shaykh, the knower of Allah, Sayyidi Ali al-Khawwas, may Allah return us from their blessings and support. And I also transmitted it in a treatise I titled: Ikram Uli al-Albab bi-Sharif al-Khitab.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage first presents a hadith about the iqamah: when the mu'adhdhin says 'qad qamat al-salah', the listener responds with 'aqamaha Allah wa adamaha'. For the rest of the iqamah, the response is similar to the adhan. The hawqalah (saying la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah) is recommended at the hay'alah ('hayya 'ala'). Then the author notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Yusuf, the imam should not start the prayer until the iqamah is complete; according to Abu Hanifa, the imam can begin once the mu'adhdhin reaches the hay'alah, as that indicates the prayer is about to start. The author of al-Majma' prefers Abu Yusuf's view. The passage then provides a spiritual fa'idah on the station of al-Wasilah, explaining its supreme rank in Paradise and the Prophet's unique position in the hereafter, quoting from Sufi scholars. This shows how the Hadith is interpreted at a deeper level.

Key Terms
الحَيْعَلَة (al-hay'alah): The phrase 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah' in the adhan and iqamah.
الإقامة (al-iqamah): The second call to prayer, which signals the immediate start of the congregational prayer.
الوسيلة (al-wasilah): The highest station in Paradise, reserved for the Prophet; also used metaphorically for spiritual rank.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith, what should one say when the mu'adhdhin says 'qad qamat al-salah' during the iqamah?
A) 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah'
B) 'Aqamaha Allah wa adamaha'
C) 'Allahu akbar'
D) 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the proper response to 'qad qamat al-salah' is 'aqamaha Allah wa adamaha', and the preferred view is to wait until the iqamah ends before starting prayer.

The Station of al-Wasilah: The Prophet's Supreme Rank in Paradise
Spiritual commentary on al-Wasilah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the spiritual interpretation of al-Wasilah as the highest station in Paradise from which all other gardens branch, and describe the Prophet's unique manifestations on the Day of Resurrection.

Core Idea
Al-Wasilah is the highest station in Paradise, from which all gardens branch, and the Prophet appears to each garden's inhabitants from its branch.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah provides a profound spiritual commentary on the hadith that commands believers to ask for al-Wasilah for the Prophet. The commentary, drawn from Sufi masters, explains the metaphysical significance of this station. While not a fiqh ruling, it enriches our understanding of the Prophet's rank and the structure of Paradise.

Guided Path
1
Understand the hadith about al-Wasilah
The Prophet commanded us to ask Allah to grant him al-Wasilah, described as a station in Paradise.
This is a well-known hadith (Sahih Muslim).
2
Grasp the spiritual interpretation
Al-Wasilah is the highest station in Jannat 'Adn; from it, a branch extends into every garden, through which the Prophet manifests to its inhabitants.
This interpretation is from Sufi scholars like al-Sha'rani and al-Khawwas.
3
Note the Prophet's eschatological role
On the Day of Resurrection, the Prophet will stand before Allah to execute divine commands, and he will be seen as 'all face' from all directions, communicating directly.
This highlights the Prophet's unique intercessory and executive role.

The Prophet's Station (al-Wasilah) and Its Virtue
Exhortation to ask for al-Wasilah and mystical description of the Prophet's station

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the meaning of al-Wasilah and identify the recommended practice of asking for it after the adhan.

Core Idea
Al-Wasilah is the Prophet's highest station in Paradise; asking for it after the adhan is a sunnah that brings great reward.

This passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah encourages asking for al-Wasilah for the Prophet after the adhan. It defines al-Wasilah as a special station in Paradise from which all gardens branch. The hadith commands us to ask for it, and the mu'adhdhin is included in this virtue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the command from the hadith
The hadith quoted says 'ثُمَّ سَلُوا لِي الوَسِيْلَةَ' – then ask for me al-Wasilah. This establishes the recommended practice.
The hadith is from Abu Dawood and is hasan.
2
Define al-Wasilah
The passage explains that al-Wasilah is a station in Paradise (منزلة في الجنة) that belongs to the Prophet. It is the highest station from which all other gardens branch.
It is not just any means but a specific, elevated rank.
3
Understand the implication for the mu'adhdhin
The author notes that the mu'adhdhin also asks for al-Wasilah to obtain virtue, implying it is recommended for all who hear the adhan.
The mu'adhdhin is not exempt from this supplication.

الحديث في هذا الباب كثير، والقصد الحث على الخير وإبلاغ حديث رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لأمته لنيل ما ترجاه هم بذلك رزقنا الله تقواه في جميع الأحوال بفضله ورحمته، كما سأله الكمال «بفتح القدير». تنبيه: المؤذن يدعو بالوسيلة كغيره لتحصل له الفضيلة. وروى أبو داود بإسناده إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: أنَّ بلالاً أخذَ في الإقامة فلما قال: قد قامتِ الصَّلاةُ، قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : أقامها الله وأدامها ، وقال في سائر الإقامة كنحو حديث عمر في الأذان)، وفيه الحوقلة عندَ الحَيْعَلة، وهذا يتأتى عند أبي يوسف، وإلا فعند أبي حنيفة يكون الإمام عند الحَيْعَلة أخذ في الشروع في الصلاة. وقال صاحب « المجمع » : قول أبي يوسف أعدل، وهو كما قال كذا بخط شيخ أستاذي العلامة « المقدسي) رحمه الله. فائدة جليلة : قوله : ( ثُمَّ سَلُوا لِي الوَسِيْلَةَ فَإِنَّهَا مَنْزِلَةٌ فِي الجنَّة» (۳) الحديث، اعلم وفقنا الله وإياك أن من هذه المنزلة تتفرع جميع الجنات، وهي في جنة عدن دار المقامة، ولها شعبة في كل جنة من الجنان، ومن تلك الشعبة يظهر محمد لأهل تلك الجنة، وهي في كل جنة أعظم منزلة فيها، وأما منزلته يومَ الزَّوْرِ الأعظم على اليمين من حيث التجلي، ومنزلته يوم القيامة بـيـن يــدي الحكم العدل لتنفيذ الأوامر الإلهية والأحكام في العالم، فالكل عنه يأخذ في ذلك الموطن، وهو وجه كلُّهُ يُرَى من جميع جهاته، وله من كل جانب إعلام عن الله، يفهم عنه، يرونه لساناً، ويسمعونه صوتاً وحرفاً فاعلم ذلك. كذا في تفسير الحديث بلسان القوم، نقلته مختصراً مــن خـط مؤلفه شـيـخ أستاذي طريقة العارف بالله تعالى الشيخ عبد الوهاب الشعراني ) (4)، عن شيخه العارف بالله سيدي علي الخواص ( ) (0) أعاد الله علينا من بركاتهما، ومددهما، ونقلته أيضاً ضمن رسالة سميتها: إكرام أولي الألباب بشريف الخطاب».

(۲) تقدم تخريجه ص (۳) تقدم تخريجه ص ) (٤) هو سيدي الشيخ أبي المواهب عبد الوهاب بن أحمد الشعراني، الإمام العامل العابد الزاهد الفقيه الصوفي، يرتفع نسبه إلى الإمام محمد بن الحنفية بن علي بن أبي طالب له من تصانيفه لطائف المنن، اليواقيت والجواهر، تنبيه المغترين تنبيه الغافلين الجواهر والدرر، ولد سنة (۸۹۸)، توفي سنة (٩٧٣)هـ كشف الظنون (٦١٨/١).
(٥) هو سيدي علي الخواص أحد أكابر العارفين وأعيان الأولياء وأئمة الأصفياء وكراماته وعلومه وأسراره ملات كتب الشعراني جامع كرامات الأولياء (۳۷۱/۲).
Hadith on this topic are many, and the intent is encouragement towards good and conveying the hadith of the Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) to his nation to attain what they hope for thereby. May Allah grant us His piety in all circumstances by His grace and mercy, as He asked for perfection 'by the opening of the Powerful'. Note: The caller to prayer (mu'adhdhin) asks for al-Wasilah like others to obtain virtue. Abu Dawood narrated from the Prophet (ﷺ) that Bilal began the iqamah, and when he said 'Qad qamat al-salah', the Prophet said: 'Aqamaha Allah wa adamaha' (May Allah establish it and perpetuate it), and for the rest of the iqamah it is similar to the hadith of 'Umar regarding the adhan. And in it is the hawqalah (saying 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah') at the hay'alah. This is plausible according to Abu Yusuf, but according to Abu Hanifa, the Imam begins the prayer at the hay'alah (the caller saying 'Hayya 'ala al-salah'). The author of al-Majma' said: The statement of Abu Yusuf is more balanced, and it is as he said. Written in the handwriting of my teacher's teacher, the scholar al-Maqdisi. A great benefit: His saying: 'Then ask for me al-Wasilah, for it is a station in Paradise' (hadith). Know, may Allah grant us and you success, that from this station all Gardens branch out. It is in the Garden of 'Adn, the Abode of Permanence, and it has a branch in every Garden of Paradise. From that branch, Muhammad appears to the people of that Garden. It is the greatest station in every Garden. As for his station on the Day of the Great Visit, at the right side in terms of manifestation, and his station on the Day of Judgment before the Judge of Justice to execute divine commands and judgments in the world, all take from him in that station. He is all face, seen from all directions. From every side he has signs from Allah, understood from him; they see him as a tongue and hear him as a voice and letters. So know that. This is from the interpretation of the hadith in the language of the people. I extracted it briefly from the handwriting of its author, my teacher's teacher, the knower of Allah, Sheikh 'Abd al-Wahhab al-Sha'rani, from his teacher, the knower of Allah, Sayyidi 'Ali al-Khawwas. May Allah return to us their blessings and support. I also transmitted it in a treatise I named: 'Ikaram Uli al-Albab bi Sharif al-Khitab'. (1) Reported by Abu Dawood in al-Salah, chapter on what to say when hearing the iqamah (528). (2) ... (3) ... (4) He is Sayyidi Abu al-Mawahib 'Abd al-Wahhab ibn Ahmad al-Sha'rani, the knowledgeable, practicing, devout, ascetic, jurist, Sufi; his lineage traces back to Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah ibn 'Ali ibn Abi Talib. Among his works are Lata'if al-Minan, al-Yawaqit wa al-Jawahir, Tanbih al-Mughtarin, Tanbih al-Ghafilin, al-Jawahir wa al-Durar. He was born in 898 AH and died in 973 AH. Kashf al-Zunun 1/618. (5) He is Sayyidi 'Ali al-Khawwas, one of the great knowers, prominent saints, and leading pure ones; his miracles, knowledge, and secrets fill al-Sha'rani's works. Jami' Karamat al-Awliya' 2/371.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the virtue of asking for al-Wasilah. It begins with a note that the mu'adhdhin should ask for al-Wasilah like everyone else. Then it mentions a hadith where the Prophet responded to Bilal's iqamah with a du'a, and discusses a point of dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: Abu Hanifa held that the Imam starts the prayer at the hay'alah (when the mu'adhdhin says 'Hayya 'ala al-salah'), while Abu Yusuf held that the Imam waits until the end of the iqamah. The author of al-Majma' preferred Abu Yusuf's view. Then the passage provides a lengthy mystical explanation of the Prophet's station (al-Wasilah) in Paradise, describing it as the central station from which all gardens branch, and how the Prophet will appear to each garden's inhabitants. This explanation is taken from the Sufi tradition, specifically from al-Sha'rani and al-Khawwas. This passage is not a legal ruling (hukm) but a exhortatory and spiritual elaboration.

Key Terms
الوسيلة (al-wasīlah): A station in Paradise that the Prophet ﷺ occupies; it is the highest station from which all other gardens branch.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is al-Wasilah according to the passage?
A) A special prayer recited after the adhan
B) A station in Paradise from which all gardens branch
C) A specific phrase said during the iqamah
D) The name of the Prophet's mosque

Key Takeaway
Al-Wasilah is the Prophet's highest station in Paradise; asking for it after the adhan is a sunnah that brings great virtue.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on When the Imam Starts Prayer During Iqamah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of the Imam starting prayer during iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding when the Imam starts the prayer during the iqamah, and identify which view is considered more balanced according to al-Majma'.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf's view that the Imam starts after the iqamah is complete is considered more balanced than Abu Hanifa's view of starting at the hay'alah.

This passage from the sharh presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf about the timing of the Imam's starting of the prayer during the iqamah. The author quotes the hadith of Bilal and notes that the hawqalah should be said at the hay'alah. He then cites the author of al-Majma', who considers Abu Yusuf's position more balanced (a'dal).

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
When the mu'adhdhin says 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' (hay'alah) during the iqamah, should the Imam begin the prayer immediately or wait until the end?
The iqamah consists of several phrases; the hay'alah occurs after 'Allahu Akbar' and before 'Qad qamat al-salah'.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa held that the Imam starts the prayer at the hay'alah (when 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' is said).
This means the prayer begins before the iqamah is complete.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf held that the Imam does not start until after the iqamah is complete. At the hay'alah, the listener should say the hawqalah (La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah).
This is derived from the hadith of Bilal: the Prophet responded after 'Qad qamat al-salah', not at the hay'alah.
4
Examine the evidence
The hadith of Bilal is cited: when Bilal said 'Qad qamat al-salah', the Prophet said 'Aqamaha Allah wa adamaha'. This suggests that the Prophet waited until that phrase, implying the iqamah should be completed.
The hadith is from Abu Dawood (528) and is used to support Abu Yusuf's view.
5
Determine the tarjih
The author of al-Majma' states that Abu Yusuf's view is more balanced (أعدل), and the author of this sharh agrees, quoting it from his teacher's teacher.
This indicates that in later Hanafi scholarship, Abu Yusuf's view is preferred (mufta bihi).

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the virtue of asking for al-Wasilah. It begins with a note that the mu'adhdhin should ask for al-Wasilah like everyone else. Then it mentions a hadith where the Prophet responded to Bilal's iqamah with a du'a, and discusses a point of dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: Abu Hanifa held that the Imam starts the prayer at the hay'alah (when the mu'adhdhin says 'Hayya 'ala al-salah'), while Abu Yusuf held that the Imam waits until the end of the iqamah. The author of al-Majma' preferred Abu Yusuf's view. Then the passage provides a lengthy mystical explanation of the Prophet's station (al-Wasilah) in Paradise, describing it as the central station from which all gardens branch, and how the Prophet will appear to each garden's inhabitants. This explanation is taken from the Sufi tradition, specifically from al-Sha'rani and al-Khawwas. This passage is not a legal ruling (hukm) but a exhortatory and spiritual elaboration.

Key Terms
الحوقلة (al-ḥawqalah): Saying 'Lā ḥawla wa lā quwwata illā billāh' (There is no power nor strength except with Allah).
الحَيْعَلة (al-ḥayʿalah): The phrase 'Hayya ʿalā al-salāh' in the adhan/iqamah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Imam Muhammad
D) The author of al-Majma'

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi position is that the Imam should wait until the end of the iqamah to start the prayer, based on Abu Yusuf's view.

The Meaning of Shart (Condition) in Hanafi Fiqh
Defines the term shart (condition) linguistically, technically, and categorically.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the technical definition of shart (condition) in Hanafi fiqh and identify its three main types (intellectual, legal, contractual).

Core Idea
A shart is an external condition that must persist throughout the act.

This lesson unpacks the term 'shart' (condition) as used in the Hanafi school. Understanding the precise meaning is crucial because conditions determine the validity of acts like prayer. The passage defines it linguistically as a sign, and technically as something whose existence is necessary and which is external to the essence.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the linguistic meaning
The passage explains that 'shart' linguistically means a necessary sign, like 'ashrat al‐sa‘ah' (signs of the Hour). This root idea of a sign points to something external.
The plural 'shurut' is used by jurists, not 'ashrat'.
2
State the technical definition
In Sacred Law, a condition is 'that upon whose existence something depends, and it is external to the essence of the thing.' This means the act cannot exist without it, yet it is not part of the act's inner structure.
This definition is from Ghayat al‐Bayan.
3
List the three types of shart
The passage lists: intellectual (e.g., an axe for a carpenter), legal (e.g., purification for prayer), and contractual (e.g., a condition for divorce). These cover physical, religious, and stipulative conditions.
Legal conditions are the most relevant to fiqh.
4
Understand the continuity requirement
Al‐Mabsut defines shart as that which requires continuity from the beginning to the end of the act, like purification or covering the ‘awrah. If it ceases, the act becomes invalid.
This is a key practical test for identifying conditions in worship.
5
Note the classification differences
The passage mentions that early Hanafi scholars divided shart into four (Abu Zaid), five (al‐Bazdawi), six (al‐Sarakhsi), or two (real vs. metaphorical). This shows the depth of Hanafi usul.
The two‐category division simplifies: real shart is what the cause depends on; the rest is metaphorical.

Chapter on the Conditions (Shurut) and Pillars (Arkan) of Prayer. [The author] combined them, although they are each placed in separate chapters, because the goal is to know all of them for the correctness of prayer, so combining them makes clearer what constitutes a valid prayer. In some copies it is 'shara'it' as expressed by the jurist Abu al-Layth and the author of Munyat al-Musalli. And the commentator said: 'Sharai't is the plural of sharitah, meaning shart.' End. Likewise in Sharh al-Kanz al-Dayri: 'Sharitah is in the meaning of shart, and its plural is sharai't.' By this one knows the answer to the statement of the author of al-Bahr in this regard. End. And 'shurut' is the plural of 'shart' with sukun on the ra', and 'ashrat' is the plural of 'shart' with fatha on the ra', and both mean a sign. The prevalent usage among jurists is 'shurut' rather than 'ashrat'. Linguistically, 'shart' is a necessary sign; from it is 'ashrat al-sa'ah' (signs of the Hour), i.e., its necessary signs. In Sacred Law, it is: that upon whose existence something depends, and it is external to the essence of the thing. This is from Ghayat al-Bayan. Fakhral-Islam said: It is a term for what existence is attached to, not obligation. It is said: what the cause precedes in existence, and it does not require the existence of the condition. There is disagreement on its division: Abu Zaid made it four types, Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi five, Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi six, and some verifiers made it two types: real and metaphorical. The real is that upon whose existence the cause comes into effect, or that upon whose existence the effect depends for the establishment of the ruling; the metaphorical is other than that. The remaining divisions are metaphorical, not real. 'Arkan' is the plural of 'rukn', which linguistically means the strong side: Allah says: 'Or take refuge in a strong support' (Hud 11:80), i.e., might and protection. In terminology, it is the integral part from which the essence is composed along with others. It is said: that by which something stands, and it is a part inside the essence of the thing. 'Fard' can be applied to both portion and pillar. Then, the condition (shart) is of three types: intellectual, like the axe for the carpenter; legal, like purification for prayer; and contractual, like the condition upon which divorce is suspended. In al-Mabsut: The definition of shart is that whose continuity is required from the beginning of prayer to the end, like purification and covering the 'awrah. The definition of rukn is that which does not last from the beginning of prayer to the end, but rather ends upon commencing another pillar, like standing and recitation, each of which ends with bowing, and bowing ends with moving to prostration. The six conditions are conditions of permissibility (shurut jawaz), not conditions of existence (shurut wujud). The condition of existence is continuous ability at the time of the act. In this chapter are conditions that precede entering the prayer, among them the opening takbir, and intermediate conditions, like the order of pillars, in what is not prescribed repeatedly. Commentary
This passage is a definitional and terminological introduction to the chapter on the conditions and pillars of prayer. The author explains why he combined them in one chapter: to help the student understand what is needed for a valid prayer. He then clarifies the linguistic and technical meanings of 'shart' (condition) and 'rukn' (pillar). A condition is a necessary prerequisite that is external to the essence of the act, while a pillar is an integral part of the act. He also discusses the different classifications of conditions by early Hanafi scholars. The passage further distinguishes between the continuity required: conditions must persist throughout the prayer (like purification), while pillars are discrete acts that expire as one moves to the next. He mentions the six conditions (shurut) of prayer as conditions of permissibility (shurut al-jawaz), not conditions of existence. Finally, he notes that there are conditions that precede the prayer (e.g., takbir tahrimah) and intermediate conditions (e.g., order of pillars). This is a foundational text for understanding the structure of prayer in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
شرط (sharṭ): In fiqh: that upon which the existence of something depends, and it is external to the essence of the thing. It is of three types: intellectual ('aqli), legal (shar'i), and contractual (ja'li).
ركن (rukn): In fiqh: an integral part (juz' dhati) from which the essence of the act is composed; it is inside the essence (dakhil fi mahiyyat al-shay').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of a legal condition (shart shar‘i)?
A) An axe for a carpenter
B) Purification for prayer
C) A condition for divorce
D) A strong side of a building

Key Takeaway
A condition (shart) is an external prerequisite that must persist continuously throughout an act; without it, the act is invalid.

The Meaning of Rukn (Pillar) and its Distinction from Shart
Defines the term rukn (pillar) linguistically, technically, and with practical continuity test.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define rukn (pillar) in Hanafi terminology and explain how it differs from shart using the continuity criterion, with examples from prayer.

Core Idea
A rukn is an internal integral part that expires upon the next pillar; it does not persist like a condition.

This lesson focuses on the term 'rukn' (pillar), the counterpart to 'shart'. While a condition is external and continuous, a pillar is an internal component that is performed and then closed. The passage defines it linguistically as a strong side and technically as an integral part, and provides a practical test from al-Mabsut to distinguish it from conditions.

Guided Path
1
Explore the linguistic meaning of rukn
Linguistically, 'rukn' means the strong side, as in the Quranic verse 'take refuge in a strong support' (Hud 11:80). This conveys the idea of a fundamental support.
The plural is 'arkan'.
2
State the technical definition
In terminology, rukn is 'the integral part from which the essence is composed along with others' and 'that by which something stands, and it is a part inside the essence of the thing.'
It is internal (dakhil), unlike shart which is external.
3
Understand the continuity distinction
Al-Mabsut defines rukn as 'that which does not last from the beginning of prayer to the end, but rather ends upon commencing another pillar.' For example, standing ends with bowing, and bowing ends with prostration.
This is the key operational difference: shart persists, rukn expires.
4
Examine examples of pillars in prayer
The passage gives examples: standing (qiyam), recitation (qira’ah) — each ends when the next pillar begins. The opening takbir is also a pillar because it expires upon starting standing.
In Hanafi, recitation is actually wajib, but the principle applies.
5
Note the relationship with fard
The passage states that the term 'fard' can be applied to both portion (shart) and pillar (rukn) in general usage, though technically they are distinct.
Fard is a broader category; shart and rukn are subtypes.

باب شروط الصلاة وأركانها
جمع بينها، وإن أفردوا كلاً بباب على حدة، لأن المقصود علم جميعها لتصحيح الصلاة، فكان الجمع بينهما أظهر في المراد للتيقظ إلى ما تصح به، وفي نسخة شرائط كما عبر به الفقيه «أبو الليث»، وصاحب « منية المصلي». وقال شارحها شرائط جمع شريطة، بمعنى الشرط. انتهى. وكذا في شرح الكنز للديري»، الشريطة في معنى الشرط وجمعها شرائط، وبه يعلم الجواب عن كلام صاحب « البحر» في هذا المحل. انتهى. والشروط جمع شرط، بسكون الراء، والأشراط جمع شرط بفتحها، وهما العلامة، والمستعمل في لسان الفقهاء الشروط دون الأشراط. والشرط في اللغة: العلامة اللازمة، ومنه أشراط الساعة، أي علامتها اللازمة. وفي الشريعة هو: ما يتوقف على وجوده الشيء، وهو خارج عن ماهية الشيء. كذا في غاية البيان ) . وقال «فخر الإسلام»: هو اسم لما يتعلق به الوجود، دون الوجوب، وقيل: ما يسبقه العلة وجوداً، ولا تعمل إلى وجود الشرط. وقد اختلف في تقسيمه، فجعل « أبو زيد» أقسامه أربعة، و «فخر الإسلام البزدوي» خمسة، و«شمس الأئمة السرخسي» ستة، وبعض المحققين إلى قسمين: حقيقة، ومجاز. فالحقيقة ما توجد العلة عند وجوده، أو ما يتوقف المؤثر على وجوده في ثبوت الحكم والمجاز ما عداه، وبقية الأقسام بحسب المجاز لا بحسب الحقيقة، والأركان جمع ركن، وهو في اللغة الجانب الأقوى [ قال تعالى ]: أَوْ ءَاوِى إِلَى رُكْنٍ شَدِيدٍ ﴾ [هود: ۸۰] أي: عز ومنعة، وفي الاصطلاح الجزء الذاتي التي تتركب الماهية منه ومن غيره، ويقال: ما يقوم به الشيء وهو جزء داخل ماهية الشيء، والفرض يجوز إطلاقه على الشطر والركن جميعاً، ثم الشرط على ثلاثة أنواع عقلي: كالقَدُوم للنجار، وشرعي: كالطهارة للصلاة، وجعلي كالدخول المعلق به الطلاق. وفي « المبسوط » : حد الشرط: ما يشترط دوامه من أول الصلاة إلى آخرها كالطهارة، وستر العورة وحد الركن ما لا يدوم من أول الصلاة إلى آخرها، بل ينقضي بالشروع في ركن آخر كالقيام والقراءة، كل منهما ينقضي بالركوع، والركوع بالانتقال إلى السجود والشروط الستة شروط جواز لا شروط وجود، وشرط الوجود: القدرة المتصلة بالفعل. وفي هذا الباب شروط متقدمة قبل الدخول في الصلاة ، ومنها التحريمة، وشروط متوسطة، كترتيب الأركان، فيما لم يشرع مكرراً. وقد اتبعت هذه الطريقة تسهيلاً على المتعلم، وإن نظر في
Chapter on the Conditions (Shurut) and Pillars (Arkan) of Prayer. [The author] combined them, although they are each placed in separate chapters, because the goal is to know all of them for the correctness of prayer, so combining them makes clearer what constitutes a valid prayer. In some copies it is 'shara'it' as expressed by the jurist Abu al-Layth and the author of Munyat al-Musalli. And the commentator said: 'Sharai't is the plural of sharitah, meaning shart.' End. Likewise in Sharh al-Kanz al-Dayri: 'Sharitah is in the meaning of shart, and its plural is sharai't.' By this one knows the answer to the statement of the author of al-Bahr in this regard. End. And 'shurut' is the plural of 'shart' with sukun on the ra', and 'ashrat' is the plural of 'shart' with fatha on the ra', and both mean a sign. The prevalent usage among jurists is 'shurut' rather than 'ashrat'. Linguistically, 'shart' is a necessary sign; from it is 'ashrat al-sa'ah' (signs of the Hour), i.e., its necessary signs. In Sacred Law, it is: that upon whose existence something depends, and it is external to the essence of the thing. This is from Ghayat al-Bayan. Fakhral-Islam said: It is a term for what existence is attached to, not obligation. It is said: what the cause precedes in existence, and it does not require the existence of the condition. There is disagreement on its division: Abu Zaid made it four types, Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi five, Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi six, and some verifiers made it two types: real and metaphorical. The real is that upon whose existence the cause comes into effect, or that upon whose existence the effect depends for the establishment of the ruling; the metaphorical is other than that. The remaining divisions are metaphorical, not real. 'Arkan' is the plural of 'rukn', which linguistically means the strong side: Allah says: 'Or take refuge in a strong support' (Hud 11:80), i.e., might and protection. In terminology, it is the integral part from which the essence is composed along with others. It is said: that by which something stands, and it is a part inside the essence of the thing. 'Fard' can be applied to both portion and pillar. Then, the condition (shart) is of three types: intellectual, like the axe for the carpenter; legal, like purification for prayer; and contractual, like the condition upon which divorce is suspended. In al-Mabsut: The definition of shart is that whose continuity is required from the beginning of prayer to the end, like purification and covering the 'awrah. The definition of rukn is that which does not last from the beginning of prayer to the end, but rather ends upon commencing another pillar, like standing and recitation, each of which ends with bowing, and bowing ends with moving to prostration. The six conditions are conditions of permissibility (shurut jawaz), not conditions of existence (shurut wujud). The condition of existence is continuous ability at the time of the act. In this chapter are conditions that precede entering the prayer, among them the opening takbir, and intermediate conditions, like the order of pillars, in what is not prescribed repeatedly. I have followed this method to facilitate the learner, and if one looks into
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and terminological introduction to the chapter on the conditions and pillars of prayer. The author explains why he combined them in one chapter: to help the student understand what is needed for a valid prayer. He then clarifies the linguistic and technical meanings of 'shart' (condition) and 'rukn' (pillar). A condition is a necessary prerequisite that is external to the essence of the act, while a pillar is an integral part of the act. He also discusses the different classifications of conditions by early Hanafi scholars. The passage further distinguishes between the continuity required: conditions must persist throughout the prayer (like purification), while pillars are discrete acts that expire as one moves to the next. He mentions the six conditions (shurut) of prayer as conditions of permissibility (shurut al-jawaz), not conditions of existence. Finally, he notes that there are conditions that precede the prayer (e.g., takbir tahrimah) and intermediate conditions (e.g., order of pillars). This is a foundational text for understanding the structure of prayer in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
ركن (rukn): In fiqh: an integral part (juz' dhati) from which the essence of the act is composed; it is inside the essence (dakhil fi mahiyyat al-shay').
فرض (farḍ): May be applied to both shart (condition) and rukn (pillar) in general usage, but technically distinguished.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to a pillar (rukn) when the next pillar begins?
A) It continues throughout the prayer
B) It expires and ends
C) It becomes a condition
D) It requires repetition

Key Takeaway
A pillar (rukn) is an internal integral part that expires upon the next pillar; it is distinguished from a condition (shart) which persists.

Covering the Awrah and Seeing It Through an Open Collar
Ruling on covering 'awrah and seeing it through open collar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of covering the 'awrah in prayer and apply the Hanafi ruling that seeing one's own 'awrah through an open collar does not invalidate the prayer.

Core Idea
Seeing your own 'awrah through an open collar does not break prayer because your 'awrah is not 'awrah to yourself.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah addresses two key aspects of prayer: the absolute obligation to cover the 'awrah and a nuanced scenario where the covering is present but one's own 'awrah becomes visible through an opening in the garment. The author clarifies that the cover must be opaque and surround the body from all sides, yet accidental self-observation through a collar does not nullify the prayer. Understanding this ruling requires distinguishing between external covering (required for validity) and personal visibility (which is not a breach of obligation).

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary obligation
Covering the 'awrah is fard (obligatory) in prayer by consensus (ijma'), even in darkness. The cover must be thick enough to hide what is beneath.
2
Contrast the collar scenario
Consider a person praying with an open collar (jayb) such that his own 'awrah is visible to him during bowing. The covering is still present externally.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle
One's own 'awrah is not considered 'awrah relative to oneself; it is permissible to touch and see it. Therefore, accidental self-observation does not invalidate the prayer.
This is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some later Hanafi scholars conditioned covering even from oneself. However, the correct view (al-sahih) is that prayer remains valid.
The author's phrasing 'on the correct view' endorses the majority position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وستر العورة، ولا يضر نظرها منْ جَيْبِهِ. روي عن أبي يوسف جوازها، إن أعاده على طاهر، وإن كان موضع أنفه نجساً وموضع جبهته طاهراً كباقي المواضع، صحت صلاته، بالاتفاق، كأنه اقتصر على الجبهة، وموضع الأنف أقـل مـن قـدر الدرهم، فلم يضر اتصاله بالنجس، والأصل في لزوم تطهير الثوب قوله تعالى: ﴿وَثِيَابَكَ فَطَعَرَ) [ال : ٤] وإذا لزم التطهير في الثوب، لزم في البدن والمكان بطريق الأولى؛ لأنهما ألزم للمصلي من الثوب، إذ لا وجود للصلاة بدون مكان، وقد توجد بدون ثوب، كما في صلاة العاري، فالوارد في الثوب عبارةً وأورد في البدن والمكان دلالة، ولأن الصلاة مناجاة مع الرب عزّ وعلا، فيجب أن يكون المصلي على أحسن الأحوال وذا في طهارته وطهارة ما يتصل به من الثوب والمكان، ولــو صـلـى عـلـى مكـان طاهر، إلا أنه إذا سجد تقع ثيابه على أرض نجسة لا تلوث ثيابه، جازت صلاته. وسنذكر (۱) تفاريعه إن شاء الله تعالى. (وَ) يشترط (ستر العورة)، وسنذكر حقيقتها، وكان سترها فرضاً للإجماع عـلـيـه في الصلاة، ولو كان في بيت مظلم، ولحديث عائشة « لا يَقبَلُ الله صَلَاةَ حَائِضِ إِلَّا بِخِمَارٍ » (۳) وصححه الحاكم والساتر هو الذي لا يرى ما تحته، فالثوب الرقيق الذي يصف ما تحته لا يكون ساتراً، وفي «التجنيس امرأة صلت وعليها ثوب رقيق، يصف ما تحته، لا يجوز صلاتها، لأنها بمنزلة العارية. قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لَعَنَ اللهُ الكَاسِيَاتِ العَارِيَاتِ » (۳) أراد به ما ذكرنا. انتهى. والشرط الستر من الجوانب، حتى لو صلى في قميص محلول الجيب)، فرأى منه عورته حال الركوع، جازت صلاته على الصحيح أشار إليه بقوله : ( ولا يضر نظرها منْ جَيْبِهِ) لأنه غير كاشف عورته، وروی ( ابن شجاع » نصاً عن أبي حنيفة، وأبي يوسف أنه لو كان محلول الجيب فنظر إلى عورة نفسه، لا تفسد صلاته. وهو قول عامتهم، لأنها ليست عورة في حق نفسه لأنه يحـل لـه مسها والنظر إليها. وشرط بعض المشايخ ستر عورته عن نفسه، حتى لو كان بحال لو نظر إليها من زيقه(٥)
And covering the 'awrah, and seeing it from one's collar does not harm. It is narrated from Abu Yusuf that it is permissible if he repeats it on pure (ground), and if his nose is impure and his forehead is pure like other places, his prayer is valid by consensus, as if he confined (prostration) to the forehead, and the place of the nose is less than a dirham, so its connection with impurity does not harm. And the principle regarding the necessity of purifying the garment is the saying of Allah: 'And your garment purify' (74:4). And if purification is necessary for the garment, it is necessary for the body and place by a stronger reason, because they are more essential for the prayer than the garment, since prayer has no existence without a place, and it may exist without a garment, as in the prayer of a naked person. So what is mentioned in the garment is explicitly mentioned, and in the body and place by implication. And because prayer is a private conversation with the Lord, mighty and majestic, so it is necessary that the prayer be in the best conditions, which is in his purity and the purity of what is connected to him of garment and place. And if he prays on a pure place, except that when he prostrates, his clothes fall on impure ground that does not soil his clothes, his prayer is permissible. And we will mention its branches if Allah wills. And covering the 'awrah is required, and we will mention its reality. And its covering was obligatory by consensus in prayer, even if in a dark house, and due to the hadith of 'A'ishah: 'Allah does not accept the prayer of a menstruating woman except with a khimar.' And al-Hakim authenticated it. And the cover is that which does not show what is under it. Thus, a thin garment that describes what is under it is not a cover. In 'al-Tajnīs': A woman prays with a thin garment that describes what is under it, her prayer is not permissible, because she is like a naked woman. He ﷺ said: 'Allah curses the clothed naked women.' He meant what we mentioned. End. And the condition is covering from the sides, so that if he prays in a shirt with an open collar, and sees his 'awrah from it during bowing, his prayer is permissible according to the correct (view), indicated by his saying: 'And seeing it from his collar does not harm', because he is not uncovering his 'awrah. And Ibn Shuja' narrated a text from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that if the collar is open and he looks at his own 'awrah, his prayer does not become invalid. And it is the saying of the majority of them, because it is not 'awrah in relation to himself, since it is permissible for him to touch it and look at it. And some mashāyikh conditioned covering one's 'awrah from oneself, so that if he were in a state where if he looked at it from his collar, (it would invalidate).
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage covers two interrelated matters: first, the obligation to cover the 'awrah in prayer, and second, the ruling on uncovering or seeing one's own 'awrah through an open collar (jīb). The author begins by stating the principle: covering the 'awrah is obligatory by consensus for prayer, even in darkness, supported by the hadith of 'A'ishah that a menstruating woman must cover with a khimar. The cover must be thick enough to hide what is beneath; a thin or transparent garment does not suffice, as it renders the woman like a naked one, incurring a curse. The condition of covering is from the sides, meaning all surrounding areas must be covered. Then the text addresses a specific scenario: if a person prays with a shirt that has an open collar (halūl al-jayb) and sees his own 'awrah from it while bowing, the prayer remains valid according to the correct view. This is because the person is not intentionally uncovering his 'awrah; rather, the garment is still covering it from the outside. The author cites a text from Ibn Shuja' quoting Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that looking at one's own 'awrah does not invalidate the prayer, since one's own 'awrah is not 'awrah in relation to oneself—one is permitted to touch and look at it. However, the passage notes that some later mashāyikh (teachers) conditioned that one must cover even from oneself, implying that if one could see it through the collar, it would be problematic. But the relied-upon position is the former. The passage also includes an earlier part about repeating prayer if the forehead was on a pure place after the nose was impure, but that seems a continuation from previous discussion. The key takeaway: covering 'awrah is fard, but seeing one's own 'awrah through an opening in the clothing does not break the prayer.

Key Terms
عورة ('awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered in prayer; for men the navel to knees, for women entire body except face and hands.
جيب (jayb): The opening of the garment at the neck or chest (collar).
زيق (zyq): The opening around the neck (collar) of a garment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Prayer is invalid
B) Prayer is valid
C) Valid only if he repeats the prayer
D) Invalid only if he looks intentionally

Key Takeaway
Covering the 'awrah is fard in prayer, but accidentally seeing your own 'awrah through an open collar does not invalidate the prayer according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Ruling on Covering the Awrah and Seeing from Below the Hem
Explains the ruling when the awrah is seen from below the hem during prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for covering the awrah during prayer and identify when seeing the awrah invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
Intentionally seeing your own awrah invalidates prayer; unintentional sight from below the hem does not due to hardship.

This passage from the Sharh of Nur al-Idah addresses a practical scenario: what happens if a person sees his own private parts during prayer? The author distinguishes between intentional and unintentional exposure, and also discusses the ruling on praying in silk, number of garments, and the disliked nature of praying in trousers alone. By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply these rulings correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is covering the awrah during prayer. The ruling is that covering awrah is wajib (obligatory), not fard. Identify the exact hukm level stated or implied.
The passage quotes the verse 'Khudhu zinatakum' as proof for wujub.
2
Locate the dalil and its proof
The author cites the Quranic verse (7:31) 'Take your adornment at every mosque'. The command 'khudhu' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
The dalil is qati al-thubut but zanni al-dalala, hence wajib not fard.
3
Analyze the ruling on seeing the awrah
The text states 'ra'aha fasadat salatuhu' – if he sees his awrah, prayer becomes invalid. But an exception is made for thick beard covering it. Also, unintentional sight by someone from below the hem does not harm due to hardship.
Distinguish between the praying person seeing his own awrah vs being seen by others.
4
Apply the subsidiary rulings
The passage also covers silk garments (valid but disliked without necessity), preference for wearing best clothes, number of garments (three recommended, two sufficient with turban), and dislike of praying in trousers alone.
These are practical applications of the principle of covering awrah with dignity.

وأسفل ذَيْلِهِ، واستقبال القبلة.
(٤)
رآها فسدت صلاته، ولذا قيل: إن كانت لحيته كثيفة وستر بها [؟] صحت وإلا فلا (و) لا يضر لو تكلف أحد النظر، فرآها من أسفل ذَيْلِهِ)، لأن ستر العورة على وجـه لا يمكـن الـغـيـر النظر إليها، إذا تكلف مما يؤدي إلى الحرج، ولو لم يجد إلا ثوباً حريراً صلى فيه، وإن وجد غيره، صحت أيضاً، لكن کره کلبسه بلا ضرورة كالمغصوب، وأرض الغير، كما سنذكره ) ، والأفضل أن يلبس أحسن ثيابه عنـد أداء الصلاة، رعاية للفظ الزينة المذكورة بقوله تعالى: ﴿ خُذُوا زِينَتَكُمْ عِندَ كُلِّ مَسْجِدٍ [الأعراق: ٣١] وفيه استعارتان، إحداهما : إطلاق اسم الحال على المحل، وهو زينتكم، والثانية: إطلاق المحـل عـلـى الـحــال، وهو عند كل مسجد، والمستحب أن يصلي في ثلاثة أثواب، قميص وإزار وعمامة، وقال « الزيلعي : والأفضل أن يصلي في ثوبين، لقوله : « إِذَا كَانَ لأحَدِكُمْ ثَوبَان، فَلْيُصَلِّ فِيهِمَا " يعني مع العمامة، لأنه يكره مكشوف الرأس إلا للتذلل، كما سنذكره (۳) إن شاء الله تعالى. وقال في « الاختيار شرح المختار » : ويكره أن يصلي في السراويل وحده، لما روي أنَّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نَهَى أَنْ يُصلِّي الرَّجلُ فِي قَوْبِ لَيْسَ عَلَى عَاتِقِهِ مِنْهُ شَيء ) (). قال أبو حنيفة: الصلاة في السراويل تشبه فعـل أهـل الـجفـاء، وفي الثوب يتشح به أبعد من الجفاء وفي قميص ورداء عادة الناس. انتهى.
And below his hem, and facing the qiblah. (4) He saw it, his prayer became invalid. Therefore it was said: If his beard was thick and he covered his [private part] with it, his prayer is valid; otherwise not. And it does not harm if someone makes an effort to look and sees it from below his hem, because covering the awrah in a way that others cannot see it, if one makes an effort, leads to hardship. And if he finds only a silk garment, he prays in it, and if he finds other, it is also valid, but it is disliked like wearing it without necessity, like a usurped garment or another's land, as we will mention. And it is better to wear one's best clothes at the time of prayer, observing the word 'adornment' mentioned by Allah: 'Take your adornment at every mosque' [Al-A'raf: 31]. In this there are two metaphors: one is the use of the state for the place, which is 'your adornment'; and the second is the use of the place for the state, which is 'at every mosque'. And it is recommended to pray in three garments: a shirt, a waistcloth, and a turban. Al-Zayla'i said: It is better to pray in two garments, due to his saying: 'When one of you has two garments, let him pray in them' meaning with the turban, because it is disliked to have the head uncovered except for humility, as we will mention (3) if Allah wills. And he said in al-Ikhtiyar Sharh al-Mukhtar: It is disliked to pray in trousers alone, because it is narrated that the Prophet ﷺ prohibited a man from praying in a garment without something on his shoulders. Abu Hanifa said: Praying in trousers resembles the act of rough people; and in a garment wrapped around is further from roughness; and in a shirt and cloak is the custom of people. End.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sharh of Nur al-Idah. It discusses the condition of covering the awrah in prayer and the effect of seeing it. The author states that if one sees his own awrah during prayer, the prayer is invalidated. However, if the beard is thick and covers the private part, the prayer is valid. Looking without intent from below the hem does not harm because requiring covering in a way that prevents all possible sight leads to hardship. The passage then discusses silk garments: if only silk is available, prayer is valid, but it is disliked (makruh) without necessity, similar to praying in a usurped garment. It recommends wearing the best clothes for prayer, citing the Quranic verse 'Take your adornment at every mosque.' Two metaphors are identified. It then discusses the number of garments: it is recommended to pray in three (shirt, waistcloth, turban), but al-Zayla'i suggests two (with turban) based on a hadith. Praying in trousers alone is disliked by Abu Hanifa as it resembles rough people.

Key Terms
العورة (al-awrah): The private parts that must be covered during prayer for validity.
السراويل (al-sarawil): Trousers; praying in them alone is disliked according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person deliberately makes an effort to look at his own awrah from below the hem during prayer?
A) His prayer becomes invalid.
B) His prayer remains valid because it was from below the hem.
C) His prayer becomes invalid only if someone else sees.
D) His prayer remains valid if he has a thick beard.

Key Takeaway
Covering the awrah is wajib in prayer; intentionally seeing one's own awrah invalidates the prayer, but unintentional sight by another from below due to hardship does not affect validity.
